601 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burroughs


AC 26095


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


99 Conn. App. 413; 914 A.2d 592; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 49


September 27, 2006, Argued  
February 6, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Burroughs, 282 Conn. 909, 922 A.2d 1099, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 202 (2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Burroughs, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 355 (Conn., Sept. 23, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment in the first case reversed in part, further proceedings; judgment in the second case affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), upon a conditional plea of nolo contendere, to possession of narcotics with the intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics, after the denial of his motion to suppress. He was sentenced to six years in prison and six years of probation. Defendant was also convicted of failure to appear and forgery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the police subjected him to an illegal stop that constituted an unconstitutional seizure. The appellate court held that the stop was an investigatory stop under the state and federal constitutions. Defendant's car was legally parked on the street. The police drove past defendant's car in a marked patrol car, turned the patrol car around, and parked behind defendant's car. One officer approached defendant's car on the driver's side, while the other officer approached on the passenger's side. A reasonable person would not have felt free to leave. The seizure was not based on a reasonable and articulable basis of suspicion. There were no criminal allegations or predictive information in an anonymous tip, upon which the police were dispatched. Although defendant's car fit the description in the tip, the police witnessed no suspicious or criminal activity that would warrant further investigation. The initial detention was, therefore, illegal. Finally, the evidence should have been suppressed. It was impossible to separate the illegal seizure from the evidence collected. The police did not have a reasonable suspicion to approach defendant's car.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only with respect to the charges of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics. The case was remanded with direction to grant defendant's motion to suppress and for further proceedings according to law. The judgments were affirmed in all other respects.

 

602 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rweyemamu v. Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities


AC 27108


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


98 Conn. App. 646; 911 A.2d 319; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 509; 99 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1112


September 21, 2006, Argued  
December 12, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Rweyemamu v. Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities, 281 Conn. 911, 916 A.2d 51, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 43 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rweyemamu v. Conn. Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10750 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Hon. Howard T. Owens, Jr., judge trial referee.) Appeal from the decision by the named defendant dismissing the plaintiff's employment discrimination complaint against the defendant Roman Catholic Diocese of Norwich, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Hon. Howard T. Owens, Jr., judge trial referee, rendered judgment of dismissal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Rweyemamu v. Ct. Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2798 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 19, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff priest challenged a decision of defendant Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities dismissing his complaint, which alleged employment discrimination under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60 against defendant diocese. The Superior Court, New Britain, Connecticut, found that neither state agencies nor state courts had subject matter jurisdiction to review purely ecclesiastical disputes and dismissed the priest's challenge. The priest appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission's dismissal of the priest's complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction was based on a ministerial exception with respect to individuals employed by religious institutions in a ministerial capacity. The appellate court recognized this exception in the enforcement of employment discrimination statutes such as § 46a-60 because the constitutional guarantee of free exercise of religion required courts and government agencies from exercising jurisdiction over a religious institution's actions regarding the employment of its clergy and ministers. The appellate court declined to look to federal caselaw interpreting the Religious Freedom Restoration Act of 1993, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb et seq., as persuasive guidance for the position that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-571b had displaced the ministerial exception, federal precedent, while often persuasive, was not binding on Connecticut courts. Rather, the appellate court found that the employment practices of religious institutions were a form a religious belief for purposes of § 52-571b(d), which prevented the application of the strict scrutiny test of § 52-571b(a) and (b), and thus did not displace the ministerial exception.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

603 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanseverino


AC 25793


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


98 Conn. App. 198; 907 A.2d 1248; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 445


May 23, 2006, Argued  
October 24, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Sanseverino, 280 Conn. 945, 912 A.2d 481, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 483 (2006)
Appeal granted by, in part State v. Sanseverino, 280 Conn. 946, 912 A.2d 481, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 482 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Sanseverino, 287 Conn. 608, 949 A.2d 1156, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 250 (2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Sanseverino, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 145 (Conn., May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Espinosa, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and with the crimes of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Espinosa, J., denied the defendant's motion to sever; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trials.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), for sexual assault in the first degree as to two different victims, attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree as to one victim, and kidnapping in the first degree as to one victim. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly denied his motion to sever the two cases against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired both victims at different times to work in a bakery. Defendant allegedly grabbed both victims in a back room and sexually assaulted them. Neither victim knew the other. Defendant argued that the two cases did not involve discrete, easily distinguishable factual scenarios and that he suffered substantial prejudice as a result of the consolidation which was not cured by the trial court's inadequate instructions to the jury. The appellate court agreed. The similarities in both cases were significant enough to impair defendant's right to the jury's fair and independent consideration of the evidence in each case. Thus, defendant suffered substantial prejudice from the consolidation of the two cases. The trial court failed to instruct the jury that it could not use or consider the evidence from one victim's case in determining whether to convict on the other case. It moreover did not clearly advise the jury to distinguish the charges relating to the first victim from the charges relating to the second victim. Thus, the instruction did not adequately cure the prejudice. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a) was not unconstitutionality vague as applied to defendant's conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial in each case.

 

604 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hayes Family Ltd. P'ship v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


AC 26726


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


98 Conn. App. 213; 907 A.2d 1235; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 452


May 23, 2006, Argued  
October 24, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hayes Family Ltd. P'ship v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 281 Conn. 904, 916 A.2d 44, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 25 (2007)
Appeal denied by Hayes Family Ltd. P'ship v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 281 Conn. 903, 916 A.2d 44, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 21 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Tolland, Scholl, J.) Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application to amend the Manchester zoning regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Scholl, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court; thereafter, this court granted the plaintiff's motion to add Manchester Tolland Development, LLC, as a party plaintiff.
Hayes Family Ltd. P'shp v. Manchester Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 758 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 18, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which dismissed plaintiff's appeal from the decision of defendant, a town planning and zoning commission. The main issue presented by plaintiff was whether plaintiff's challenge to a 1998 amendment of the town's zoning regulation on the ground that there was improper public notice was time barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(r).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owned property upon which it desired to develop multi-family housing units. The regulation at issue that was amended limited the number of multi-housing units on any parcel. The trial court dismissed the appeal as untimely pursuant to § 8-8(r), which required any appeal to have been brought within one year. Plaintiff contended on appeal that the trial court improperly dismissed the appeal because § 8-8(r) did not apply to actions taken during the time period at issue or, alternatively, that the statute was impermissible retroactive legislation abrogating substantive legal rights. The court agreed with plaintiff that § 8-8(r) was inapplicable but that a different statutory provision, 1999 Conn. Spec. Acts 99-7(6)(c), applied to validate the amendment at issue. The court noted that several amendments have been made to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(r) and that the enactment of 1999 Conn. Spec. Acts 99-7(6)(c) was a proper exercise of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

605 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Culver


(AC 26018)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


97 Conn. App. 332; 904 A.2d 283; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 396


May 23, 2006, Argued  
September 5, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Culver, 280 Conn. 935, 909 A.2d 961, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 440 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, Holden, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of unlawful restraint and disorderly conduct, and with three counts of the crime of criminal violation of a restraining order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Holden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of criminal violation of a restraining order, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of two counts of criminal violation of a restraining order, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-223b (Rev. to 2003). The court imposed a total sentence of one year and nine months incarceration. Defendant had already served his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim had been in a dating relationship for approximately six months after which she obtained a restraining order against defendant. Defendant's conviction arose when he blocked the victim's car at a fast-food restaurant and tried to speak to her through her passenger side car window. The victim managed to maneuver her vehicle out and drove directly to the police station. Defendant followed and was arrested. On appeal, defendant claimed that his conviction under § 53a-223b(a)(1) and (2) violated his constitutional protection against double jeopardy and that the subdivisions were unconstitutionally vague. The court found no double jeopardy violation because § 53a-223b(a)(1) and (2) required proof of an element that the other did not in that the term "stay away" in § 53a-223b(a)(1) denoted physical proximity or spatial nearness and the term "contact" in § 53a-223b(a)(2) meant not having any form of communication with the victim. The court did not find the statute unconstitutionally vague since a person of ordinary intelligence would have fair warning as to the distinct conduct proscribed and defendant had actual notice via the restraining order issued against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

606 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kondrat v. Town of Brookfield


AC 26625


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


97 Conn. App. 31; 902 A.2d 718; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 358


May 26, 2006, Argued  
August 8, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 22, 2007.
Appeal denied by Kondrat v. Town of Brookfield, 280 Conn. 926, 280 Conn. 926, 908 A.2d 1087, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 409 (2006)
Appeal denied by Kondrat v. Town of Brookfield, 280 Conn. 926, 280 Conn. 926, 908 A.2d 1087, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 412 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket; Carroll, J., Schuman, J.) Action in each case to recover damages for, inter alia, personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff et al. in the first case and by the named plaintiff's decedent in the second case et al. as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Carroll, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion to consolidate; thereafter, the matters were transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket; subsequently, the court, Schuman, J., granted the motions for summary judgment filed by the defendant Joseph H. Austin, Jr., in each case and rendered judgments thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Curtin v. Town of Brookfield, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 919 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sued defendants, a city and a landowner, seeking damages for personal injuries, wrongful death, and other claims associated with an accident caused by a tree that fell on a car. The landowner filed a motion for summary judgment. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), granted the landowner's motion, and plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tree was located on the landowner's property, approximately eight feet from a road. Ten years after cutting limbs off of the tree, the landowner informed the city that the tree was beginning to split. A representative of the city inspected the tree but did not have it removed. The tree later fell on a vehicle traveling on the road. The Connecticut Supreme Court had interpreted Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 23-59 and 23-65(b) as vesting exclusive control in a town tree warden over trees located in whole or in part in public roadways. The Supreme Court had held that owners of private, adjoining land were not liable to anyone accidentally injured by a tree falling in the roadway. Plaintiffs argued that this interpretation did not bar a claim for intentional damage to a tree that later caused personal injury. The appellate court held that the record did not support an assumption that the tree immediately threatened the life and limb of those who traveled on the road. The landowner's responsibility for denuding the tree was difficult to distinguish from what his liability would have been if the tree had been hit by lightning. Thus, the existing law absolved the landowner of liability.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

607 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Halle T.


(AC 25675)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


96 Conn. App. 815; 902 A.2d 670; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 364



August 8, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Halle T., 280 Conn. 924, 280 Conn. 924, 908 A.2d 1087, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 413 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters, Hon. William L. Wollenberg, judge trial referee.) Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters, and tried to the court, Hon. William L. Wollenberg, judge trial referee; judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent father appealed to this court.
In re Halle T., 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1898 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), terminating his parental rights with respect to his minor child. Petitioner was the Commissioner of the Department of Children and Families (DCF).


OVERVIEW: The father first claimed that the trial court improperly adopting verbatim significant portions of social studies in its written memorandum of decision. The appeals court's review of the record revealed that the DCF set forth sufficient, i.e., clear and convincing, evidence to support the court's factual findings regarding the termination of parental rights, despite the parroting of the social studies. The verbatim adoption of portions of the social studies did not dilute the DCF's burden of proof. Evidence supported the trial court's conclusion that a father failed to attain a degree of rehabilitation sufficient to warrant the belief that, at some time in the foreseeable future, he would be capable of assuming a responsible position with respect to his child's care, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3). Accordingly, the court's decision to terminate the father's parental rights was not clearly erroneous. The child suffered from the effects of fetal alcohol syndrome and exhibited numerous developmental disabilities. The father's progress, made over approximately two years, was insufficient when considered in relation to the child's special needs and her need for permanency.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

608 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dalzell


AC 26255


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


96 Conn. App. 515; 901 A.2d 706; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 332


February 22, 2006, Argued  
July 18, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Dalzell, 280 Conn. 914, 908 A.2d 539, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 380 (2006)
Reversed by, in part, Remanded by State v. Dalzell, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 236 (Conn., June 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, J. R. Downey, J.; Mintz, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the infraction of failure to wear a seat belt and with the crimes of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell, possession of narcotics, possession of drug paraphernalia and operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of drugs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, where the court, J. R. Downey, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Mintz, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charges of failure to wear a seat belt, possession of narcotics with the intent to sell, possession of narcotics, possession of drug paraphernalia and operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of drugs; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Dalzell, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3895 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Superior Court, Judicial District of Danbury, geographical area number three (Connecticut), denied defendant's motions to suppress evidence, defendant pled nolo contendere to possession of narcotics with the intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), failure to wear a seat belt in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-100a(c)(1), and other crimes. Defendant appealed the denial of the motions to suppress.


OVERVIEW: A police officer followed defendant's vehicle for approximately one mile prior to making a stop after he observed that defendant was not wearing a seat belt. The officer did not observe other traffic violations or erratic driving. After observing that defendant's pupils were dilated and that defendant acted lethargic, the officer arrested defendant for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of drugs. The officer discovered drugs in the vehicle while performing an inventory search. Defendant argued that the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to justify the stop, and that the search violated his rights under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9. The court held that the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant based on the observation that defendant was not wearing a seat belt, a violation of state law. However, the appellate court held that there was no probable cause justifying the seizure and arrest of defendant or the search of the car. The appellate court found that the observations on which the officer based his belief that defendant was under the influence of drugs were indistinguishable from otherwise innocent conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, except as to defendant's seat belt infraction, and the case was remanded with direction to grant defendant's motions to suppress.

 

609 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Mercer v. Strange


AC 26616


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


96 Conn. App. 123; 899 A.2d 683; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 278


February 17, 2006, Argued  
June 20, 2006, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Burke, J.) Action to recover damages for alleged disability discrimination, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Burke, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Mercer v. Strange, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 895 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 28, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sued appellee state corrections department employees, in their official capacity, in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), for alleged violations of the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq., and § 504, 29 U.S.C.S. § 794, of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973. The trial court dismissed the action. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that the state corrections department employees discriminated against him on the basis of his physical disability by refusing his request for placement in a single cell in the back of one of the housing facilities at the correctional institution in which he was housed. The inmate also contended that the trial court erred in dismissing his claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. On appeal, the court found that the inmate brought his action against the employees solely in their official capacities. Because suing the employees in their official capacities was tantamount to bringing the action against the State of Connecticut, the only immunity defense available to the employees was sovereign immunity. The trial court, therefore, improperly granted the motion to dismiss on the ground of statutory immunity. Further, by alleging that the employees' department received federal funding, the inmate alleged facts sufficient to defeat the defense of sovereign immunity as to his Rehabilitation Act claim. Finally, remand of the case was necessary for consideration of the inmate's claim under the Rehabilitation Act and for further consideration of the inmate's ADA claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for consideration of the inmate's claim under the Rehabilitation Act and for further consideration of the inmate's claim under the Americans with Disabilities Act.


 

610 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winot


AC 25186


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


95 Conn. App. 332; 897 A.2d 115; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 214


February 14, 2006, Argued  
May 16, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Winot, 279 Conn. 904, 901 A.2d 1229, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 266 (2006)
Appeal granted by, in part State v. Winot, 279 Conn. 905, 901 A.2d 1229, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 267 (2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Winot, 294 Conn. 753, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 45 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Mullarkey, J. Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, kidnapping in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Mullarkey, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss and to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a mistrial; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a new trial and for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), convicted defendant of kidnapping in the second degree, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94(a), attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-94(a) and 53a-49(a)(2), and risk of injury to a child, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1). He was sentenced to eight years in prison followed by 10 years of special parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took the 12-year-old victim by the arm and attempted to pull her toward his parked vehicle. The appellate court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94(a) failed to provide defendant fair notice that the brief encounter, in which he forcibly took the victim's arm but did not move her, was criminal misconduct. The evidence of the movement and confinement fell into the realm of the "minuscule" movement or duration of confinement. Thus, to hold that he was put on notice that the conduct would have violated the kidnapping statute was an absurd and unconscionable result. Further, the evidence did not establish that defendant was guilty of risk of injury to a child, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1), because the victim's statement that defendant pulled on her arm, alone, did not permit a rational trier of fact to conclude, without resorting to speculation and conjecture, that defendant's conduct was likely to jeopardize the victim's physical health. However, the evidence supported the conviction for attempted kidnapping. The trial court properly ruled that the noose found in defendant's car was admissible to establish his intent to kidnap the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed with respect to the conviction of kidnapping in the second degree and risk of injury to a child and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment of not guilty of those crimes. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

611 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. LaSalle


AC 26650


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


95 Conn. App. 263; 897 A.2d 101; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 206


January 3, 2006, Argued  
May 9, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. LaSalle, 279 Conn. 908, 901 A.2d 1227, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 276 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied LaSalle v. Comm'r of Corr., 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1028 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 29, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Lasalle, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3004 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 25, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied LaSalle v. Murphy, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 92233 (D. Conn., July 8, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London, Schimelman, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), for murder. Defendant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of murder, that the trial court improperly declined to instruct the jury that the use of a deadly weapon, by itself, did not establish the intent to kill and that the trial court improperly instructed the jury as to the burden of proof.


OVERVIEW: A landlord informed defendant that he was being evicted from a boarding house. The jury had evidence that defendant was angry with the landlord for evicting him and that defendant had threatened two other tenants within hours of the landlord's stabbing death. The appellate court held the statements were highly indicative of defendant's state of mind at the time of the crime. Moreover, given the location and depth of the stab wounds, it was not unreasonable for the jury to infer that defendant intended to kill the landlord. The jury also had before it evidence that defendant attempted to conceal the murders. Several police officers testified that he spoke normally and showed no signs of intoxication. Thus, there was sufficient evidence for the jury reasonably to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant had the specific intent to kill the landlord. Reviewing the trial court's instruction as a whole, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by trial court's failure to include defendant's requested language. Finally, the instruction accurately conveyed the concept of reasonable doubt to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

612 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Ridgefield Bank v. Stones Trail LLC.


AC 26371


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


95 Conn. App. 279; 898 A.2d 816; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 207



May 9, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Ridgefield Bank v. Stones Trail, LLC, 279 Conn. 910, 902 A.2d 1069, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 288 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Comerford, J.; Hon. Richard J. Tobin, judge trial referee; Wilson, J.) Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property owned by the named defendant brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the defendants filed counterclaims; thereafter, the court, Comerford, J., rendered judgment of foreclosure by sale; subsequently, the court, Hon. Richard J. Tobin, judge trial referee, denied the motion to open the judgment filed by the named defendant; thereafter, the court, Wilson, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to confirm the sale, and the named defendant appealed to this court.
Stones Trail, LLC v. Ridgefield Bank, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3333 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bank brought a mortgage foreclosure action against defendant property owner. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Connecticut, rendered a judgment of foreclosure by sale, a judge trial referee denied the owner's motion to open the judgment, and the superior court granted the bank's motion to confirm the sale. The owner appealed, challenging how a valuation for the property was reached.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that he should have had an evidentiary hearing to determine the true valuation, as he claimed that the property consisted of six lots worth over $ 2 million. An appraiser stated that there was one 19-acre lot worth $ 1.4 million. Affirming, the court, in its limited scope of review, ruled that the superior court did not abuse its discretion in accepting the valuation because the appraiser testified at the foreclosure hearing that while the owner bought the property years earlier as six lots with a higher value, circumstances concerning it had changed and that its highest and best use was as one lot. Noting that the owner did not file a motion for a second appraiser and an evidentiary hearing as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-25 allowed, the court further ruled that because the owner could have made such a request but failed to do so, there was no Due Process Clause violation. Moreover, the owner did not file a motion to reopen the judgment within four months, as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a required. In so ruling, the court took note of the superior court's equitable power to confirm the sale, which was properly exercised absent fraud, misrepresentation, surprise, or mistake.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

613 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinez


AC 26647


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


95 Conn. App. 162; 896 A.2d 109; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 202


January 6, 2006, Argued  
May 2, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Martinez, 279 Conn. 902, 901 A.2d 1224, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 260 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Certificate of appealability denied Martinez v. Warden, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 92158 (D. Conn., Dec. 17, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Martinez v. Warden, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 354 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 6, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction entered by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), after a jury found him guilty of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm. Defendant claimed that the trial court failed to inquire into possible jury taint, that he was denied due process of law as a result of prosecutorial misconduct and that the court improperly charged the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his victim in a dispute over the right to sell heroin on a particular street corner. The court affirmed his conviction. The trial court sufficiently investigated and dealt with allegations of jury misconduct. Individual voir dire ensured a fair and impartial jury even in light of potential contamination of the venire panel before such questioning and an investigation limited to a preliminary inquiry of counsel on the record was sufficient regarding an alleged premature discussion of the case after the jury was seated. Although a comment on the strength of defendant's case, made by the prosecutor during cross-examination of defendant's sister, was improper, it did not deny defendant of a fair trial as it was an isolated instance of misconduct and curative instructions were given. Questions asked of defendant regarding that witness were appropriate for uncovering potential bias. The prosecutor's closing argument was also appropriate. Finally, the trial court's instructions on consciousness of guilt and reasonable doubt were proper and the instructions did not improperly raise any mandatory presumptions that improperly relieved the State of its burden of persuasion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Faraday v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 26340


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


95 Conn. App. 1; 894 A.2d 1048; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 204


December 2, 2005, Argued  
April 18, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Faraday v. Comm'r of Corr., 279 Conn. 907, 901 A.2d 1225, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 274 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Faraday v. Comm'r of Corr., 288 Conn. 326, 952 A.2d 764, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 301 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee. Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford where the court, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee rendered judgment dismissing the petition; thereafter, the court granted the petitioner's motion for reconsideration and rendered judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Faraday, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3890 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), granted a habeas corpus action by petitioner, a prisoner, and ordered respondent, an agency, to provide certain medical services to the prisoner. The agency appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: In the habeas corpus petition, the prisoner alleged that a magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scan of his back and an operation to repair herniated discs in his back were medically necessary, and that the agency had denied his requests for the same. The appellate court held that the trial court properly granted relief to the prisoner. The trial court relied on a doctor's report and the results of an earlier MRI, which indicated that the prisoner had a herniated disc in his back, and that the condition was degenerative. The appellate court held that this was sufficient evidence to demonstrate that the prisoner suffered from a serious medical condition. The appellate court further held that the trial court properly determined that the agency was deliberately indifferent to the prisoner's condition. The trial court made ample findings concerning the fact that the treatment afforded to the prisoner had not alleviated his condition, and the agency's repeated refusal to provide the prisoner with the evaluative services of a neurologist or a neurosurgeon. Thus, the trial court properly found that the prisoner's rights under the Eighth Amendment were violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Perry v. State


AC 25885


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


94 Conn. App. 733; 894 A.2d 367; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 146


January 18, 2006, Argued  
April 11, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Perry v. State, 278 Conn. 915, 899 A.2d 621, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 206 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Gallagher, J., Doherty, J.) Action to recover damages for legal malpractice, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Gallagher, J., granted in part the defendants' motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Doherty, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Perry v. Conn. Pub. Defenders Serv. Comm'n, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2581 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accused person sued defendants, the State of Connecticut, the public defender services commission, and a public defender, with the general assembly's consent, in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for legal malpractice and other relief. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss a civil rights claim, and, after a bench trial, entered judgment for defendants. The accused person appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the person was jailed for months, his alleged victim was asked to identify him and said he did not commit the crime, after which charges were dismissed. A claims commissioner rejected the person's claim, but the legislature let him to sue. The appellate court held the evidence supported the trial court's findings that counsel did not negligently handle an alibi defense, and counsel investigated that defense and handled it according to a sound trial strategy. When necessary, counsel competently explained to the person each part of the defense strategy and got the person's informed consent to use it. Counsel comported to the requisite standard of care. The person's claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(f), regarding actions against the State, unconstitutionally deprived him of his right to a jury trial was not preserved for review. The person's counsel's "exception" stating a desire for a jury trial did not raise the constitutional issue raised on appeal or preserve the issue for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. John M.


AC 25313


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


94 Conn. App. 667; 894 A.2d 376; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 144


October 20, 2005, Argued  
April 11, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. John M., 278 Conn. 916, 899 A.2d 622, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 212 (2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Conn. v. John F.M., 2008 Conn. LEXIS 51 (Conn., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee. Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to sexual assault in the second degree; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault (SA) in the third degree and acquitted him of SA in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-72a(a)(2) and 53a-71.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in sexual acts with the 17-year-old victim, and he entered not guilty pleas. The trial court acquitted defendant on the second degree SA, and the jury found defendant guilty of third degree SA. Defendant was sentenced and he appealed. The court found that defendant's admission that he was married to the victim's mother, together with testimony from a witness who was present at the marriage celebration, sufficiently established that relationship. However, testimony from the victim was insufficient to establish that the victim was the daughter of defendant's wife. The court reviewed the unpreserved constitutional challenge and held that defendant's equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV were violated by the prohibition of heterosexual, rather than homosexual, intercourse between kindred persons in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2). It was noted that homosexual relationships were beyond the purview of the degrees of kindred for marriage purposes in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-21. There was no rational basis shown for such a distinction, either to prevent dangers of inbreeding, protect the family, and/or based on moral considerations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed judgment of not guilty for defendant on the third degree SA conviction.

Manifold v. Ragaglia


AC 25811


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


94 Conn. App. 103; 891 A.2d 106; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 91


September 21, 2005, Argued  
February 28, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Manifold v. Ragaglia, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1836 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London at Norwich, Martin, J.). Action to recover damages for, inter alia, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at Norwich, where the court, Martin, J., granted in part the motion to dismiss filed by the named defendant et al.; thereafter, the court denied the motion for summary judgment filed by the named defendant et al., and the named defendant et al. appealed to this court.
Manifold v. Ragaglia, 272 Conn. 410, 862 A.2d 292, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 528 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two children and their parents, sued defendants, the commissioner and employees of the department of children and families, alleging intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress in relation to neglect petitions that were ultimately withdrawn. The Superior Court, judicial district of New London at Norwich, Connecticut, denied defendants' motion for summary judgment, and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in denying the motion for summary judgment, stated that because defendants sought summary judgment on the basis of subject matter jurisdiction, the motion would be treated as a motion to dismiss. As an initial matter, the reviewing court found that the denial was a final judgment for purposes of appeal because the motion asserted the protections of sovereign immunity and qualified immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The court also agreed with defendants that the trial court should have applied the standard for summary judgment. The court held that a motion for summary judgment could and should be used to address claims for lack of subject matter jurisdiction in certain circumstances, particularly, as in the case at bar, when a motion to dismiss had been denied but additional discovery could provide further evidence on which to decide the claim. The policy behind sovereign immunity was better effectuated by a thorough review of the materials before the court than by the more limited review associated with the motion to dismiss. The court declined to address defendants' other claim because they failed to provide an adequate record for review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to treat the motion as a motion for summary judgment.

Reid v. Comm'r of Corr.


(AC 24947)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


93 Conn. App. 95; 887 A.2d 937; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 16


October 25, 2005, Argued  
January 10, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Reid v. Comm'r of Corr., 278 Conn. 921, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 236 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee.) Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Reid v. Armstrong, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3287 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), denied petitioner inmate's request for a writ of habeas corpus. Upon the grant of certification, the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed on appeal that the court improperly concluded that the condition of his parole that his release not be incompatible with the welfare of society was not void for vagueness and therefore constitutional. The appeals court disagreed, first finding that because the inmate's challenge did not substantially implicate his First Amendment rights, its review was limited to an as-applied-vagueness challenge. Second, the court believed that a reasonable person would believe that the inmate communicated a serious expression of an intent to commit an act of unlawful violence on the victim. As such, his conduct was not entitled to First Amendment protection. Further, his parole was revoked because he engaged in a pattern of behavior that encompassed a series of statements and actions that a reasonable person would find to be a "true threat," and, a reasonable person of ordinary intelligence would be on fair notice that the threatening conduct the inmate exhibited violated the condition that his release not be "incompatible with the welfare of society."


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate habeas relief was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, convicted defendant of two counts of sixth-degree larceny and one count of second-degree forgery. Defendant then pled guilty to having committed the crimes while on bond. After the instant court reversed an order denying his motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the trial court denied a second motion for correction, defendant appealed.

Fourth, although defendant was afforded the right to be addressed personally at sentencing and to speak in mitigation of his punishment, he waived these rights by his voluntary failure to appear at his sentencing hearing. Finally, nothing in the record suggested vindictiveness by the judge at the sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the superior court, on remand, was affirmed.

State v. Kalman


AC 24788


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


93 Conn. App. 129; 887 A.2d 950; 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 18


October 12, 2005, Argued  
January 10, 2006, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Kalman, 277 Conn. 915, 895 A.2d 791, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 76 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Thompson, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of an assault weapon, threatening, reckless endangerment in the first degree and breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Thompson, J.; judgment of guilty of possession of an assault weapon, threatening and breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in part; Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted defendant of possession of an assault weapon, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202c, threatening, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-62, and breach of the peace, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181. Defendant appealed the possession of an assault weapon and the threatening convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the court violated his due process rights by (1) concluding that a Maadi MISR firearm was a prohibited assault weapon under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202a (1999) and (2) failing to conclude that § 53-202a was vague as applied to him. The appeals court disagreed. The relevant text of § 53-202a indicated that all selective-fire firearms and certain specified semiautomatic firearms were "assault weapons" banned by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202c. Second, testimony from a sergeant with the state police, who had been assigned to the special licensing and firearms unit for nearly five years, testified via a tripartite test that the Maadi MISR firearm used by defendant was comparable to an "Avtomat Kalashnikov AK-47 type," which was one of the listed semiautomatic firearms prohibited under § 53-202c. Second, defendant's due process argument was rejected, as he failed to show that the statute did not provide fair warning that it applied to the conduct at issue. He even considered the weapon he possessed to be an AK-47. Hence, his argument that he could not know that the Maadi MISR was a prohibited "Avtomat Kalashnikov AK-47 type" assault weapon was rejected.


OUTCOME: The conviction for possession of an assault weapon was affirmed. But, by failing to brief the issues relating to the threatening conviction, his appeal from that conviction was dismissed.

December 27, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, Cremins, J.). Allowing the officer to be reinstated would violate those clearly established public policies.

State v. Metz


(AC 25721)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


92 Conn. App. 206; 883 A.2d 1264; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 455


September 12, 2005, Argued  
November 1, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Metz, 276 Conn. 934, 890 A.2d 572, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 573 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Bingham, J.; Hon. Samuel S. Freedman, judge trial referee.) Petition for an order to extend the commitment of the defendant, who had been found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of the crimes of assault of a victim sixty or older in the second degree and interfering with an officer, to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Bingham, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, pursuant to the parties' stipulation, the court, Hon. Samuel S. Freedman, judge trial referee, reserved three questions of law for the advice of the Supreme Court; subsequently, the reserved questions were transferred to this court.
State v. Metz, 230 Conn. 400, 645 A.2d 965, 1994 Conn. LEXIS 253 (1994)



DISPOSITION: No costs will be taxed in this court to either party.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), denied defendant's motion to dismiss a petition to extend his commitment filed by the State. The parties then stipulated to three questions of law for the advice of the Supreme Court, as well as the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat § 17a-593. Subsequently, the questions were transferred to the instant court, and this matter followed.


OVERVIEW: At issue in the instant action was the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c), pursuant to which a court could order a person who has been acquitted of a crime because of mental disease or defect to be recommitted to the psychiatric security review board for continued hospitalization. Defendant claimed that his constitutional rights were violated when the statute was applied to him, as no history of his mental status had been documented like that of the defendant in State v. Long. But, this argument presupposed that defendant was foreclosed from initiating judicial review of the validity of his commitment. That was not the case. Defendant did not claim that he had a constitutional right to express notice of his right to apply directly to the court for his discharge. The court thus concluded that § 17a-593(c) did not violate defendant's equal protection rights under Conn. Const. art. I, § 20 or the Fourteenth Amendment, nor did not violate his due process rights under Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The statute was constitutional, and the three questions were answered in the negative.

624 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gillespie


(AC 25564)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


92 Conn. App. 143; 884 A.2d 419; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 456


May 31, 2005, Argued  
November 1, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Miano, J.) Petition for an order extending the acquittee's commitment to the psychiatric security review board, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Miano, J., granted the acquittee's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court granted the state's motion to open, denied the acquittee's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and restated its judgment of dismissal, and the acquittee appealed to this court.
State v. Gillespie, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1315 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 7, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent insanity acquittee appealed and petitioner State cross-appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), that granted the State's motion to open and correct its previously filed petition to extend the acquittee's commitment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593, denied the acquittee's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, and dismissed the petition on constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee was on conditional release from a commitment in an assault when he killed someone. Once again found guilty by reason of insanity, he was committed for 25 years, the presumptive prison term for that type of murder. As the 25-year mark approached, the State sought to extend his term pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593, but mistakenly referenced the assault prosecution's docket number in its petition. The court held, first, that this type of error was circumstantial rather than substantive, since the acquittee certainly understood which case was being referenced, so that the trial court's subject matter jurisdiction was not implicated by the error, which could be corrected under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-123. Furthermore, according to the decision of Connecticut's highest court in State v. Long, made final while the instant appeal was pending, the trial court's determination that the extension of a commitment term violated due process and equal protection guarantees was an error, so that consideration of the petition could proceed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with regard to the existence of subject matter jurisdiction but reversed the judgment in all other respects. It remanded the matter for further consistent proceedings on the merits of the petition.

Baker v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 25128


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


91 Conn. App. 855; 882 A.2d 1238; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 433


June 6, 2005, Argued  
October 11, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Baker v. Comm'r of Corr., 276 Conn. 927, 889 A.2d 816, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 558 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Baker v. Comm'r of Corr., 281 Conn. 241, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 57 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Tolland, White, J.; Fuger, J.) Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, White, J., pursuant to a stipulation of the parties, granted the motion to cite in the board of parole as a respondent; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Baker v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3419 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 4, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was granted leave to appeal from a decision of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which dismissed the inmate's petition for writ of habeas corpus against respondents, the Connecticut Commissioner of Corrections and the state board of parole. The inmate had sought an order directing the board to declare him eligible for parole after he served 50 percent of his underlying sentence.


OVERVIEW: In his petition, the inmate asserted that under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a, he should be eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentence for gun, narcotics, and forgery convictions. On appeal, the inmate argued that the trial court improperly dismissed his petition after finding that jurisdiction was lacking because the inmate had no liberty interest in or right to parole release and, therefore, there was no illegal confinement or an ex post facto unconstitutional application of a statute, such as § 54-125a. The court reversed on the jurisdictional issue. Read together, § 54-125a(a) and (b) clearly vested a liberty interest in parole eligible status to all persons described within § 54-125a(a), subject to the exclusion for the enumerated offenses and the 85 percent limitation embodied in § 54-125a(b). Thus, while the inmate had no right to parole release, he did have a liberty interest in parole eligible status. The fact that the trial court could not grant him a writ and order his immediate release did not negate the trial court's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

626 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Racsko v. Racsko


(AC 24781)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


91 Conn. App. 315; 881 A.2d 460; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 401


April 26, 2005, Argued  
September 13, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Racsko v. Racsko, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 265 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Middlesex, Abery-Wetstone, J.) Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the court, Abery-Wetstone, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Racsko v. Racsko, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2186 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which dissolved her marriage to defendant husband, entered custody orders, and entered other orders, including granting the husband sole authority to determine the parties' children's international travel, denying the wife's request to relocate out of state, and denying the wife's request for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The wife appealed certain orders in a dissolution judgment that gave the husband sole authority over whether the children could travel internationally, that denied her request to relocate to another state, that did not enter orders on the children's college expenses, and that did not require the husband to pay the wife's attorney's fees. The court found that the international travel orders did not restrict the wife's ability to travel or to exercise her religion. The reasonableness of restricting her ability to unilaterally travel with the children internationally was supported by the record, which showed that travelling to Israel was not in the children's best interests. Moreover, the guardian ad litem opposed relocation to Israel or another state since that would severely restrict the husband's parenting time with the children, who bonded with both parents and who needed regular contact from both parents. The children were very young, so retaining jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56c for a later decision on college expenses was proper. Finally, the wife received ample resources in property division to deny her request for attorney's fees under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-62.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, and it affirmed all the challenged orders in favor of the husband.

 

627 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hernandez


(AC 25451)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


91 Conn. App. 169; 883 A.2d 1; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 385



August 30, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hernandez, 276 Conn. 912, 886 A.2d 426, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 478 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Licari, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Licari, J., verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of his murder conviction, defendant contended that the trial court improperly excluded evidence of his intoxication, which was relevant to whether he had the requisite intent to commit murder, and improperly charged the jury on consciousness of guilt and reasonable doubt. The evidence defendant sought to introduce was a hospital record indicating that alcohol was in defendant's blood at a certain level on the day of the murder, but defendant did not explain what the level meant or show that he was drinking prior to the time of the murder. The trial court could have reasonably concluded that the foundation defendant laid for admission of the evidence was insufficient to support his claim of intoxication and, therefore, the evidence was too speculative to be relevant. Although the trial court improperly instructed the jury that false statements "are," rather than "may be," circumstantial evidence of guilty consciousness, the instructions as a whole did not mislead the jury, as the next instruction used permissive language on the same subject. Finally, the language used to explain reasonable doubt was previously upheld in cases that were binding precedential authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

State v. DeJesus


AC 25589


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


91 Conn. App. 47; 880 A.2d 910; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 380


March 22, 2005, Argued  
August 30, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. DeJesus, 279 Conn. 912, 903 A.2d 658, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 305 (2006)
Appeal granted by, in part State v. DeJesus, 279 Conn. 912, 903 A.2d 658, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 306 (2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. DeJesus, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 308 (Conn., Aug. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Lavine, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Connecticut transferred to the instant court an appeal by defendant from a judgment on jury verdict of the Connecticut Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford, convicting him on two counts each of sexual assault and kidnapping. He challenged various rulings on evidence and argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, in his supermarket management position, hired the victim, a young girl with mental disabilities, as a bagger. During two periods of employment, he told her to accompany him to isolated areas of the building where he prevailed upon her to perform sex acts to which she lacked the capacity to consent. At his trial, another former employee with similar disabilities described similar experiences. The court held that these prior bad acts were admissible, since the trial court had provided a proper limiting instruction, and they could be considered with regard to consent issues and a possible pattern of conduct. Defendant failed to preserve certain due process claims, and they did not qualify for Golding review. Defendant's pre-Miranda statements were admissible, because his presence at the police station was completely voluntary when he made them. Finally, even though kidnapping did not merge with sexual assault charges under Connecticut law, the kidnapping statute was impermissibly vague as applied to one of defendant's sexual assaults, because there was not even a miniscule act of asportation or restraint of the victim's movement so as to justify the additional charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed one of defendant's kidnapping convictions and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to render judgment of not guilty as to that count. It affirmed in all other respects.

Fish v. Fish


AC 24542


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


90 Conn. App. 744; 881 A.2d 342; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 364


March 28, 2005, Argued  
August 16, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Fish v. Fish, 275 Conn. 924, 883 A.2d 1243, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 417 (2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Fish v. Fish, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 4 (Conn., Jan. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Rubinow, J.; Prestley, J.). Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Rubinow, J., judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the defendant filed a motion to modify custody; subsequently, the court, Prestley, J., granted the motions to intervene filed by Barbara Husaluk et al. and the plaintiff's motion for a protective order; thereafter, the court, Prestley, J., issued an order modifying custody, and the defendant appealed to this court; subsequently, the court issued an articulation of its decision.
Fish v. Fish, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2488 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which modified the judgment of child custody. The court awarded joint custody of the child to appellee mother and appellee paternal aunt and ordered that the child reside primarily with the aunt in Aspen, Colorado. The father claimed, inter alia, that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant the aunt's motion to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The parties shared joint custody of the child with an evenly divided parenting arrangement. There were frequent contentious disputes with respect to educational placement, tuition, and child support. A guardian ad litem was appointed for the child. The father sought sole custody of the child. Following an emergency request by the guardian ad litem, the trial court determined that the child could elect the extent and the circumstances of her visitation with the father. The appellate court held that while the father enjoyed the rights of a parent recognized in Roth, the jurisdictional pleading requirements and heightened burden of persuasion of Roth were inapposite to the contested custody case. The father offered no support for his assertion that the specific requirements of Roth applied to a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-57 third party motion to intervene. There was ample evidence to conclude that the presumption in the father's favor was rebutted. Also, the father had notice of the potential placement of the child with a relative. However, he was not given an opportunity to respond or to present any evidence on his view of the most efficient allocation of the tax exemption.


OUTCOME: The court's order with respect to the tax dependency exemption was reversed. The case was remanded with direction to remove references to tax exemptions. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Whitaker v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 24485


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


90 Conn. App. 460; 878 A.2d 321; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 332


November 19, 2004, Argued  
August 2, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Whitaker v. Comm'r of Corr., 276 Conn. 918, 888 A.2d 89, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 501 (2005)
On remand at Whitaker v. Warden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 735 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Tolland, Fuger, J.) Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment granting the petition in part, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Whitaker v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1527 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which granted his habeas corpus petition in part but which did not grant him all the relief he requested against respondent commissioner of correction on claims that the commissioner miscalculated various credits on his criminal sentence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate raised a multitude of statutory and constitutional claims related to an alleged miscalculation of the proper amount of credit he should have received on his criminal sentence. The court, on appeal of partial relief, found that the claims of violations of his due process and equal protection rights, along with separation of powers claims, fell under challenges to the commissioner's applications of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 18-98d, 53a-38(c). The court found, under the authority of both Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 18-98d(a)(1), 53a-38(b)(1), the inmate's presentence credit was properly applied only once where his concurrent sentences were not imposed on the same day. Moreover, his claims were rejected that such an application violated equal protection or due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, as amended by Conn. Const. amend. arts. V, XXI, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, based on precedent on the same issue. However, the commissioner improperly failed to apply the relation back doctrine of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-38(c) to determine the starting date of his sentence, and the commissioner failed to credit the inmate for a vacated sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded for the proper calculation of the inmate's credits but otherwise affirmed the judgment. The court remanded for a determination of the inmate's proper release date.

In re Christina M.


AC 25539, AC 25540


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


90 Conn. App. 565; 877 A.2d 941; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 329


April 21, 2005, Argued  
August 2, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part In re Christina M., 276 Conn. 903, 884 A.2d 1024, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 449 (2005)
Appeal granted by, in part In re Christina M., 276 Conn. 903, 884 A.2d 1024, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 448 (2005)
Affirmed by In re Christina M., 2006 Conn. LEXIS 414 (Conn., Nov. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Middlesex, Child Protection Session, Driscoll, J.). Coterminous petitions by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, Juvenile Matters at Willimantic, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the matter was tried to the court, Driscoll, J.; judgments terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondents filed separate appeals to this court.
In re Christina M., 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1006 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 2, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex in the Child Protection Session (Connecticut), which, upon petition by petitioner commissioner of children and families, terminated the parents' parental rights (TPR).


OVERVIEW: The parents had been found to have neglected their three daughters. The commissioner moved to TPR under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B)(ii). The trial court found that the parents were unable or unwilling to benefit from reunification. They appealed, raising three issues: (1) whether clear and convincing showed a lack of rehabilitation; (2) that the trial court erred in failing to appoint, on its own initiative, not only a lawyer to represent the children's legal rights but also a guardian ad litem (GAL); and (3) that the procedural due process rights under Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 8, 10, for the economically disadvantaged parents required proof beyond a reasonable doubt of the grounds for termination. The court found that there were no challenges to the accuracy of the facts recited by the trial court and that such facts supported a finding of a lack of reunification. Moreover, a GAL was only required upon petition by the children's attorneys, not on the court's own initiative. Finally, a court order denying the fundamental freedom to be a parent did not require the same proof as a criminal conviction, and clear and convincing evidence was the proper constitutional standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the TPR.
