Writ of habeas corpus denied Hamlin v. Warden, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2914 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, Mullarkey, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Mullarkey, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss and to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, and sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Mullarkey, J., granted in part the defendant's motion for rectification or augmentation.
State v. Hamlin, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 837 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 12, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hartford Superior Court (Connecticut) denied defendant's motions to dismiss and to suppress certain evidence and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of assault in the first degree and of carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim fought. The victim later returned to make peace with defendant. Defendant, however, had a gun in his hand. The victim ran, but was shot. Defendant then got in a car that a second man was driving and fled. Defendant was charged with assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit. The State also filed a notice of intent to seek sentence enhancement pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k. While awaiting trial, he spoke to the second man while in a holding cell. Defendant told him to say he had not been with defendant during the shooting. At trial, the second man testified about what defendant told him to say. Defense counsel did not ask about the statement on cross-examination. Defendant was then convicted on both charges. On appeal, the appellate court found that defendant's claim that his Sixth Amendment right to counsel had been violate was not adequately developed for review, the identification of defendant did not violate his due process rights, and application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k, the sentence enhancement statute, was not void for vagueness in a prosecution for violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(5).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Irizarry v. Irizarry


(AC 25364)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


90 Conn. App. 340; 876 A.2d 593; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 314


April 19, 2005, Submitted on briefs  
July 19, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Kavanewsky, J.; Hon. Stanley Novack, judge trial referee.) Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Kavanewsky, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the court, Hon. Stanley Novack, judge trial referee, granted in part the plaintiff's motion for modification of child support, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Irizarry v. Irizarry, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 671 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 11, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a post-decree proceeding, plaintiff father filed a motion to reduce his child support paid to defendant mother. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), granted the motion and set the father's total child support at $ 80 per week. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that Conn. Agencies Regs. § 46b-215a-2a(e) was unconstitutional. However, the appellate court found that the claim was not preserved for appellate review as the father failed to make the claim to the trial court. In his brief, the father did not seek review under either of the doctrines recognized to review unpreserved claims of error, and it was inappropriate to engage in a level of review that was not requested. The father also claimed that the trial court improperly relied on representations of the mother's counsel, in lieu of evidence, as the basis for its finding as to the child care costs. The appellate court agreed. The mother's financial affidavit did not list any cost for child care. During the hearing, the trial court solicited from the mother's counsel information regarding the cost of the child care, and counsel represented that the cost was $ 180 per month. The mother did not testify regarding the child care costs and did not provide any documentary evidence regarding that cost. Absent evidence, the trial court was without any basis to support its finding of the child care expenses, and its finding regarding those costs was clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the order regarding child care costs, and the case was remanded for further proceedings to determine the child care costs, if any, that the mother could recover from the father. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Antonio A.


(AC 24739)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


90 Conn. App. 286; 878 A.2d 358; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 306


March 24, 2005, Argued  
July 19, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Antonio A., 275 Conn. 926, 883 A.2d 1246, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 421 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Antonio A. v. Connecticut, 546 U.S. 1189, 126 S. Ct. 1373, 164 L. Ed. 2d 81, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1413 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Antonio A. v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1241 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 19, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Lavine, J.) Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with violation of probation and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of risk of injury to a child and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the second case was tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the first case was tried to the court; judgment of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal in the second case and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court for the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) of two counts of risk of injury to a child and two counts of first degree sexual assault, as well as a violation of probation, and was sentenced to a total effective term of 44 years incarceration, execution suspended after 24 years, followed by 10 years probation and lifetime sex offender registration. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant digitally penetrated his eight-year-old daughter twice. The appellate court held a jury could find the insertions were distinct, so he was guilty of two counts each of risk of injury to a child and first degree sexual assault. He was not put in jeopardy twice for the same crime. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2), prohibiting risk of injury to a child, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2), prohibiting first degree sexual assault, were clear to persons of common intelligence and not unconstitutionally vague. His offer to take a polygraph was properly excluded given its slight probative value, risk of prejudice to him from accompanying explanatory testimony, and potential for jury confusion. Prosecutorial comments about constancy of accusation witnesses explained such testimony's nature and did not deprive defendant of a fair trial, nor did references to the victim's credibility, in the entire trial's context. References to defense counsel's argument did not impugn counsel's integrity or institutional role. A sentence based on finding the victim was under 10, which was not submitted to the jury, was harmless error, given overwhelming evidence of the victim's age.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

(AC 23521)

Affirmed by State v. Fabricatore, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 71 (Conn., Feb. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, Hon. William F. Hickey, Jr., judge trial referee.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the third degree and breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Hon. William F. Hickey, Jr., judge trial referee; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a continuance; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), for assault in the third degree and breach of the peace. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal, denied his request for a continuance, instructed the jury on the requirements of self-defense, and remanded defendant into custody pending sentencing.


OVERVIEW: The victim told defendant to stop choking a friend and a fight ensued. Several witnesses testified that defendant "danced" around the victim with his fists raised. The verdict allowed the appellate court to assume that the jury found that defendant hit the victim first. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request for a continuance. Although the trial court's remarks about an alleged prior conviction were improper, defendant implicitly waived that claim as he agreed with the curative instruction. Gen. Stat. § 54-63f was unconstitutional and as the appellate court could not predict whether the determination, which it concluded was retroactive, might have impacted defendant's sentence to two years of probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the sentence imposed and the case was remanded for resentencing. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Tuchman v. State


(AC 24792)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


89 Conn. App. 745; 878 A.2d 384; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 254


February 14, 2005, Argued  
June 24, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Tuchman v. State, 275 Conn. 920, 883 A.2d 1252, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 406 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Harper, J.) Action, inter alia, to enjoin the defendants from prohibiting the plaintiffs from operating their chemical and waste transport business, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Harper, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiffs' motion to reconsider, and the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Tuchman v. State, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2333 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hazardous waste transporters appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which dismissed their action against defendants, the state department of environmental protection and a department employee, premised, essentially, on a refusal to issue a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-454(a) to allow them to ship hazardous waste. They also challenged denial of a reconsideration motion.


OVERVIEW: The transporters' business was intrastate shipment of hazardous waste products. In 1991, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-454 was amended to authorize the department to regulate, and issue permits for, such transportation, but it did not immediately enforce the statute. Meanwhile, the transporters operated without a permit. In 1998, the department ordered the transporters to stop shipping without a permit. The transporters complied. But, when their permit application was denied, they sought money damages and declaratory relief under various constitutional theories. The action was dismissed on subject matter jurisdiction grounds due to sovereign and qualified immunity. The transporters appealed. The court found that it was undisputed that no permission was granted under Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 53, §§ 4-141 to 4-165 for money damage claims, so those claims were properly dismissed. Moreover, the transporters failed to show they had a right either to the permit or to conduct their business. Constitutional protection was not triggered to defeat sovereign immunity. The employee's conduct was authorized by statute, so it was not reckless under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 to trigger individual liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the transporters' action. It also affirmed denial of the motion for reconsideration.

State v. Brooks


(AC 24873)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


89 Conn. App. 427; 874 A.2d 280; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 225


February 15, 2005, Argued  
June 7, 2005, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, Jongbloed, J.; Hadden, J.) Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of less than four ounces of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, where the defendant was presented to the court, Jongbloed, J., on a plea of guilty; judgment of guilty; thereafter, the court, Hadden, J., dismissed the defendant's motion to withdraw the plea and denied the defendant's petition for a writ of error coram nobis, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New London Superior Court (Connecticut) entered a final judgment of conviction after defendant pled guilty to one count of possession of less than four ounces of marijuana. It then imposed a $100 fine upon him. Thereafter, the trial court dismissed his motion to withdraw his guilty plea and his alternative petition for a writ of error coram nobis. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a resident alien, was charged with possession of less than four ounces of marijuana in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(c). He decided to plead guilty and was not represented by counsel at the time he did so. The trial court entered a judgment of conviction on the charge and fined defendant $100. Defendant did not receive any jail time. Based on that conviction and other convictions, defendant was eventually deported. Defendant filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea and an alternative petition for writ of error coram nobis. The trial court dismissed defendant's motion and denied his petition. On appeal, the appellate court found that defendant's Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-296 right to counsel was not violated because defendant was not deprived of his liberty; although defendant could have received jail time, the trial court merely fined him, and it was the actual deprivation of liberty, not the possibility of it, that triggered the right to counsel. It also found that because he had not been denied his statutory right to counsel, defendant could not show that the judgment of conviction was void or voidable as was required for writ of error coram nobis purposes.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

638 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Orellana


(AC 24480)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


89 Conn. App. 71; 872 A.2d 506; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 188



May 17, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Orellana, 274 Conn. 910, 876 A.2d 1202, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 275 (2005)
Related proceeding at, Summary judgment granted, in part, summary judgment denied, in part by Orellana v. Sencio, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 61326 (D. Conn., Aug. 29, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Orellana v. Warden, State Prison, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 529 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Espinosa, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, conspiracy to sell narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics with the intent to sell within 1500 feet of a public housing project, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Espinosa, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; subsequently, the court granted, in part, the defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person not drug-dependent (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b)), conspiracy to sell narcotics by a person not drug-dependent (Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48, 21a-278(b)), and possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of a public housing project (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b)).


OVERVIEW: Defendant first claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence of 350 packets of heroin found in his automobile in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights. The appeals court disagreed. The police had probable cause to believe that heroin would be found in the automobile based on the reliability of an informant and police surveillance that corroborated key details about the narcotics delivery. The trial court properly permitted the State to introduce evidence of prior misconduct as the evidence of defendant's prior criminal activity tended to make it more probable that he had knowledge of the heroin in the automobile and that he intended to deliver the heroin to the informant. Prior consistent statements by the informant were properly admitted as it was reasonable for the court to conclude that defendant attempted to impeach the informant on the ground of recent contrivance. Finally, the prosecutor's use of the term "smoke and mirrors," although improper, was neither strongly critical nor severely condemnatory of defendant's attorney. Therefore, it was not so egregious as to implicate defendant's due process right to a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

639 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howard


(AC 25251)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


88 Conn. App. 404; 870 A.2d 8; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 134


December 6, 2004, Argued  
April 12, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by State v. Howard, 275 Conn. 917, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 398 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Harper, J.) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and with the crimes of capital felony, criminal possession of a firearm and carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Harper, J., granted the state's motion to consolidate and denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Howard, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3374 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 18, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him for capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(8), two counts of murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), criminal possession of a firearm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(a), carrying a pistol without a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35, and possession of narcotics under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on various charges after he shot and killed two men. He appealed, claiming that the trial court improperly: (1) instructed the jury on intent for murder, (2) sanctioned a non-unanimous verdict, (3) consolidated murder and drug charges, (4) denied his motion to suppress pretrial identifications, (5) admitted autopsy photographs, and (6) instructed the jury on reasonable doubt. The court found that defendant did not preserve his challenge to the intent instruction and, regardless, the evidence overwhelmingly showed defendant's specific intent to kill. Unanimity was required by the jury charge. Consolidation of charges was proper since evidence on the drug charges went to motive for the murders and did not impair the jury's ability to decide the charges fairly. An eyewitness to the murders identified defendant independently of any state action and a subsequent identification that was arranged by police, while suggestive, was necessary for investigation of the crimes and apprehension of defendant. Gruesome autopsy photos were relevant to crucial issues and limiting instructions were given. Finally, similar reasonable doubt charges were approved in other cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for capital felony, murder, criminal possession of a firearm, carrying a pistol without a permit, and possession of narcotics.

Santiago v. Comm'r of Corr.


(AC 24980)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


87 Conn. App. 568; 867 A.2d 70; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 70


October 13, 2004, Argued  
February 22, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Santiago v. Comm'r of Corr., 273 Conn. 930, 873 A.2d 997, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 169 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Hon. Frank S. Meadow, judge trial referee; Pittman, J.) Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hon. Frank S. Meadow, judge trial referee; judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal; subsequently, the court, Pittman, J., granted the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
Santiago v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2904 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 24, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which denied the inmate's habeas corpus petition. The inmate claimed that the habeas court improperly denied him certification for leave to appeal and that the denial of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was improper because trial counsel in an underlying murder prosecution was burdened by an actual conflict of interest.


OVERVIEW: The court first ruled that the certification issue was moot because the habeas court had in fact granted certification based on a renewed request by the inmate for certification. The inmate's ineffective assistance argument was based on a claim of actual conflict in that the public defender's office that had represented him in his underlying murder trial had also represented three other people who were potential alternate suspects in the murder. He argued that the office failed to adequately investigate the three people and that the conflict prevented his public defender from presenting the plausible alternative defense theory of third party culpability. The court affirmed the habeas court's ruling that no actual conflict existed and that the inmate received effective assistance of counsel. The office did not represent one of the people, so there was no conflict there. As to the other two people, all that was proven by the evidence was that a potential conflict existed. The conflict never matured into an actual conflict. The failure to present the alternative defense was not a lapse in representation because the evidence supporting it was weak and was contrary to other evidence.


OUTCOME: The habeas court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hernandez


(AC 23384)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


87 Conn. App. 464; 867 A.2d 30; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 60


November 18, 2004, Argued  
February 15, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hernandez, 273 Conn. 920, 871 A.2d 1030, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 131 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Cofield, J.; Damiani, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Cofield, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant, after a conditional plea of nolo contendere, of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from a stop of his vehicle by a police officer, who had received a radio transmission that a car matching defendant's vehicle was involved in a shooting. The broadcast advised that numerous weapons were involved and that the responding officers should proceed with caution. Drugs were subsequently found in defendant's pants. Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the physical evidence seized from him and the statements he made to the police on the basis that the initial stop of his vehicle was not supported by a reasonable and articulable suspicion and that, even if the stop was justified, it was more intrusive than necessary. The court disagreed and found that defendant's vehicle matched the vehicle description that had been broadcast. The court found no merit in defendant's argument that his car was red versus maroon. The court further determined that the stop did not become more intrusive than necessary, because the arriving officers were advised to proceed with extreme caution as numerous weapons were reportedly involved in the initial incident, and the officers were entitled to ensure their safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Mussington


(AC 24342)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


87 Conn. App. 86; 864 A.2d 75; 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 20


November 15, 2004, Argued  
January 25, 2005, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Mussington, 273 Conn. 914, 870 A.2d 1084, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 102 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London, geographical area twenty-one, Devlin, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault of an employee of the department of correction, and with one count each of the crimes of assault in the second degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area twenty-one, and tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of assault of an employee of the department of correction and assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New London, geographical area twenty-one (Connecticut), which convicted him of assault on an employee of the department of correction and assault in the second degree. Defendant contended that the trial court's charge to the jury on reasonable doubt diluted the State's burden of proof in violation of the United States and Connecticut constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The evidence permitted a finding that defendant assaulted and injured a correctional officer who was performing his duties. The trial court gave a lengthy instruction to the jury on the subject of reasonable doubt and, in the course of it, instructed the jury that if it could reconcile all of the facts proved with any reasonable theory consistent with the innocence of defendant, then it could not find him guilty. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, he argued that the language of the trial court unconstitutionally suggested that it was for the jury to evaluate the evidence in an attempt to prove a theory of innocence rather than deciding whether the State carried its burden of proof. In affirming the judgment, the court noted that defendant did not preserve his constitutional claim. The court found that because the challenged part of the charge had been approved on several occasions and the trial court's instructions on reasonable doubt, considered in their entirety, were not improper, defendant had failed to establish that a constitutional violation clearly existed and deprived him of a fair trial, and thus, defendant could not prevail on his claim of constitutional error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Hartmere, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Hartmere, J., denied the defendant's motion in limine to preclude the state from presenting certain expert testimony; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty of one count of sexual assault in the first degree and of risk of injury to a child; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a new trial and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2) and one count of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1).

He also compelled her to hold a book bag filled with tapes and clothes on a stick over her head for long periods of time. On another occasion, he made her kneel on grains of rice. Defendant also forced the victim to have oral, anal, and vaginal intercourse with him. Defendant was charged and convicted of sexual assault and risk of injury to a child. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that while it did not know, based on the general verdict, whether the jury convicted defendant of risk of injury to a child on the basis of his having given the victim a bloody nose or his sexually assaulting her or both. the fact that the jury convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree assured the court that as a matter of law, there was sufficient evidence found by the jury upon which defendant could have been convicted of risk of injury to a child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Alexander v. Comm'r of Admin. Servs.


(AC 24912)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


86 Conn. App. 677; 862 A.2d 851; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 562



December 28, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Blue, J.) Action to enjoin the defendants from seizing certain assets of the named plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Blue, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Alexander v. Comm'r of Admin. Servs., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3197 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 12, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate and executrix filed suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for an injunction to prevent defendants, the Connecticut Commissioner of Administrative Services and the Connecticut Commissioner of Correction, from seizing the inmate's inherited funds under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-85b. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, Connecticut, granted defendants' motion to strike plaintiffs' substituted complaint. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants placed a lien on half of the inmate's inherited funds, as authorized by § 18-85b and Conn. Agencies Regs. §18-85a-2. Plaintiffs' initial complaint alleged that this violated their rights (1) to procedural due process, (2) under the Takings Clause of the Fifth Amendment, (3) to substantive due process, and (4) under the Equal Protection Clause. They did not appeal the trial court's order striking that complaint but filed a substituted complaint with the same allegations, plus a new allegation transforming their previous, generic equal protection claim into a colorable claim of selective enforcement. Therefore, the appellate court held that they could appeal only the trial court's striking of the new equal protection claim. Plaintiffs alleged that the State unfairly targeted the inmate to the exclusion of similarly-situated inmates and that defendants lacked a rational basis for this differential treatment. Because plaintiffs failed to allege specific instances of discrimination among the members of the class of eligible inmates, the trial court properly struck plaintiffs' equal protection claim for failure to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Segal v. Segal


(AC 24661), (AC 22567)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


86 Conn. App. 617; 863 A.2d 221; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 566



December 28, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeals from Superior Court, judicial district of Litchfield, Brunetti, J., DiPentima, J., Cremins, J.) Action, in the first case, for the partition of certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, DiPentima, J.; judgment of partition by sale and appointing a committee to conduct the sale; thereafter, the court, DiPentima, J., pursuant to the parties' motions for a determination of interests and equities in the sale proceeds, rendered a supplemental judgment ordering the distribution of proceeds, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court; subsequently, the defendant in the first case, as plaintiff in the second case, brought an action for interpleader concerning the proceeds of the partition sale held by the court clerk, the defendant Brian J. Murphy; thereafter, this court affirmed the trial court's supplemental judgment in the first case, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Supreme Court; subsequently, the court, Cremins, J., rendered judgment dismissing the second case, from which the plaintiff in that case appealed to this court; thereafter,  [***2] the Supreme Court reversed the judgment of this court in the first case and remanded the case for further proceedings; subsequently, the court, Brunetti, J., granted the motion filed by the defendant in the first case for an order distributing the proceeds and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court. Judgment in the first case (AC 24661) affirmed; appeal in the second case (AC 22567) dismissed.
Segal v. Segal, 264 Conn. 498, 823 A.2d 1208, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 241 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in partition action; appeal dismissed as moot in interpleader action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former husband and defendant former wife appealed decisions of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut) in separate proceedings. The husband challenged a judgment that the wife was entitled to all proceeds of a partition sale and the wife challenged a decision in her independent interpleader action, which refused to compel a court clerk to pay the partition sale proceeds to her.


OVERVIEW: The wife obtained a judgment against the husband in Nevada for non-payment of alimony. She domesticated the judgment under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-605. The husband began a partition action on jointly held Connecticut property. After a decision dividing the proceeds between the parties was reversed, the superior court held that the wife's judgment entitled her to all the partition proceeds. The husband appealed. The parties agreed that affirming that decision would render the wife's separate appeal of an interpleader action moot. The husband argued that the wife's judgment became unenforceable when a Nevada court subsequently modified it, that the wife did not file a judgment lien on the property, and that he had no opportunity to be heard on his defenses. The court found that the modification did not require further domestication and, due to the timing of the proceedings, it was not feasible for the wife to obtain a judgment lien prior to partition. Finally, the order to pay the wife the partition proceeds did not infringe on the clerk's sovereign immunity and the husband's substantive defenses to the wife's judgment had to be tried in Nevada and not Connecticut.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in the husband's appeal of the awarding of the partition sale proceeds. The court dismissed the wife's appeal as moot.

 

646 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. Aiken


(AC 25102)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


86 Conn. App. 587; 862 A.2d 319; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 555



December 21, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Cox v. Aiken, 273 Conn. 916, 871 A.2d 370, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 115 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Cox v. Aiken, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 163 (Conn., May 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Doherty, J.). Action for an injunction requiring the defendants to reinstate the plaintiff to his employment with the defendant department of social services, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Doherty, J., denied in part the defendants' motion to dismiss, and the defendants appealed to this court.
Cox v. Aiken, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 309 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the department of social services and the assistant director of human resources for the department (department), appealed an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which dismissed plaintiff former department employee's claims for back pay, but which denied dismissal of his claims for reinstatement due to the department allegedly terminating him in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-241.


OVERVIEW: The employee commenced an action, alleging he was laid off in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-241. He claimed he was entitled to a transfer to another position in the event of a layoff and that layoffs were to be based on seniority, but an employee with less time at the same position was not laid off. He sought reinstatement and back pay. The department moved to dismiss on the basis of sovereign immunity and failure to exhaust remedies. The superior court granted dismissal of the monetary claims, but it denied dismissal of the reinstatement claim, holding that the relief sought was injunctive and sovereign immunity did not bar such claims. The department appealed. The court found that the allegations that an employee with less seniority was not laid off, if proven true, would sufficiently establish that the department acted in excess of its authority under § 5-241 and sovereign immunity was inapplicable to claims for injunctive relief based on actions in excess of the department's authority. On the same reasoning, exhaustion did not bar the claim because the employee could seek judicial relief without seeking the consent of the claims commissioner under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the department's motion to dismiss the employee's claims for reinstatement to his former position.

State v. Bloom


(AC 24915)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


86 Conn. App. 463; 861 A.2d 568; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 542


October 15, 2004, Argued  
December 14, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bloom, 273 Conn. 911, 870 A.2d 1081, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 87 (2005)
Summary judgment granted, in part, summary judgment denied, in part by Bloom v. Town of Stratford, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 84655 (D. Conn., Nov. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, Damiani, J.) Information charging the defendant with the infraction of injury to property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the court, Damiani, J., which denied the defendant's motion for a continuance; thereafter, the court rendered judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of violating Stratford, Conn., Code of Ordinances § 152-10A, by a magistrate. He filed a claim for a new trial in the trial court. Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction rendered by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), of injury to property, following the denial of his motions to dismiss the charge due to the vagueness of § 152-10A and for a continuance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 152-10A was vague as it did not define "ornamental lawn." The appellate court held an "ornamental lawn" was a lawn that decorated or adorned. A reasonable person was on notice that the lawn at the park was ornamental and that digging holes in the lawn was prohibited. The mere fact that the town permitted members of the public to use the lawn for certain activities did not take away from its ornamental value. The evidence supported the conviction. There was testimony that defendant dug holes in the park's lawn and that the digging damaged the lawn and killed the grass. The damage created by the digging did not repair itself. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding photographs of the lawn as they were not taken on the date the citation was issued and were not relevant to whether the lawn was ornamental. Finally, any error in the refusal to grant a continuance for defendant to obtain a town report was harmless as defendant did not show that he was prejudiced by the ruling.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Lee


(AC 23551)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


86 Conn. App. 323; 860 A.2d 1268; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 533


September 23, 2004, Argued  
December 7, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lee, 272 Conn. 921, 867 A.2d 839, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 48 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, Swords, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the second degree, assault in the second degree as an accessory, assault in the third degree, breach of the peace and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Swords, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the second degree, assault in the third degree, breach of the peace and interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve (Connecticut), convicted defendant of second degree assault, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60(a)(1), breach of the peace, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(1), and interfering with an officer, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was the victim of vindictive prosecution when the prosecutor filed additional charges in retaliation for his motion for a bill of particulars. The prosecutor added the charge of interfering with an officer before the trial started. The appellate court did not believe that the charge was added as retaliation. Since the prosecutor was not informed of jury selection and only received notice of the bill of particulars moments before the start of trial, the prosecutor added a charge she thought was appropriate and that would have emerged had she had the time and opportunity to review the case file. The charge was warranted. Since defendant already was charged with second degree assault as a principal, he was on notice that he could be convicted as an accessory or of a lesser included offense, and added charges of second degree assault as an accessory and third degree assault did not violate Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 36-18. Defendant failed to show that the prosecutor added the charges in retaliation for his motion for a bill of particulars. Defendant waived any claim that he should have been allowed to discharge his counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen


(AC 24360)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


85 Conn. App. 820; 859 A.2d 586; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 472


March 30, 2004, Argued  
November 9, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen, 272 Conn. 920, 867 A.2d 837, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 46 (2005)
Appeal granted by, in part Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen, 272 Conn. 920, 867 A.2d 837, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 47 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 186 (Conn., June 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Radcliffe, J.). Appeal from the decision by the named defendant approving the application by the defendant Anthony DelMonaco Family Limited Partnership for a planned development district, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Radcliffe, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Campion v. Bd. of Aldermen of New Haven, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 874 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbors appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from a decision of defendant board of aldermen. That decision approved an application by defendant landowner for creation of a planned development district pursuant to New Haven, Conn., Zoning Ordinance § 65. The neighbors argued that their was no enabling authority for the ordinance in question.


OVERVIEW: After earlier efforts to expand the parking area for its catering business, located in what was primarily a residential district, the landowner withdrew its request, and the aldermen and other local authorities agreed not to interfere with the landowner's use of an abutting parcel it also owned for parking purposes. When the landowner finally requested that a planned development district be created out of its several parcels, the neighbors challenged the aldermen's authority for granting approval. In the absence of any statutory references to such districts, the appellate court examined the powers conferred generally on municipalities by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2, as amended by 1959 Conn. Pub. Acts 614, § 2, and the narrower powers conferred on the city in question in particular by 1925 Conn. Spec. Acts 490, to authorize such exceptions to zoning as special permits, variances, floating zones, and nonconforming uses. It found no authority for the authorization of planned development districts. Furthermore, all the other exceptions were circumscribed by standards for a municipal body to apply in granting them, but there were no such definite standards for such a district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter with direction to sustain the neighbors' appeal.

 

650 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


George v. Town of Watertown


(AC 24867)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


85 Conn. App. 606; 858 A.2d 800; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 438


June 1, 2004, Argued  
October 19, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by George v. Town of Watertown, 272 Conn. 911, 863 A.2d 702, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 588 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Matasavage, J. Action for, inter alia, a judgment declaring the rights of the parties relative to contributions to the named defendant's sidewalk fund, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Matasavage, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
George v. Town of Watertown, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3198 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 17, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought a judicial declaration that the actions of defendants, a town and its planning and zoning commission, with regard to a sidewalk fund and a subsequent amendment of the town regulations were unlawful. The landowner also sought restitution. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), dismissed the landowner's complaint. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner obtained approval of a subdivision plan subject to the condition that he contributed to the town's sidewalk fund. The landowner paid the sum requested and never challenged it. Two years later, the town's attorney advised it that the commission was not authorized to require contributions to the sidewalk fund, and the landowner sought a refund. The refund was refused, and the landowner brought the underlying suit. The motion to dismiss was filed on the ground that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction in that the landowner had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies with regard to challenging the sidewalk fund payment within the statutory time period and that the constitutional challenge count lacked ripeness. The court upheld the dismissal of the landowner's counts with regard to obtaining a refund as he had failed to challenge the payment and was precluded from collaterally attacking the same via the initiation of his cause of action. Because the landowner was entitled to ascertain the validity of the amended regulation in dispute and its affect on his property rights, the third count of the complaint was dismissed in error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment only as to count three, which sought a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality and validity of an amendment to a town regulation and, otherwise, affirmed the judgment. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Nat'l Amusements, Inc. v. Town of E. Windsor


(AC 23987)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 473; 854 A.2d 58; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 352


March 23, 2004, Argued  
August 17, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee.) Appeal from the decision by the defendant's board of assessment appeals denying the plaintiff's appeal from the defendant's valuation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, and tried to the court, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Nat'l Amusements v. Town of E. Windsor, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 333 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain, Tax Session (Connecticut), entered in the taxpayer's tax assessment challenge against defendant town. The trial court considered the valuation of the taxpayer's property as a whole and found the total fair market value of the property to be less than the valuation.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer owned and operated a 12-screen multiplex theater. The taxpayer's property contained 27 acres. The taxpayer challenged an assessment by the town. The taxpayer challenged only the valuation of its building, not the land and site improvements. After considering the valuation of the property as a whole, the trial court found the total fair market value of the property to be less than the valuation, thereby sustaining the taxpayer's appeal. On appeal, the taxpayer contended that because it challenged only one portion of the assessment in its pleadings, the trial court was permitted to determine the value of that portion only. However, the court held that the taxpayer could not limit the parameters of a valuation determination by challenging in its pleadings only one portion of the assessment. The court further held that the colloquy between the trial court and the counsel for the town indicated that there was no clear, deliberate, and unequivocal concession that only the value of the building was at issue. Finally, the court could not say that the taxpayer was denied a meaningful opportunity to be heard on the issue of the valuation of the land and site improvements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

652 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Browne


(AC 23041)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 351; 854 A.2d 13; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 342


February 10, 2004, Argued  
August 10, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Browne, 271 Conn. 931, 859 A.2d 930, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 465 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Browne v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1900 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, Clifford, J.) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree, larceny in the third degree, attempt to commit larceny in the third degree, conspiracy to commit, inter alia, burglary in the first degree and disregarding an officer's signal and, substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, manslaughter in the first degree and misconduct with a motor vehicle and, substitute information, in the third case, charging the defendant with the crime of interfering with an officer and substitute information, in the fourth case, charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, attempt to commit assault of a peace officer and criminal mischief in the first degree, and with one count of reckless endangerment in the first degree and, substitute motor vehicle complaint charging the defendant with reckless driving and engaging police in pursuit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area [***2] number nine, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Clifford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the third degree, attempt to commit larceny in the third degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree and larceny in the third degree, disregarding an officer's signal, misconduct with a motor vehicle, interfering with an officer, criminal mischief in the first degree, attempt to commit assault of a peace officer, reckless driving and engaging an officer in pursuit; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of larceny, attempt to commit larceny, conspiracy to commit burglary and larceny , disregarding an officer's signal, misconduct with a motor vehicle, interfering with an officer, criminal mischief, attempt to commit assault of a peace officer, reckless driving, and engaging an officer in pursuit.


OVERVIEW: The police pursued defendant often at speeds in excess of 100 miles per hour. Two officers attempted to box in defendant's vehicle. After the first officer passed defendant's vehicle with his cruiser, he positioned his cruiser in front of defendant's vehicle and slowed. The second officer drove his cruiser alongside defendant's vehicle, but he swerved his vehicle into the officer's travel lane. That officer avoided a collision but lost control of his cruiser, which spun counterclockwise off the highway and collided with trees on the median strip. The officer was killed. It was reasonable for the jury to conclude that the accident was within the scope of the risk defendant created by leading the police on a high-speed pursuit. Further, a reasonable person could foresee that during a high speed chase, a police officer, another motorist on the highway, an innocent bystander or defendant himself could be injured. Finally, a mechanical failure of any type was within the scope of the risk created by defendant's criminal behavior of leading the police in pursuit. The court's instruction to the jury, therefore, was not a clear violation of the defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

653 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morales


(AC 22532)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 283; 853 A.2d 532; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 336


January 21, 2004, Argued  
August 3, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Morales, 271 Conn. 928, 859 A.2d 584, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 456 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Mulcahy, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of burglary in the second degree, kidnapping in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree with a firearm, robbery in the first degree, assault in the second degree with a firearm, burglary in the first degree, and sale and possession of narcotics with intent to sell, and with two counts of the crime of burglary in the third degree, five counts of larceny in the first degree and conspiracy to commit each of those crimes, and with two counts of violating the Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Mulcahy, J.; verdict of guilty of one count each of burglary in the third degree, burglary in the first degree and larceny in the first degree, and of two counts of violating the Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act and of conspiracy; thereafter, the court declared a mistrial as to three counts of larceny in the first degree and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to [***2] this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), that found defendant guilty of burglary in the third degree, burglary in the first degree, violating the Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act, and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly instructed the jury in its charges on accessorial liability and conspiracy. However, the informations charged defendant with conspiracy to commit the crimes alleged in counts one through 14 of the information. That was sufficient to give defendant notice that the State could have sought a conviction on the ground of accessorial liability. The State charged defendant with the single offense of conspiracy, committed conjunctively in one of 14 different ways. This was not a case in which the trial court improperly instructed the jury on a theory of liability that was not included in the information. The charge was correct and, therefore, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled. Specifically, the trial court thoroughly discussed the elements contained in each of the 14 substantive underlying offenses, explained that the conspiracy count was a separate charge, and instructed the jury that to arrive at a guilty verdict, it had to find, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant intended that conduct constituting any one or more of the crimes set forth in count one through 14 of the information was performed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Foster v. Foster


(AC 23868)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 311; 853 A.2d 588; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 337


April 2, 2004, Argued  
August 3, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London, Abery-Wetstone, J.) Motion by the defendants for, inter alia, modification of an award of child custody issued in connection with a foreign dissolution judgment, and for other relief, and motion by the plaintiff to reinstate child support, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Abery-Wetstone, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for a continuance; subsequently, the court denied the defendants' motion to modify custody, denied the plaintiff's motion to reinstate child support and awarded the defendants attorney's fees, and the plaintiff appealed to this court; thereafter, the court granted the named defendant's motion for contempt, and the plaintiff filed an amended appeal.
Foster v. Foster, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 139 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 14, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which denied her motion for a continuance, denied her motion to reinstate child support, ordered her and the child to undergo psychological counseling, and awarded attorney fees to defendants, a father and paternal grandparents, in an action to terminate the grandparents' visitation rights and to reinstate child support.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a motion to terminate the grandparents' visitation rights and to reinstate child support. The father and grandparents moved to modify custody or, in the alternative, to enforce their visitation rights. The trial court denied the father and grandparents custody and visitation. The trial court ordered that the father did not have an obligation to pay child support. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not violate the mother's rights to procedural due process when it denied her motion for a continuance after her attorney withdrew. The trial court gave the mother ample time before the hearing to obtain new counsel. However, the court found that the trial court abused its discretion in eliminating the father's child support obligation on the basis of the mother's chronic interference with visitation. The trial court did not err in ordering the mother and child to undergo psychological counseling. Finally, the court found that the trial court abused its discretion in ordering the mother to pay one half of the father and grandparents' attorney fees. The award of attorney fees was not based on the financial ability of the parties, but was punitive in nature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court eliminating the father's child support obligation and awarding attorney fees to the father and grandparents. The court remanded the case with instructions to vacate those orders. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

State v. Carter


(AC 23614)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 263; 853 A.2d 565; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 335

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Judgment entered by Carter v. Warden, State Prison, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 101 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 22, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Carter, 122 Conn. App. 527, 998 A.2d 1217, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 300 (2010)

Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Remanded by Carter v. Comm'r of Corr., 133 Conn. App. 387, 35 A.3d 1088, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 58 (2012)
Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Carter, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 203 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Mulcahy, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, attempt to commit assault in the first degree, risk of injury to a child and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Mulcahy, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment on a jury verdict of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), convicting him of first-degree assault and attempted assault, creating a risk of injury to a child, and criminal possession of a firearm. Among other issues, he challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, jury instructions, and the admissibility of evidence of his past involvement in the drug trade.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one of several marijuana dealers involved in turf wars that occasionally led to gunfights, often in public places. The victim, a seven-year-old girl, was seriously injured when she was shot in the face during such a gunfight, and many witnesses saw defendant running toward his presumed intended victim, shooting, at the time the victim was hit. The appellate court held that just as in the murder statute, the assault statute permitted a jury to find transferred intent. So long as he intended to harm someone by shooting, it made no difference that he was not trying to hurt the particular victim. This rule had been adequately explained to the jury. The information adequately alleged all the charged offenses, and the evidence was sufficient to permit a rational jury to have found defendant guilty. Finally, evidence regarding defendant's involvement in drug trafficking that led to occasional gunfights was properly admissible to establish motive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

(AC 23619)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 48; 851 A.2d 1214; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 313


April 1, 2004, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bennett-Gibson, 271 Conn. 916, 859 A.2d 570, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 386 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, Cosgrove, J.). Amended information charging the defendant with the crime tampering with a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Cosgrove, J., denied the defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number 14 (Connecticut), that denied defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence, and thereafter convicted defendant of tampering with a witness in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151(a).


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant attempted to induce a witness to absent herself from any official proceeding. On appeal, defendant first claimed that there was insufficient evidence before the jury to sustain her conviction of tampering with a witness. Defendant did not challenge the allegation that she believed that an official proceeding was pending against her brother. She argued that the evidence was insufficient to show that she induced or attempted to induce a witness to absent herself from that proceeding. However, the jury reasonably could have interpreted defendant's request that the victim in the underlying criminal process drop the case from her brother and to excuse the case or cut the case. Viewed in light of defendant's expressed concerns with her brother's situation and her desire to help him, as a request that the victim absent herself from the proceeding, such instructions comported with the interpretation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151. Further, the evidence of the sexual assault charges against defendant's brother clearly was relevant to the issue of motive, to whether there was an official proceeding, and to the existence of defendant's common plan or scheme.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cortes


(AC 23668)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 70; 851 A.2d 1230; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 316


March 31, 2004, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Cortes, 271 Conn. 917, 859 A.2d 571, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 387 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Cortes, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 483 (Conn., Nov. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, D'Addabbo, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree and with one count each of the crimes of unlawful restraint in the first degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of unlawful restraint in the first degree and assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of unlawful restraint in the first degree and assault in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-95(a) and 53a-60(a)(2), respectively. On appeal, defendant argued the trial court violated his rights to present a defense and confront witnesses against him, and his due process right to a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: The complainant testified that she ended the relationship because defendant was very possessive of her and did not permit her do as she pleased. She testified that defendant did not accept that the relationship was over. On appeal, defendant first claimed that the court improperly excluded evidence of the sexual nature of the relationship between the complainant and himself. When defendant's counsel inquired concerning whether the complainant's mother knew that the complainant and defendant had engaged in a sexual relationship, the prosecutor objected, and the court sustained the objection. The court improperly excluded relevant evidence as to the intimate relationship between the complainant and defendant. Thus, the court's attempt to protect the complainant's reputation precluded him from confronting his accuser. Defendant's right to confront the complainant encompassed his right to cross-examine her vigorously for purposes of his defense. In light of the fact that the relationship between the complainant and defendant lay at the heart of the case the excluded evidence was most relevant, and the court abused its discretion in excluding it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and a new trial ordered.

State v. Sivak


(AC 23353)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


84 Conn. App. 105; 852 A.2d 812; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 318


March 29, 2004, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Sivak, 271 Conn. 916, 859 A.2d 573, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 385 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Hon. William L. Hadden, Jr., judge trial referee.). Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and with one count of the crime of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. William L. Hadden, Jr., judge trial referee; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), for assault in the first degree. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the intent element of the crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an altercation between various people outside a bar. At some point, defendant stabbed the victim. Defendant claimed self-defense and accident. The State acknowledged some error in the instructions as to general intent. However, the State claimed the pertinent instructions, as a whole, properly apprised the jury that the element of intent could be satisfied only by a finding of intent to cause the specific result of serious physical injury. Defendant claimed that because he raised self-defense, his intent to cause serious physical injury (a specific result), rather than the intent to use a knife (specific conduct), was crucial, and that the charge, viewed as a whole, deprived him of the due process right to a fair trial by unconstitutionally reducing the State's burden of proof. The appellate court agreed with defendant. On the basis of the conflicting testimony by the friends of the victim and the friends of defendant, as well as that of the victim and defendant, the charge on intent to cause serious physical injury was key to the issue of defendant's guilt. Thus, the verdict could not stand in the face of the evidence and the charge to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Giordano-Lanza


(AC 23846)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 811; 851 A.2d 397; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 298


March 26, 2004, Argued  
July 13, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Giordano-Lanza, 271 Conn. 911, 859 A.2d 572, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 374 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Holden, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of risk of injury to a child and sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Holden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2) and sexual assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court improperly criticized defense counsel and incorrectly gave a curative instruction after interrupting counsel's closing argument, and that the trial court's post-charge, supplemental instruction violated his constitutional right not to testify at a criminal trial by permitting an adverse inference to be drawn from his failure to testify. The appellate court concluded that defense counsel could not properly comment on defendant's lack of a felony record when no evidence was admitted regarding the record's existence or nonexistence. The statements to the jury about defendant's lack of a felony record resulted in defense counsel improperly vouching for defendant's credibility. Thus, the trial court properly interrupted defense counsel's improper argument and properly gave a curative instruction. However, the combination of the trial court's incorrect final curative instructions charging that defendant had no constitutional right not to testify and the trial court's use of the term "unreasonable," rather than "unfavorable," rose to the level of a constitutional violation because it was reasonably possible that the jury was misled.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Scott

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of disorderly conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was engaged in a protest outside of a clinic. He was arrested, tried, and convicted of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2). He was sentenced to 90 days of imprisonment, execution suspended, with a conditional discharge of one year. One of the conditions of the discharge was that he could not be within 100 yards of any such facility. On appeal, the court found no merit to defendant's contention that there was insufficient evidence to convict him of disorderly conduct. The evidence presented allowed the trial court to find that defendant had the requisite intent to be guilty of disorderly conduct. In the course of the protest, defendant chased one car as it entered the parking lot and, as the car began to turn, his actions and proximity to the car nearly caused the car to collide with him. That greatly upset the driver. The court further found no merit to defendant's contention that the State failed to prove its case beyond a reasonable doubt. The court declined to review defendant's claim regarding the constitutionality of § 53a-182(a)(2) because it was briefed inadequately.
