State v. Coleman


(AC 23424)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 672; 851 A.2d 329; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 287


January 6, 2004, Argued  
July 6, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Coleman, 271 Conn. 910, 859 A.2d 571, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 371 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Coleman v. Conn., 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4220 (U.S., May 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Hartmere, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of tampering with a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hartmere, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of the crime of tampering with a witness, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151, as well as other crimes. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), convicted defendant of the witness tampering charge. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: During an earlier trial, defendant's girlfriend and her mother testified as alibi witnesses, and the trial resulted in a hung jury. It was subsequently discovered that the alibi testimony was fabricated based on defendant's influence. On appeal, defendant argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151 was unconstitutionally void for vagueness as applied to the fact of this case. Defendant argued that the statute did not fairly warn that its terms could be violated when a witness was willing to testify falsely at the outset, independent of any coercive influence. The appellate court found that the state supreme court had interpreted the statute such that the statute could be violated even though a witness might be independently willing to provide false testimony. Defendant was presumed to have been aware of this interpretation. Thus, the appellate court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally void. Defendant also claimed that the conviction was not supported by sufficient evidence. The appellate court held that the evidence presented by the State could have persuaded the jury beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intended to induce the witness to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Neuhaus v. DeCholnoky


(AC 23317), (AC 23946)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 576; 850 A.2d 1106; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 272


March 31, 2004, Argued  
June 29, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 271 Conn. 903, 859 A.2d 563, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 421 (2004)
Appeal granted by, in part Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 271 Conn. 904, 859 A.2d 563, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 438 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Neuhaus v. DeCholnoky, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 329 (Conn., Oct. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Adams, J.; Hon. William B. Lewis, judge trial referee.)  [*577] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, medical malpractice, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court,  [*578] Adams, J., granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the defendant Stamford Hospital; thereafter, the court, Hon. William B. Lewis, judge trial referee, granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the named defendant and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 276 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 3, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents, individually and on behalf of their child, appealed summary judgment by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), in favor of defendants, an obstetrician and a hospital. The trial court found the parents' action was time barred pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584. The parents claimed there was a continuing course of conduct, fraudulent concealment, and that § 52-584 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The child was delivered prematurely with premature lungs. He later developed a condition known as respiratory distress syndrome. The parents alleged that both the obstetrician, who delivered the child, and the neonatologist, an employee of the hospital, were negligent in several ways and that as a consequence, the child suffered from serious infirmities, including brain damage and cerebral palsy. The appellate court held that since the parents presented some evidence from which a jury could conclude that the neonatologist was aware that the child was at risk for subsequent brain injuries and failed to warn the parents of that risk, there were genuine issues of material fact as to whether the repose section of § 52-584 was tolled. However, the obstetrician did not have a duty to warn the parents of the known health risks flowing from a diagnosis of respiratory distress syndrome, as upon delivery, the child's care was entrusted to the hospital and the neonatologist. The parents failed to demonstrate the obstetrician fraudulently concealed the cause of action from them. Finally, there was a rational basis for Connecticut's three-year statute of repose embodied in § 52-584.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court as to the obstetrician was affirmed. It was reversed as to the hospital.

Hill v. Conn. State Emples. Ret. Comm'n


(AC 24478)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 599; 851 A.2d 320; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 273


March 30, 2004, Argued  
June 29, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hill v. State Emples. Ret. Comm'n, 271 Conn. 909, 859 A.2d 561, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 419 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Dunnell, J.) Appeal from a declaratory ruling by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for service connected disability retirement benefits, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Dunnell, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured worker appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) which dismissed the worker's appeal from a declaratory ruling by defendant Connecticut State Employees Retirement Commission which denied the worker's application for service-connected disability retirement benefits. The trial court held the Commission had no jurisdiction to review the state medical examining board.


OVERVIEW: The worker obtained workers' compensation benefits for his work site injury. He then filed an application for disability retirement benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-169. The medical board found the worker had not shown that his injury was service connected pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p. The appellate court held that it was indisputable that applicability of the doctrine of collateral estoppel raised difficult issues on which medical training and practice shed no light. As far as the record showed, the medical board did not seek legal advice to assist it in its deliberations. The Commission had jurisdiction to decide whether the medical board had exclusive authority to decide the worker's eligibility. The worker had not established his alleged right to a disability retirement pension. Pursuant to § 5-192p(f), the medical board had exclusive authority to decide whether his injury was service connected. As a matter of law, the medical board was not precluded from deciding the issue of service connection because that issue had not actually been litigated in prior workers' compensation proceedings. The worker was not deprived of his right to procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The Commission's declaratory ruling properly denied the worker's application for a disability retirement pension. The trial court properly dismissed the administrative appeal, albeit, on incorrect grounds.

State v. Farnum


(AC 24025)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 326; 849 A.2d 393; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 236


March 30, 2004, Argued  
June 8, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Farnum, 271 Conn. 912, 859 A.2d 572, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 375 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, Judgment entered by State v. Farnum, 275 Conn. 26, 878 A.2d 1095, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 297 (Conn., Aug. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, Espinosa, J.) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the sixth degree and substitute information in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the matters were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Espinosa, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; subsequently, the matter was tried to the court; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for judgments of acquittal and rendered judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in the first case; reversed and remanded.in the second case.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), for two counts of robbery in the first degree, one count of larceny in the sixth degree, and one count of larceny in the third degree. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress identification evidence and his motion for judgments of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Two different robberies were committed. Defendant and an acquaintance were arrested on unrelated narcotics charges. The acquaintance testified that defendant told him that he had committed a robbery. A bank employee at the second robbery identified defendant as the robber when shown a photographic array. She also made an in-court identification. The police found a green camouflage hat with an elastic chin strap from the truck of the acquaintance's girlfriend that matched a hat depicted in a black and white photograph made from the second bank's surveillance videotape at the time of the robbery. The appellate court held that after a visual review of the photographic array, it determined the array was not impermissibly suggestive although defendant's picture was darker. The difference in color composition, alone, did not render the array unnecessarily suggestive. Thus, the motion to suppress was properly denied. There was not sufficient evidence as to the first robbery as there were no witnesses who could identify defendant. But, there was sufficient evidence to prove defendant was the perpetrator of the second robbery.


OUTCOME: The judgment in the first robbery was affirmed. The judgment as to the second robbery was reversed. The second case was remanded with direction to render a judgment of not guilty.

(AC 23831)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, Miano, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, attempt to commit assault in the first degree, threatening, carrying a dangerous weapon and criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the court, Miano, J.; judgment of guilty of assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, threatening, carrying a dangerous weapon and violation of a protective order, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), Geographical Area Number 14, convicted defendant of assault in the first degree with intent to cause serious physical injury, kidnapping in the second degree, threatening, carrying a dangerous weapon, and criminal violation of a protective order. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assault in the first degree with intent to cause serious physical injury, kidnapping in the second degree, and other crimes after he grabbed the mother of his children and held her wrists while he used a box cutter to cut her face. OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the portions of the trial court's judgment that prohibited defendant from having any contact with his children until they reached the age of majority and sentenced him to five years' incarceration for carrying a dangerous weapon, affirmed the trial court's judgment in all other respects, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

McLaughlin v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


(AC 24359)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


83 Conn. App. 190; 850 A.2d 254; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 231


March 26, 2004, Argued  
June 1, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McLaughlin v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 270 Conn. 916, 853 A.2d 530, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 336 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee.) Appeal from the decision by the named defendant denying the disclosure of certain records, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
McLaughlin v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1703 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 4, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which upheld the decision of appellee Freedom of Information Commission denying the disclosure of certain records requested from appellee first selectman under the Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq., finding the records were protected by the attorney-client privilege.


OVERVIEW: A Supreme Court decision held that an ordinance restricting nonresident access to a town park with a beachfront was unconstitutional. The resident sent a letter to the board of selectmen and the newspaper urging a solution for this problem. His recommendations were rejected based on legal advice the first selectman had received. The resident made a request for documents under the Act, including all legal advice received. The first selectman released some documents, but declined to furnish legal memoranda, citing the attorney-client privilege. The resident argued that a newspaper article quoting a letter from legal counsel waived any privilege related to legal advice. The quoted letter was then disclosed, but no other documents. The Commission and the trial court dismissed the resident's appeal. On appeal, the court affirmed. The requested documents were protected by the attorney-client privilege. Because there was no pending litigation or claim involved, implied waiver of the privilege was inapplicable. Voluntarily disclosure of the letter did not create an express waiver of the privilege. The letter was not made in confidence, but was written for the very purpose of disclosure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the resident's appeal and the finding that the requested records were protected from disclosure by the attorney-client privilege.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him, following a jury trial, of eight counts of failure to pay wages in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-71b.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired individuals who were referred to him by an agency and agreed to pay them $ 15 per hour while being trained and while working for defendant. The employees were trained for two weeks, but did not receive their first paychecks. They continued working for a short time, believing that they would get paid, but defendant never paid them. The employees filed claims with the department of labor. Defendant was eventually convicted on eight counts of failure to pay wages in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-71b. State v. Hall


(AC 23045)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


82 Conn. App. 435; 844 A.2d 939; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 162


January 12, 2004, Argued  
April 13, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Hartmere, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with twenty- two counts of the crime of illegally prescribing a narcotic substance and with fourteen counts of the crime of illegally prescribing a controlled substance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hartmere, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions in arrest of the judgment and for a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Hall, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3079 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 10, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of on 22 counts of illegally prescribing a narcotic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) and 14 counts of illegally prescribing a controlled substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was a physician, was convicted on multiple counts arising from his writing of prescriptions to undercover officers. Defendant appealed, arguing the trial court improperly: (1) admitted evidence, (2) concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a- 252(a) was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness, and (3) allowed an expert to testify as to an ultimate issue in the case. The court found the trial court did not improperly admit into evidence the 13 boxes of pads of prescription forms because that was not the type of evidence that was likely to excite the passions of the jury or implicate criminal propensity. Moreover, since defendant was a physician, his obviously legitimate reasons for having the forms minimized any prejudice that could possibly result. The court next found that defendant's argument for why Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-252(a) was unconstitutionally vague would distort the intent of the legislature and would lead to an illogical result. Finally, the expert's testimony regarding prescription practices and procedures, which was elicited through the use of hypothetical questions, was necessary to educate the jury and was not impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for illegally prescribing a narcotic substance and illegally prescribing a controlled substance.

Dontigney v. Brown


(AC 23629)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


82 Conn. App. 11; 842 A.2d 597; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 101


October 28, 2003, Argued  
March 16, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Blue, J.) Action for a judgment declaring that the plaintiff is entitled to membership in the Mohegan Tribe of Indians of Connecticut, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Blue, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Dontigney v. Brown, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3297 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 8, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a claimed member of the Mohegan Tribe of Indians of Connecticut (member), challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted a motion to dismiss by defendants, the Mohegan Tribe, its tribal chairman, and its chief legal counsel (tribe), in the member's action alleging entitlement to membership in the tribe.


OVERVIEW: The member brought an action for a judgment declaring that he was entitled to membership in the tribe, and for other damages resulting from denial of his membership. The superior court dismissed the case for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and because the tribe enjoyed sovereign immunity from any other claims. The member appealed. The court found that the member failed to follow the procedures set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-66j(b), which provided that membership disputes were to be settled by a tribal council and that the council's decision would be final on substantive issues. The statute also provided an appeal to the superior court on procedural issues, but it granted primary jurisdiction of tribal membership disputes to a tribal council. Since the tribal council had primary jurisdiction and since the member did not pursue that avenue of relief, the superior court lacked subject matter jurisdiction and the action was properly dismissed. To the extent that any remaining claims could be construed as against the tribe, those claims were properly dismissed based on tribal immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the member's action.

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


82 Conn. App. 1; 842 A.2d 590; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 102


September 15, 2003, Argued  
March 16, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bailey, 269 Conn. 913, 852 A.2d 744, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 269 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Ford, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of marijuana with intent to sell, possession of more than four ounces of marijuana and conspiracy to sell marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Ford, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell marijuana by a person who is not drug-dependent, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), for possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell marijuana by a person who was not drug-dependent. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress statements he made to the police and gave improper jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: The police found $ 10,340 in United States currency and $ 20,000 in Jamaican currency, two loaded handguns, and 15 pounds of marijuana in defendant's residence. Defendant was placed under arrest and read his Miranda rights from a printed warning card. He subsequently signed and initialed a Miranda waiver form and answered questions regarding his involvement in drug activity. With respect to the oral advisement of rights upon defendant's arrest, the record did not reveal what specific rights the officer included or omitted. Thus, the appellate court did not have enough facts to judge whether the police failed to inform defendant adequately of his rights. The different factual scenarios invoked by the State concerned only one element of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b), namely, knowing possession of marijuana with the intent to sell. Accordingly, a specific unanimity instruction was not required. The trial court gave an adequate charge on the elements of conspiracy. None of the challenged instructions, when considered in the broader context of the instructions as a whole, diluted the State's burden of proof or misled the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hall v. Kasper Assocs.


(AC 23617)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


81 Conn. App. 808; 846 A.2d 228; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 96


November 21, 2003, Argued  
March 9, 2004, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Danbury, Comerford, J.) Action for a judgment declaring invalid a certain mortgage held by the named defendant against the real property of the plaintiff M & E Land Group, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Comerford, J.; judgment discharging the mortgage and granting certain other relief, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgage holder sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which declared a certain mortgage invalid, discharged it pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-13, and awarded damages as well as attorney's fees together with costs. The mortgagee contested the standing of appellee attorney and possessor.


OVERVIEW: A mortgage was given some property owners to the mortgage holder more than 20 years earlier. The evidence indicated the mortgage was satisfied. The possessor, the owner of the property at the time of litigation, and its immediate predecessors in title held an undisturbed possession of the property for more than six years. The mortgage holder failed to deliver a release, despite a demand. The attorney represented clients who purchased the former property owners' land. When those clients conveyed the land to the possessor, the unreleased mortgage to the mortgage holder was discovered, and the attorney signed an indemnity agreement with the title insurer in order to facilitate the sale to the possessor. Thus, the attorney was both statutorily and classically aggrieved. In the event that the mortgage was not declared invalid by the action brought under § 49-13, the possessor would have been required to defend any foreclosure of the mortgage holder's mortgage that was brought against its grantees who had received warranty deeds from the possessor. Since the possession was undisturbed for more than six years, the possessor was also aggrieved, even though it was not the sole owner.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Valle


(AC 23348)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


81 Conn. App. 525; 840 A.2d 1200; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 60


November 17, 2003, Argued  
February 17, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Valle, 268 Conn. 921, 846 A.2d 883, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 173 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Danbury, White, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts each of the crimes of sale of a hallucinogenic substance and conspiracy to sell a hallucinogenic substance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before White, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court granted in part the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment of guilty of four counts of sale of a hallucinogenic substance and of one count of conspiracy to sell a hallucinogenic substance, from which the defendant appealed to this court. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a jury verdict, the Superior Court, Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), convicted defendant of four counts of sale of a hallucinogenic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-277(a) and 53a-8, and one count of conspiracy to sell a hallucinogenic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-277(a) and 53a-48. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose from four incidents in which defendant arranged to sell "Ecstasy," a hallucinogenic substance, to a cooperating witness in an undercover operation. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury as to accessory liability. The appellate court held that as defendant failed to take an exception to the trial court's instructions, the Golding standard applied. The appellate court held that the trial court properly instructed the jury on the use of circumstantial evidence. The trial court properly defined the intent elements of accessorial liability and instructed the jury that the State had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt each and every element of the crimes charged. Therefore, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by the trial court's instruction on the use of circumstantial evidence to infer the intent elements of accessorial liability. The appellate court further held that because defendant had to have knowingly sold a hallucinogenic substance to violate Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), it was proper for the trial court to instruct the jury on the definition of "knowingly" as part of its accessory charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Spiegelmann


(AC 22726)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


81 Conn. App. 441; 840 A.2d 69; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 51


November 18, 2003, Argued  
February 10, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Spiegelmann, 268 Conn. 921, 846 A.2d 882, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 171 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Spiegelmann, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2389 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 24, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Spiegelmann v. Warden, State Prison, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2173 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Blue, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and one count of unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Blue, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of three counts each of sexual assault in the first degree and one count of risk of injury to a child, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2), risk of injury to a child, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(1) (1997), risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(2) (1997), and unlawful restraint, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95(a). Defendant appealed the convictions.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant were based on the claims of the victim that defendant sexually assaulted her on a regular basis beginning at age four. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in admission of "scatological" fantasy stories that were printed from the Internet and the admission of some e-mail correspondence arising out of Internet chat room discussions. The appellate court held that the issue of the e-mail chats was not preserved for review, and that issues of evidence were not reviewable under the Golding doctrine. As to the scatological stories, the appellate court held that defendant failed to show any harm based on the admission. A large amount of similar evidence was properly identified by the victim, and defendant did not object to those admissions. Defendant next argued that the trial court improperly admitted testimony of four witnesses under the constancy of accusation doctrine. The appellate court again held that defendant failed to preserve the issue for appeal. Defendant finally argued that the prosecutor committed misconduct. The appellate court held that the use of rhetorical devices by the prosecutor during closing arguments was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

675 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crudup


(AC 23263)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


81 Conn. App. 248; 838 A.2d 1053; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 35


September 10, 2003, Argued  
January 27, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Crudup, 268 Conn. 913, 845 A.2d 415, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 136 (Conn., Mar. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, geographical area number seven, Winslow, J.) Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts each of the crimes of threatening and breach of the peace and, in the second part, with being a persistent offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Winslow, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of threatening and breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Superior Court in the New Haven at Meriden Judicial District convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of one count each of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-62(a)(2) (Rev. to 1999) threatening and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(3) (Rev. to 1999) breach of peace. Defendant appealed, contending that since breach of peace was a lesser included offense of threatening, his two concurrent sentences for one act violated double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stated he was trying to protect his son when he told the victim that he should "pop" the victim. Defendant could argue double jeopardy was violated even though the sentences were concurrent and even though that argument was not preserved. The Blockburger test was applied and required two conditions: that both crimes arise out of the same incident and be the same offense. Defendant's statement, as the predicate act for both crimes, satisfied the first condition. The appeals court's analysis concluded (1) that it could not determine that the legislature specifically intended to create two separate crimes and punishments for the same act, and (2) that breach of peace was not a lesser included offense of threatening, based on both crimes' statutory requirements, as a person could commit either crime without committing the other. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183's intent to harass, annoy, or alarm could be accomplished without necessarily violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-62(a)(2)'s threatening to commit any crime of violence with the intent to terrorize another, and vice-versa. Section 53a-62(a)(2) was not facially vague. The specific intent instructions were proper.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Green


(AC 22968)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


81 Conn. App. 152; 838 A.2d 1030; 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 25


October 16, 2003, Argued  
January 20, 2004, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Green, 268 Conn. 909, 845 A.2d 413, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 138 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New London at Norwich, geographical area number twenty-one, Robaina, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell narcotics by a person who is not drug- dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, and tried to the jury before Robaina, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New London Superior Court (Connecticut) denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of a sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer parked his car on a street. A man approached. The officer used street talk to explain to him that he needed crack cocaine. The man said it was being cooked. The officer said he would wait. The man entered a building, exited a minute later with defendant in his company, and walked towards the officer's car. Defendant stopped several feet short of the car. The man walked up to it. The man then handed the officer a quantity of crack cocaine. The officer paid for it, and then watched the man walk to defendant and hand the money to him. The trial court instructed the jury on accessory liability and conspiracy. Defendant was then found guilty of selling narcotics and conspiring to sell narcotics. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal, as the trial court's instructions on conspiracy and accessorial liability did not mislead the jury, the evidence supported a finding that defendant acted as an accessory, defendant was not placed in jeopardy twice for the same offense, and the trial court properly instructed the jury on the elements of conspiracy to sell narcotics.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Russo v. Common Council of Middletown


(AC 23380)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


80 Conn. App. 100; 832 A.2d 1227; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 458


May 27, 2003, Argued  
November 4, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Middlesex, B. Fischer, J.) Application for a writ of mandamus to compel the defendants to publish, inter alia, a corrected city budget, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, B. Fischer, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike and rendered judgment of dismissal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Russo v. Common Council of Middletown, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1847 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which granted defendant city officials' motion to strike an application for a writ of mandamus to compel publication of a corrected city budget and rendered a judgment of dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the city officials improperly reduced the net taxable grand list for a budget year, thereby increasing the city's mill rate and raising taxes for city residents. The city officials claimed that the action had been rendered moot because the contested practice had ceased and that the action should be dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the action was moot because the budgeting methods had changed. Although an exception to the mootness doctrine existed with regard to a claim that was capable of repetition, yet evading review, the court found that the exception did not apply. The taxpayer's claims were not of a nature to evade review because the budget process was not of a limited duration and did not present a functionally insurmountable time constraint. Moreover, the claim did not appear to be capable of repetition because there was no indication that the city officials planned to use the same budgeting method in the future.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the action.

 

678 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Claud-Chambers v. City of W. Haven


(AC 22792)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


79 Conn. App. 475; 830 A.2d 385; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 407


June 6, 2003, Argued  
September 16, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Claud-Chambers v. City of West Haven, 266 Conn. 924, 835 A.2d 472, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 510 (2003)
Related proceeding at Claud-Chambers v. City of W. Haven, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17534 (D. Conn., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Arnold, J.) Action to recover damages for the alleged taking by inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiffs' real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Arnold, J., granted the defendants' motions for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Claud-Chambers v. City of W. Haven, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 282 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 4, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the city and its redevelopment agency, filed a statement of compensation for the taking of plaintiff property owners' properties. Then a certificate of taking was filed. No appeal was ever filed by the property owners. The property owners filed an inverse condemnation proceeding. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted defendants' motions for summary judgment. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the property owners argued that the trial court improperly determined, as a matter of law, that they were precluded from bringing an action for inverse condemnation after eminent domain proceedings had been concluded. The appellate court concluded that the trial court properly determined that Russo controlled the appeal. The property owners received just compensation through the condemnation proceedings and chose not to challenge the value assigned to the property during those proceedings. They failed to challenge the valuation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-132. If the property owners were unsatisfied with the compensation that they received, an appeal should have been taken during the compensation process. The property owners' inverse condemnation claim would serve only to relitigate the issues that were resolved in the eminent domain action. The fact that the property owners chose not to pursue their remedies pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 8-129 to 8-133 was fatal to their claim. There could be no valid inverse condemnation claim when the property in question already had been taken by eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Bain v. Inland Wetlands Comm'n


(AC 23240)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


78 Conn. App. 808; 829 A.2d 18; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 361


May 29, 2003, Argued  
August 19, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, Hon. George W. Ripley II, judge trial referee.) Appeal from the decision by the defendant inland wetlands commission denying the plaintiffs' application for a permit to construct a house on property containing an area of wetlands, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Hon. George W. Ripley II, judge trial referee; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Bain v. Inland Wetlands Comm'n of Oxford, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1390 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 24, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, prospective property owners, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut). The trial court dismissed their appeal of a decision by defendant, the Inland Wetlands Commission of the Town of Oxford, which denied their application for a wetlands and watercourses permit in connection with the proposed construction of a residential home.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs submitted an application to the Commission for permission to build a two bedroom residential home, a driveway, and a septic system. A portion of the proposed construction was for a driveway and piping for the septic system, which would cross 267 square feet of wetlands. The Commission denied the application, and the trial court affirmed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The record before the Commission contained substantial evidence to support its decision that activities on the non-wetlands portion of the land would likely impact or affect the wetlands, resulting in additional decline in its functional values. A site inspection report indicated the potential dangers of flooding resulting from fill on the lot, flooding onto neighboring property, and seasonal flooding. A report by a soil scientist stated that the household use of fertilizer, pesticides, and herbicides was a concern because the wet conditions encountered on the site for much of the year promoted the mobility of those items. The report also identified problems with the septic system leaching field in light of the unidirectional flow of perched groundwater on the property's level terrain.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.

State v. Lopes


(AC 22596)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


78 Conn. App. 264; 826 A.2d 1238; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 330



July 29, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lopes, 266 Conn. 902, 832 A.2d 66, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 383 (2003)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Ford, J.) Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of attempt to commit murder, and one count each of the crimes of assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, and, in the second part, with the crime of possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty one count each of attempt to commit murder, assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit; thereafter, the court dismissed the charge of possession of a firearm, denied the defendant's motion for a new trial, rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and imposed sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of attempt to commit murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-54a(a), and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached the victim while he was standing outside the police substation. They had had words some days earlier, and an exchange again took place whereupon the victim was shot. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly (1) instructed the jury on the charge of attempt to commit murder, (2) deprived him of a fair trial as a result of the court's remarks, criticism and elicitation of evidence from witnesses, (3) restricted cross-examination, and (4) failed to admonish jurors as required. The appellate court found that defendant did not properly preserve his claim of an improper instruction for appeal. Further, it was defendant's contention that the instructions as a whole misled the jury and diluted the State's burden of proof. The appellate court found that the trial court properly instructed the jury as to the State's burden of proof regarding intent to cause a death necessary to convict defendant on the charge of attempt to commit murder. That instruction, however, did not eliminate any possible juror confusion concerning the element of intent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the conviction of attempt to commit murder, and the case was remanded for a new trial on that charge.

State v. Charles


(AC 21771)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


78 Conn. App. 125; 826 A.2d 1172; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 317



July 22, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Charles, 266 Conn. 908, 832 A.2d 73, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 400 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, Harper, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of harassment in the second degree and violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Harper, J.; verdict of guilty of violation of a protective order; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, geographical area number six (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of violation of a protective order under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-1103 (Rev. to 1999), now Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-223.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested for domestic violence, a protective order was issued forbidding him from threatening or harassing the victim. Defendant then telephoned the victim twice, leaving messages on her answering machine that were rife with expletives and threats. On appeal from defendant's conviction, the court held that the trial court did not violate defendant's constitutional right to due process by failing to charge the jury that intent was a necessary element of the crime because the statute was a general intent statute and no instruction on general intent was required as defendant had not put in issue the question of whether his conduct was voluntary. Defendant's vagueness and overbreadth challenges as to application failed because the order was adequate to give him fair warning that leaving two expletive and posturing laden messages on the victim's answering machine constituted a violation of the order prohibiting him from harassing or threatening her. Finally, there was sufficient evidence for conviction because the jury could have concluded that defendant violated the protective order by leaving two messages replete with profanities and thinly disguised threats.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Caracoglia


(AC 22607)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


78 Conn. App. 98; 826 A.2d 192; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 306



July 15, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Caracoglia, 266 Conn. 903, 832 A.2d 65, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 385 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, Alexander, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of breach of the peace, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, and tried to the jury before Alexander, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), for breach of peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(2) and (5) (Rev. to 2001). The trial court denied motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial. Defendant claimed the trial court improperly allowed the state to amend the information. Defendant also claimed that § 53a-181(a)(5) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant verbally and physically accosted the victim outside a hardware store. At no time did the victim attempt to strike defendant. At the time of the attack, people were walking in the parking lot and passing in cars. The State, by substitute information, charged defendant with two counts of breach of the peace in violation of § 53a-181. After the parties had presented evidence, but before closing arguments and jury instructions by the court, the State filed its second substitute information, which amended count one. The appellate court held the State did not charge an additional or different offense by the omission of "tumultuous" behavior. Defendant could not demonstrate that a substantive right may have been prejudiced by the amended information. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the state to amend the information. Section 53a-181(a)(5) was not overbroad. It did not prohibit constitutionally protected speech. Therefore, there was no clear constitutional violation that deprived defendant of a fair trial and his claim failed to satisfy the third prong of Golding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Rudy's Limousine Serv. v. Comm'r, DOT


(AC 23013)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


78 Conn. App. 80; 826 A.2d 1161; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 310


March 25, 2003, Argued  
July 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 26, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Cohn, J., Schuman, J.) Appeal from the decision by the named defendant granting in part and denying in part the plaintiff's application to operate a livery service, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Rudy's Limousine Serv. v. State DOT, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1072 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 11, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff livery service applied under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13b-103 for additional livery permits from defendant commissioner of the Connecticut department of transportation. The application was partially granted. The service appealed to the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut). That court granted the department's motion to strike and the service's appeal was dismissed. The service appealed that order.


OVERVIEW: The service sought an additional 61 livery permits. The department granted five new permits after it determined that five was the number of permits that would improve the public's convenience and necessity, the criteria set out in § 13b-103(b). The service contended that the statute lacked the constitutionally required standards to guide the department in making determinations about livery permits and that the department improperly applied the standard set out in § 13b-103(b) to the service's application. The trial court never reached the constitutional question. The court addressed both contentions and affirmed. The court held that (1) although the service was seeking a benefit under the statute, the court could still properly consider the constitutional issue; (2) the standard of "public convenience and necessity" set out in § 13b-103(b) was constitutionally sufficient to provide the department with guidance in considering permit applications; (3) the trial court applied the proper standard in reviewing the service's appeal; and (4) the department reasonably interpreted § 13b-103(b) to require an applicant to satisfy all of the factors enumerated therein for issuance of permits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


(AC 23014), (AC 23015), (AC 23016), (AC 23017), (AC 23069), (AC 23078), (AC 23079), (AC 23161)

77 Conn. App. 690; 825 A.2d 153; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 280

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 266 Conn. 906, 832 A.2d 71, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 398 (2003)
Appeal granted by Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 266 Conn. 907, 832 A.2d 72, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 399 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Rosado v. Bridgeport Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2005 Conn. LEXIS 482 (Conn., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Levin, J.; McWeeny, J.). Actions to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the plaintiffs as a result of the defendants' alleged negligent supervision of employees, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Levin, J., granted the defendants' requests for the protection of discovery materials from disclosure; thereafter, the matter was transferred to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury; subsequently, the action was withdrawn as against the defendants; thereafter, the New York Times filed a motion to intervene and to vacate the protective orders, and the Hartford Courant Company et al. filed motions to intervene; subsequently, the court, McWeeny, J., ordered the creation of a new file for the purpose of docketing the application to vacate the protective orders and the motions to intervene, and the named defendant et al. filed three appeals to this court and the intervenor John Doe et al. filed an appeal to this court; subsequently, the court rendered judgment ordering, inter alia, the unsealing and release of certain documents in the custody of the [***2] clerk of the Superior Court, from which the defendant Charles Carr et al., the named defendant et al., the intervenor John Doe et al. and the defendant Martin Frederici filed separate appeals to this court.
In re New York Times, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1634 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 8, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, clergymen and diocese, and intervenor newspaper publishers, appealed separately from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which ordered the unsealing and release of certain documents in the court clerk's custody, which had been previously under protective orders in an underlying personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Twenty-three lawsuits were filed against clergymen and the diocese, alleging sexual abuse of minors, all of which were withdrawn upon settlement prior to trial. Documents obtained by counsel had been sealed and protective orders had issued during pretrial discovery. More than one year thereafter, the trial court granted the publishers' application for creation of a new file and also granted the motion to vacate sealing and protective orders entered in those lawsuits. The court held that the creation of a new file should not have been granted because the trial court no longer had continuing jurisdiction after the jurisdictional time limitation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a expired, and accordingly that and the subsequent orders regarding disclosure of the sealed and protected materials were erroneous. The court noted that the appeal from the order creating a new file was proper because it effectively restored the underlying cases to the docket. The court held that the trial court had no inherent authority over the files in its custody that would have permitted it to so act. There was no waiver of the limitation period, nor was the protective order akin to an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the trial court regarding the newspapers' application for creation of a new file and the subsequent orders regarding disclosure of the sealed and protected materials.

State v. Cotton


(AC 23473)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


77 Conn. App. 749; 825 A.2d 189; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 281



July 1, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal denied by State v. Cotton, 265 Conn. 911, 831 A.2d 251, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 369 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Hon. William L. Hadden, Jr., judge trial referee.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of unlawful restraint in the first degree and with the crimes of unlawful restraint in the second degree, kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. William L. Hadden, Jr., judge trial referee; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), that convicted defendant of unlawful restraint in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the second degree, kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third degree, and burglary in the first degree. The trial court also denied defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The victim was invited to dine with defendant and his wife. The victim was 52 years old, partially blind, and developmentally disabled. Defendant drove the victim home. After unsuccessfully attempting to coerce and then force the victim to have sex with him on the way home, defendant attacked and raped her at her home. After his conviction, the appellate court found that there was no evidentiary basis from which a reasonable fact finder could have determined that the victim had consented to defendant's behavior toward her on the evening in question, either by her words or actions. Further, there was no evidentiary basis on which the jury could have concluded that defendant could have misapprehended the victim's attitude toward his advances. Contrary to defendant's claims on appeal, the appellate court believed that the prosecutor's comments were not such that the jury would naturally and necessarily consider them to be comments on defendant's failure to testify. Instead, the comment could reasonably have been understood as an effort by the prosecutor to remind the jury of the evidence regarding the victim's intellectual and emotional limitations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Stewart


(AC 22465)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


77 Conn. App. 393; 823 A.2d 392; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 257



June 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Stewart, 265 Conn. 906, 831 A.2d 253, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 356 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, Hon. Bernard D. Gaffney, judge trial referee.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the jury before Hon. Bernard D. Gaffney, judge trial referee; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal of possession of narcotics; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Stewart, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4202 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 10, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of the sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent. The trial court had previously granted his motion for judgment of acquittal on the charge of possession of narcotics, and after trial, denied the same relief with respect to the sale charge.


OVERVIEW: Police officers who were watching the area of a motel where defendant was, based on information that there was drug activity, observed defendant making phone calls in a pattern that appeared to be drug-related. An undercover officer bought drugs from him and defendant was thereafter arrested and charged. The trial court granted his motion for a judgment of acquittal with respect to the possession charge, finding that he was legally in possession of a painkiller pursuant to a prescription. He was convicted on the sale charge. On appeal, the court held that defendant's claim that he was a "drug-dependent person" within Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) because he was medically dependent on the painkiller did not show, by a preponderance of the evidence, that he was dependent on drugs at the time of the charged offense. Accordingly, the denial of his motion for a judgment of acquittal was proper. Additionally, it was noted that defendant's claim that the statutory definitions of drug dependence in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) were unconstitutionally vague lacked merit because he failed to show that a constitutional violation clearly existed that clearly deprived him of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Musumano


(AC 22870)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


76 Conn. App. 724; 822 A.2d 261; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 210


February 14, 2003, Argued  
May 20, 2003, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, Fuger, J.). Information charging the defendant with the crimes of harassment in the second degree, disorderly conduct and threatening, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Fuger, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of recklessly engaging in disorderly conduct, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), for recklessly engaging in disorderly conduct. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court's jury instructions improperly failed to provide the necessary judicial gloss to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(2) as required by Indrisano.


OVERVIEW: Defendant called the department of labor's telephone benefits center to inquire into why he had not received his unemployment benefits check. While speaking to an employee, defendant became upset, cursed the employee, and hung up the telephone. Defendant called a couple more times and eventually told another employee that he was going to sue the state for all of its money, and that he was crazy and was going to get a gun and shoot the employee. Defendant did not raise his jury charge claim at trial and sought review under Golding. The appellate court held the trial court failed to provide the necessary judicial gloss to § 53a-182(a)(2), as required by Indrisano. While the trial court's charge to the jury included the required judicial gloss to the phrase "annoys or interferes with another person," it failed to include the necessary judicial gloss to the phrase "by offensive and disorderly conduct." Since § 53a-182(a)(2) was unconstitutionally vague on its face without the judicial gloss, it could not be said, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the omission of the Indrisano gloss did not contribute to the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial on the disorderly conduct charge.

 

688 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Pearce v. City of New Haven


(AC 22958)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


76 Conn. App. 441; 819 A.2d 878; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 194


February 20, 2003, Argued  
April 29, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Pearce v. City of New Haven, 264 Conn. 913, 826 A.2d 1155, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 278 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from the workers' compensation review board.) Appeal from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district dismissing the plaintiff's claim for benefits, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fireman claimed entitlement to workers' compensation benefits pursuant to General Statutes § 7-433c, commonly referred to as the Heart and Hypertension Act. The workers' compensation commissioner determined that the fireman's claim for benefits was untimely, and he dismissed the claim. The workers' compensation review board (Connecticut) affirmed the determination. The fireman appealed.


OVERVIEW: The fireman claimed that the commissioner improperly concluded that his claim for benefits was untimely, as he was not diagnosed with, placed on medication for, or disabled by hypertension until October 15, 1998. The appellate court held that the board correctly upheld the commissioner's decision that the fireman's claim for benefits was untimely, as the commissioner's conclusion reflected a proper application of the law to the facts of the case. The fireman failed to file a notice of injury or claim until 1998, despite having been repeatedly informed by his physician that his blood pressure readings during 1988, 1989, and 1990 were elevated. The procedure for determining recovery under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c was the same as that outlined in Conn. Gen. Stat. tit. 31, ch. 568 of the Connecticut Workers' Compensation Act. Accordingly, the fireman was required to provide both notice of injury and notice of a claim, despite whether his symptoms of hypertension caused immediate permanent or partial disability.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the workers' compensation review board was affirmed.

State v. Pare


(AC 23066)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


75 Conn. App. 474; 816 A.2d 657; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 86



March 11, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by State v. Pare, 263 Conn. 924, 823 A.2d 1216, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 215 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Devlin, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At the end of a trial held after the Supreme Court of Connecticut reversed defendant's first conviction on a charge of murder, a jury sitting in the Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), returned a verdict finding defendant guilty of murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. The superior court denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and entered judgment convicting defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder after he told police that he killed a woman who lived with him. Defendant testified at his first trial and told the jury that he had never "put his hands on a female" before he killed the victim. Defendant was convicted of murder after his first trial, but his conviction was reversed on appeal. In defendant's second trial, defendant elected not to testify, but during the State's case-in-chief, defendant's testimony from the first trial was read to the jury and a police officer testified that defendant told him he had "never hit a woman before" when he reported the incident. After that evidence was introduced, the prosecutor offered a page from defendant's medical records which showed that defendant admitted assaulting his niece. The appellate court held that (1) pursuant to Conn. Code Evid. R. 8-8, the fact that defendant did not testify at his second trial did not preclude the State from using defendant's medical records to impeach defendant's statement to the police officer and the statement he made when he testified at his first trial; and (2) the instructions on reasonable doubt which the trial court gave the jury were not flawed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Crone v. Connelly


(AC 22156)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


74 Conn. App. 788; 813 A.2d 1084; 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 41


October 29, 2002, Argued  
February 4, 2003, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Crone v. Connelly, 263 Conn. 902, 819 A.2d 836, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 122 (2003)
Affirmed by Crone v. Connelly, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 18 (Conn., Feb. 3, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Hon. Edward F. Stodolink, judge trial referee.). Action to recover damages for the alleged violation of the plaintiff's civil rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the matter was tried to the jury before Hon. Edward F. Stodolink, judge trial referee; directed verdict and judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher filed an action against defendants, a superintendent and officers, alleging violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, false arrest, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and malicious prosecution. After a jury deadlocked, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) directed a verdict on favor of defendants. The teacher appealed.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was arrested after he allegedly physically abused his students. The teacher was found not guilty on the charges against him. On appeal, the teacher claimed that the trial court improperly granted defendants' motion for a directed verdict by concluding that there was insufficient evidence to establish that they had conspired to violate the teacher's rights. The appellate court concluded that the directed verdict was appropriate since the only evidence presented by the teacher went to ill will toward the teacher by the superintendent due to the teacher's critical appraisal of the superintendent's performance. Mere speculation based on the past ill will of one defendant was not sufficient to support the teacher's claim. The teacher also claimed the trial court erred in finding that that probable cause did exist to arrest the teacher. The appellate court held that the directed verdict on the false arrest and malicious prosecution claims were proper because the stories of seven students corroborated each other and the school nurse's report documented the students' physical injuries.


OUTCOME: The directed verdict in favor of defendants was affirmed.

State v. Feliciano


(AC 23063)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


74 Conn. App. 391; 812 A.2d 141; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 654


October 29, 2002, Argued  
December 31, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Feliciano, 262 Conn. 952, 817 A.2d 110, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 88 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Lavine, J.). Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and imposing sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with the use of a firearm; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court for the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him on a jury verdict of murder, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a). The trial court sentenced defendant to 45 years in prison, plus five consecutive and non-suspendable years, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k, for a total effective sentence of 50 years.


OVERVIEW: Three eyewitnesses testified that defendant fled after he shot a victim twice. The court opined that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict, and the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in instructing the jury about his flight from the scene and his statements after the shooting. The court held that while the trial court could have referenced defendant's explanations for his flight, it was not required to do so. Further, defendant's claim about the instructions regarding his statements was not preserved for review. Because neither claim raised a constitutional issue, the court reviewed the entire charge in determining that no injustice resulted from the instructions presented to the jury. In the court's view, defendant's complaint that the trial court improperly limited hearsay testimony was unpreserved, evidentiary in nature, and was not of constitutional magnitude. Finally, the trial court's failure to submit the issue of the applicability of § 53-202k to the jury, and its imposition of an enhanced sentence under the statute, were harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
