State v. Melendez


(AC 22785)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


74 Conn. App. 215; 811 A.2d 261; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 629


October 16, 2002, Argued  
December 24, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Melendez, 262 Conn. 951, 817 A.2d 111, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 87 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Melendez v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3344 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Ford, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder and with the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a new trial and for a judgment of acquittal, and rendered judgment imposing sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Connecticut Superior Court, Fairfield Judicial District, convicting him on jury verdict of murder and imposing sentence with a firearm enhancement. On appeal defendant challenged various aspects of the jury charge and argued that his cross-examination of a key witness had been unconstitutionally limited.


OVERVIEW: Eyewitnesses and the victim, before his death, identified defendant as the person who argued with him and then shot him many times. Under those circumstances, the appellate court held that the evidence of defendant's specific intent to kill was so strong that there was no requirement to comply with defendant's request for an instruction on first-degree manslaughter. The general jury instruction regarding determination of witness credibility was perfectly adequate despite its failure to single out the key eyewitness by name. Jurors would not have had any trouble, at the end of a short trial, remembering that only two witnesses had testified to having felony convictions. Even if defendant had preserved his challenge to an instruction on flight as evidence of consciousness of guilt, such an instruction was not improper in Connecticut, and there was no abuse of discretion in giving it in defendant's case. Finally, certain restrictions on defendant's cross-examination of the key eyewitness regarding her drug use were the natural result of defendant's having failed to lay a foundation for such evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Rivera


(AC 20386)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


74 Conn. App. 129; 810 A.2d 824; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 628


September 26, 2002 1, Argued


1 This appeal was first argued on December 13, 2001. Judge John J. Daly, a member of the panel that heard oral argument on that date, died before the panel was able to concur on a written decision. The appeal, therefore, was argued a second time.

 
December 17, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Mulcahy, J.) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, assault in the first degree, criminal possession of a firearm and carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of tampering with a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Mulcahy, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain identification evidence in each case; thereafter, the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury; subsequently, the state entered a nolle as to the charge of attempt to commit murder; verdicts and judgments of guilty of assault in the first degree, criminal possession of a firearm, carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit and tampering with a witness, imposing a sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Hartford Judicial District (Connecticut), convicting him of first-degree assault, weapons offenses, and witness tampering, and imposing a sentence that had been enhanced by reason of his prior felony convictions and use of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in a nightclub shooting after being implicated by a female companion and being identified in a photo array by the victim. The appellate court held that the evidence was ample to support his conviction. It was for the jury to determine credibility issues, and the victim's initial failure to provide a description was explained by the fact that medical personnel did not allow police to interview him. The eyewitness identification evidence was properly admissible. Not only was the array not unduly suggestive, but even if it had been, the victim's in-court identification had an independent basis in that he had ample opportunity to observe defendant earlier on the evening of the shooting. Finally, the reference to prior felony convictions involving a firearm was more probative than it was prejudicial. Although the jury rather than the trial court should have found the facts underlying a sentence enhancement under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k, the error was harmless because the jury had already made other findings indicating use of a firearm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in all respects.

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

Writ of habeas corpus granted Horn v. Warden, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1362 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Devlin, J.). Substitute informations charging the defendant in each case with the crime of felony murder, three counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, two counts of the crime of attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, and with the crimes of assault in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict and judgment in the first case of guilty of felony murder, three counts of robbery in the first degree, two counts of attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, and verdict and judgment of guilty in the second case, from which the defendants filed separate appeals.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted by a jury in a joint trial in the Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Connecticut, of felony murder, three counts of robbery, two counts of attempt to commit robbery, conspiracy to commit robbery, one count of assault as to only one defendant, two counts of attempt to commit robbery as to only one defendant, and carrying a pistol without a permit. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting into evidence a redacted copy of a witness's statement to the police as a prior inconsistent statement. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a defendant's motion for severance of the trial; and it did not err in denying motions to suppress identifications of defendants by witnesses from photographic arrays and by the accomplice who testified for the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McEnerney v. United States Surgical Corp.


(AC 22437)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


72 Conn. App. 611; 805 A.2d 816; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 506


May 3, 2002, Argued  
October 1, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from the workers' compensation review board) Appeal by the plaintiff from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district denying her application for disability benefits, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff worker sought workers' compensation for an injury sustained while she was employed by defendant employer. The Workers' Compensation Review Board (Connecticut) affirmed a decision of the commissioner, which denied the benefits. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The worker received benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308a. However, when she was still entitled to 15.72 more weeks of those benefits, she moved to Florida. The commissioner found that, because she moved to Florida, she did not meet the requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308a(a) that the benefits were only available to employees who were willing and able to perform work in Connecticut. On appeal, the worker claimed that the board: (1) improperly affirmed the determination that she was not entitled to the benefits, as she moved to Florida; and (2) improperly enforced the requirement that she be willing and able to perform work in Connecticut, as that requirement improperly restricted her right to interstate travel. The appellate court found that the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-308a(a) was plain and unambiguous and required that a claimant be both willing and able to perform work in Connecticut. The board properly found that the worker was neither willing nor able to perform work in Connecticut. The right to travel did not encompass one's right to relocate to another state and yet avail oneself of the benefits to which one was entitled in one's former state.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Morales


AC 21470


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


71 Conn. App. 790; 804 A.2d 902; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 453


October 30, 2001, Argued  
August 27, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Morales, 262 Conn. 902, 810 A.2d 270, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 425 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Morales v. Brighthaupt, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 144751 (D. Conn., Oct. 22, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Waterbury, Gill, J. Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Gill, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Morales, 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2287 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 21, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Waterbury Judicial District (Connecticut), convicting him on jury verdict of murder. He claimed various Batson irregularities during jury selection, the trial court's failure to give various requested jury instructions, and that the jury was improperly instructed regarding reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: There was an enormous amount of evidence that defendant committed a brutal murder, including statements, later recanted, by both defendant and a woman friend in whom he confided, but the two defense theories he sought to advance were that he was intoxicated at the time and that he was altogether innocent. The appellate court held that neither claim was based in the evidence, and innocence was not a theory of defense, so defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on either subject. Although the trial court should not have mentioned that it was not customary to tape interrogations in Connecticut, the reference to that information did not deprive defendant of a fair trial, nor did the trial court's articulation of reasonable doubt. Finally, none of defendant's Batson challenges, not even the one in which the trial court bent over backwards to be fair to defendant and refused to allow the State to peremptorily challenge the juror in question, had merit, as the State showed race-neutral reasons for its challenges in all three situations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Clements v. Jones


(AC 21263)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


71 Conn. App. 688; 803 A.2d 378; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 431


March 22, 2002, Argued  
August 20, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, Coppeto, J.). Application by the paternal grandmother for visitation rights with the defendant's minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Coppeto, J.; judgment granting, in part, the application, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
 Clements v. Jones, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3000 (Conn. Super. Ct. Nov. 14, 2000).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother of a minor child appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which awarded visitation to plaintiff paternal grandmother, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother filed an application seeking visitation with the child. After a hearing, the trial court entered an order granting the grandmother visitation rights. On appeal, the mother argued the trial court improperly: (1) violated her U.S. Const. amend. XIV right to family privacy by requiring her to make her child available to the grandmother; and (2) applied Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 because the grandmother already had access to the child. The appellate court concluded the grandmother's allegations and the proof were insufficient to invoke the trial court's jurisdiction, and the evidence could not satisfy the high clear and convincing standard. Specifically, the appellate court determined the proof did not allow the appellate court to conclude that there was clear and convincing evidence the grandmother had a parent-like relationship with the child. In other words, the appellate court found an absence of the essential allegations and proof in support thereof, both of the nature of the relationship between the grandmother and the child as well as the harm that the child would suffer were visitation denied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment dismissing the application.

State v. Robert H.


(AC 20836)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

July 30, 2002, Officially Released

Affirmed by State v. Robert H., 273 Conn. 56, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 54 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Robinson-Thomas, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and with one count of the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the court, Robinson-Thomas, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part. Remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction, rendered after a trial to the court, of four counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 and one count of sexual assault in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-73a(a)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the evidence was insufficient to support defendant's conviction for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 with respect to the charges contained in the first, fourth, and fifth counts of the information. The State elected to charge under the second part of Conn. Gen. The court did not deprive defendant of his constitutional rights to testify on his behalf when it ruled that he had waived that right. The lower court properly ruled that defendant waived his right to testify on his behalf as he failed to invoke affirmatively his right to testify on his behalf. The lower court did not deprive defendant of his federal and state constitutional rights to effective assistance of counsel by refusing to permit defense counsel to withdraw during the sentencing phase of the trial. The prosecutor's comments did not prejudicially influence the court in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the conviction of risk of injury to a child under counts one, four, and five of the information and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment of not guilty on those charges.

State v. David P.


(AC 20907)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


70 Conn. App. 462; 800 A.2d 541; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 335


February 14, 2002, Argued  
June 18, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. David P., 262 Conn. 907, 810 A.2d 275, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 447 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied David P. v. Warden, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1232 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 19, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Fracasse, J.) Substitute information, in one case, charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, and substitute information, in another case, charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and substitute information, in a third case, charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the third degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three separate cases involving three separate minor female victims consolidated for trial, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted defendant of counts of 1st degree sexual assault, 3rd degree sexual assault, and risk of injury to a child, and sentenced him to a total effective term of 90 years in prison. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with the victims at the times of the assaults in their home. The appeals court, in affirming the judgment, determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by consolidating the cases because (1) the factual predicate to each case was distinct, (2) defendant was not prejudiced by the joinder of a shocking and brutal case, and (3) the trial was not overly complex or exceptionally long. The evidence of one offense could have been admitted in a separate trial of the other offenses to prove a pattern of criminal conduct. Additionally, the trial court's instructions cured any possible prejudice. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by excluding distracting, side issue, evidence of false complaints which had been admitted on a prior mistrial. Defendant failed to preserve or properly raise certain arguments. The prosecutor's closing arguments and comments were not improper. The prosecutor did not improperly appeal to the jury's emotions, not did his comments on defendant's closing arguments or to recall the victims' testimony rise to level to deprive defendant of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

 

700 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Salmeri v. Dep't of Pub. Safety


(AC 21106)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


70 Conn. App. 321; 798 A.2d 481; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 319


September 17, 2001, Argued  
June 11, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from the workers' compensation review board.) Appeal by the defendant from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district awarding permanent partial disability benefits to the plaintiff, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from the judgment of the workers' compensation review board which affirmed the workers' compensation commissioner's finding that plaintiff state trooper's heart condition was compensable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-145a. The employer claimed the board improperly determined, inter alia, that the trooper's condition resulted in partial disability, and the presumption in § 5-145a was not adequately rebutted.


OVERVIEW: The trooper began his employment after successfully passing a physical examination in which he was found to be free of hypertension and heart disease. He subsequently was found to suffer from atrial fibrillation with rapid ventricular response and was given a 10 percent permanent partial disability rating. The commissioner concluded that, while the trooper's employment did not cause his atrial fibrillation, it did produce symptoms which permanently aggravated a preexisting condition, which produced a permanent impairment. Accordingly, the trooper was awarded benefits. The appellate court held the trooper should have pursued his claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-4a. However, given the facts, the trooper's award was upheld. The commissioner did not abuse his discretion by concluding that the 10 percent rating was compensable as a permanent partial disability of the trooper's heart. The commissioner correctly concluded that the statutory presumption in § 5-145a, which was the same as § 29-4a, was not rebutted.


OUTCOME: The decision of the workers' compensation review board was affirmed.

State v. Outlaw


(AC 19968)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


70 Conn. App. 160; 797 A.2d 579; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 302


January 23, 2002, Argued  
June 4, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Licari, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, criminal possession of a firearm and carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Licari, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the jury on the first and third counts of the information, and to the court on the second count of the information; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with assault in the first degree, criminal possession of a firearm, and carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit, and he made a motion to suppress evidence. The Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), denied the motion and, after a jury trial on the first and third charges and a bench trial on the second charge, the court entered judgment convicting defendant of all charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the crimes for which he was convicted after he discharged a handgun 10 to 12 times during a fight in a bar and shot one of the people who was involved in the fight in the back as he was leaving the bar. Six days after the fight, police obtained an arrest warrant and arrested defendant at his apartment. When police entered the apartment, they saw a handgun inside an open closet, a box of bullets on a table, loose bullets, a shotgun, two rifles, marijuana, and a scale elsewhere in the apartment. The appellate court held that the evidence supported the trial court's judgment that these items were in plain view, and because the police entered defendant's apartment under authority of a valid arrest warrant, they were entitled to seize the items.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

702 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winer


(AC 20476)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


69 Conn. App. 738; 796 A.2d 491; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 242


November 29, 2001, Argued  
May 14, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Winer, 261 Conn. 909, 806 A.2d 50, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 308 (2002)
Appeal after remand at State v. Winer, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 94 (Conn. App. Ct., Mar. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, Byrne, J.) Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the fourth degree and with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and information, in the third case, charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, where the defendant was presented to the court, Byrne, J., on pleas of nolo contendere to three counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child; judgments of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to withdraw the pleas and to vacate the judgments, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant pled nolo contendere to risk of injury to a child, and the State agreed the maximum sentence of incarceration it would impose would be two years. Defendant was sentenced to eight years' incarceration, suspended after two years, and five years' probation. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), denied defendant's motion to vacate and to withdraw his plea. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his post-sentence motions to vacate the judgements and to withdraw his pleas of nolo contendere because they were involuntary, unknowing, and unconstitutional. Specifically, defendant argued that the sentence he received violated the plea agreement and was illegal. The court of appeals held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion to withdraw his pleas. The court of appeals noted that, based on the record, it was clear that defendant understood the terms of his pleas, and there was nothing to indicate that they were not voluntarily entered. The court of appeals concluded that it was clear that defendant contemplated a period of probation when he entered into his plea agreement. As for the legality of the sentence, the court of appeals held that defendant's sentence violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-29(e), since it did not satisfy the statute's minimum sentence requirement. The court of appeals noted, however, that the statutory minimum was within the parameters of the plea agreement.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The judgment was reversed only as to defendant's sentence. The case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Jacob


(AC 21375)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


69 Conn. App. 666; 798 A.2d 974; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 235


November 30, 2001, Argued  
May 14, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Richards, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, assault in the second degree and larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before W. Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect; thereafter, the court ordered the acquittee committed to the custody of the psychiatric security review board; subsequently, the court, Richards, J., denied the acquittee's application for unconditional discharge from the custody and jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board, and the acquittee appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant acquittee filed an action, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 71a-593, seeking his discharge from the custody and jurisdiction of the Connecticut Psychiatric Security Review Board (board). The board held a hearing and recommended that the acquittee not be discharged, and the acquittee sought judicial review. The Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) dismissed the acquittee's action and the acquittee appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1987, a defendant (acquittee) was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of robbery, assault, and larceny and the trial court committed the acquittee to the jurisdiction of the board for a period not to exceed 20 years. In September 1999, the acquittee filed an application seeking a discharge from the custody and jurisdiction of the board. The appellate court held that (1) although the acquittee did not raise his claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593 was unconstitutionally vague at trial, it would review that claim under the doctrine which the Supreme Court of Connecticut announced in its Golding decision; (2) § 17a-593 was not unconstitutionally vague; (3) although the trial court heard conflicting evidence on the issue of whether the acquittee was mentally ill, the court did not err by believing the State's expert witness instead of two experts who testified for the acquittee; and (4) the trial court properly considered the acquittee's past and present diagnoses in assessing whether the acquittee was dangerous and the record supported the trial court's findings that the acquittee was mentally ill and dangerous.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

704 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanchez


(AC 22340)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


69 Conn. App. 576; 795 A.2d 597; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 227



May 7, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford, Wollenberg, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Wollenberg, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), convicted defendant of murder and carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot his victim to death. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly allowed identification from a photo array. The appellate court found that the photo lineup was not unnecessarily suggestive, and the array was within constitutional bounds. Admission of a statement made by the victim was relevant since it identified defendant, even though it implied that defendant was a gang member, and its admission did not substantially prejudice defendant due to the overwhelming evidence of guilt. Although defendant was not allowed to cross-examine a witness about a nolle, his cross-examination satisfied the constitutional standard. A trial court did not err in restricting cross-examination about nolles where the accused otherwise was able to cross-examine to show bias, motive, or prejudice. The standard of review for admission of a photograph was limited to whether the trial court clearly abused its discretion. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing admission of autopsy photos because they appeared to be relevant at the time they were offered. Finally, there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

705 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Springmann


(AC 20316)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


69 Conn. App. 400; 794 A.2d 1071; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 216


December 11, 2001, Argued  
April 30, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, Klaczak) Amended information, in the first case, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, with nine counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and with aggravated sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree and threatening, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen,  [***2] where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Klaczak, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty of five counts of risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), of five counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Defendant asserted § 53-21 was unconstitutional, that the court improperly admitted pornographic videos, and his right to due process was violated when the trial court improperly failed to disclose exculpatory material after an in camera review.


OVERVIEW: The victim, who was staying with defendant as a foster child, alleged improper conduct by defendant to the police. The police subsequently seized among other items, 11 pornographic videotapes which had been shown to the minor victims. Defendant had also supplied alcohol to the victims. The appellate court held the statutory exception set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-86 was for the delivery of alcohol by a parent, guardian, or spouse of the minor. Defendant was not the equivalent of a guardian for purposes of § 30-86. Thus, his serving alcohol to minors did not fall within the exception created by § 30-86. The application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 to defendant's conduct was constitutional because the statute was not vague. Defendant placed the victims in a situation where their physical health was at risk and their morals could be impaired. The application of the § 53-21 to defendant did not implicate the constitutional right of a parent to raise a child. The pornographic videotapes were properly admitted. There was nothing exculpatory contained in the victim's records.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. McCown


(AC 21578)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


68 Conn. App. 815; 793 A.2d 281; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 172


November 26, 2001, Argued  
April 2, 2002, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. McCown, 260 Conn. 927, 798 A.2d 972, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 331 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied McCown v. Warden, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 631 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 1, 2007)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. McCown, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 466 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (TRIAL) (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Haven, Fracasse, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, attempt to commit murder and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Fracasse, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Council, 48 Conn. App. 919, 714 A.2d 733, 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 244 (1998)
State v. Rogers, 50 Conn. App. 467, 718 A.2d 985, 1998 Conn. App. LEXIS 388 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested after he admitted to the police that he had been in a car from which shots had been fired at a group of people, killing one person and wounding another. After a jury trial in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, Connecticut, defendant was convicted of murder as an accessory, conspiracy to commit murder, attempt to commit murder, and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was merely a passenger and did not know what the other two men in the vehicle had planned to do. Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court improperly precluded (1) defendant's mother from testifying during a suppression hearing, (2) defense counsel from arguing to the jury about the likely effects of defendant's age on his ability to realize the intent of others, and (3) defense counsel from cross-examining a State witness about the circumstances of her testimony in the other perpetrators' cases. The appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by (1) precluding the mother's testimony, as the mother had violated a sequestration order by being in the courtroom during another witness's testimony and could have unfairly shaped her own testimony; (2) limiting defense counsel's closing argument as to the effect of defendant's age, as no evidence was presented to the jury from which to infer that the 17-year-old defendant lacked the ability to recognize the intent of others; and (3) limiting the cross-examination of the State's witness, as the prohibited questions were irrelevant to the witness's credibility or defendant's case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Boyles v. Preston


(AC 20353)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


68 Conn. App. 596; 792 A.2d 878; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 140


September 28, 2001, Argued  
March 12, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Hon. Harry Hammer, judge trial referee, denied the defendant's motions to dismiss the complaint; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Bishop, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Boyles v. Preston, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3126 (Conn. Super. Ct. Nov. 17, 1999).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, female state court employee, sued defendant, male attorney employed by the state attorney's office located in the same building, alleging sexual harassment resulting in intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress. A Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) judgment, after denial of the attorney's motion to dismiss and a jury trial, awarded the female $ 105,201. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The female alleged the attorney engaged in a pattern of intentionally injurious, unwelcome and unwanted conduct toward her without her consent, including sexual advances, touching, rubbing, stalking, following her in the workplace, telephoning her at various hours of the day and night, and videotaping her without her knowledge or consent. The appeals court determined the attorney's motion to dismiss the prejudgment remedy sought was not filed timely, within 30 days after his general appearance in the lawsuit, and that, under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-45, 52-123, 52-278d(b) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 8-1(a) the female properly served the attorney with notice of the lawsuit. The female did not have to first file a claim with the state employment commission under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60 since there was no claim against the attorney's employer. The attorney's videotape was not a police or court record subject to erasure under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-142a(b). The evidence suppressed in the attorney's criminal trial was not necessarily not admissible in the civil trial. The attorney's failure to accept the female's offer in settlement caused additional damages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

The trial court should have held a competency hearing before the transfer was made.

Terese B. v. Comm'r of Children & Families


(AC 21570)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


68 Conn. App. 223; 789 A.2d 1114; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 89


October 31, 2001, Argued  
February 12, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant commissioner of children and families to remove a minor child from foster care at the plaintiff's home, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foster parent's foster child was removed from her care, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17A-100. She challenged the removal, and the removal was upheld. The foster parent appealed. Defendant commissioner of children and families filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) entered judgment, granting the motion. The foster parent appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner argued that the administrative proceeding was not a "contested case," within the meaning of the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166 et seq., because the foster parent did not have a statutory right to a hearing. The parent argued that as a foster parent, she had a liberty interest in family life matters. In deciding against the foster parent, the appellate court found the parent lacked standing, because she failed to establish either classical or statutory aggrievement. Therefore, the lower court did not have jurisdiction over the parent's claim. Foster parents were defined and restricted by statute. Foster families did not have the same rights as biological families or adoptive families. In the instant action, the foster parent failed to demonstrate a specific, personal, and legal interest. The statutory protection provided to foster parents, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-466(f), did not apply because the instant action was not a habeas corpus action. The administrative proceedings held in the instant action did not qualify as a "contested case" because the agency was not required to determine the foster parent's legal interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Turner


(AC 20332)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


67 Conn. App. 519; 787 A.2d 625; 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 4



January 1, 2002, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit, possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, criminal possession of a firearm, criminal possession of a pistol and altering or removing the identification mark of a pistol, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to a jury before Clark, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of carrying a pistol without a permit, possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, criminal possession of a firearm and criminal possession of a pistol, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, geographical area number six (Connecticut), that convicted him of various weapon possession offenses, claiming that the jury instructions were inflammatory and diluted the State's burden of proof.


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial for four counts of illegal possession of weapons, the trial court gave an example to the jury as part of its instructions. The appellate court held that the example did not inflame the passions of the jury or direct a verdict for the State. The trial court specifically stated that it was giving an example. It instructed the jury specifically that the factual circumstances in the evidence were left for it to pass upon. The example was not an unfair statement of the law of circumstantial evidence. It was neither a "direction" to the jury nor a "distinct intimation" that this issue was not longer for it to decide. The trial court repeatedly informed the jury that it was the sole fact finder. Defendant's unpreserved claim as to the trial court's consciousness of guilt instruction was not of constitutional magnitude.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Kachainy C. 1


(AC 21208)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


67 Conn. App. 401; 787 A.2d 592; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 637



December 25, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the parental rights of the respondents with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Rogers, J.; judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed to this court.

In re Kachainy C., 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1893 (Conn. Super. Ct. July 26, 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court adjudicated a child neglected and committed her to the protective custody of petitioner commissioner. The commissioner then sought termination of respondent mother's parental rights. The Child Protection Session at Middletown, Connecticut, granted the petition. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother claimed the trial court improperly concluded that when adjudicating a petition for termination of parental rights, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(c)(1) did not require the court to find by clear and convincing evidence that the department made reasonable efforts to reunify the child and parent where the court had previously made those findings. The commissioner argued the issue was moot. Although the appellate court concluded that the claim was not moot, the mother's claim lacked merit. The mother also argued the child protection judge's reliance on the trial judge's determinations regarding reunification was improper because the trial judge's decisions were not supported by clear and convincing evidence, and the child protection judge did not make a finding by clear and convincing evidence. The appellate court noted that statute did not require the child protection judge to make the finding herself because the trial judge did so. Finally, the mother claimed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-110 was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the mother could not prevail on the claim because it was not raised at trial and failed to satisfy all four prongs of Golding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

712 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Statewide Griev. Comm. v. Brown


(AC 20706)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


67 Conn. App. 183; 786 A.2d 1140; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 614



December 4, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Statewide Griev. Comm. v. Brown, 259 Conn. 919, 791 A.2d 568, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 68 (2002)
Motion denied by Statewide Griev. Comm. v. Brown, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3201 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 2, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Karazin, J.; judgment suspending the defendant from the practice of law for ninety days and ordering the defendant to submit to fee arbitration, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Statewide Griev. Comm. v. Brown, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2825 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 19, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) which suspended him from the practice of law and ordered him to participate in fee arbitration. The attorney claimed, inter alia, that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 2-37(a)(6), which authorized appellee statewide grievance committee to order mandatory arbitration, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A client of the attorney had filed a grievance against him as a result of an excessive and inappropriate fee. The committee voted to reprimand the attorney after he failed to respond to the reviewing committee's recommendation. The attorney was also ordered to participate in arbitration to determine a reasonable fee. The attorney failed to comply with the committee's orders. The committee then filed a presentment against the attorney. The trial court upheld the committee's orders and suspended the attorney for 90 days. The appellate court held the attorney had waived his opportunity to argue the constitutionality of the statute by initially failing to respond. Because the court's finding that the attorney had waived the right to contest the decision was supported by the record, it was not clearly erroneous. Furthermore, because the appellate court upheld the trial court's finding on waiver, it did not consider the attorney's constitutional claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

713 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hunnicutt v. Comm'r of Corr.


(AC 20250)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


67 Conn. App. 65; 787 A.2d 22; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 572


September 25, 2001, Argued  
November 20, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, L. Sullivan, J.; judgment granting the petition in part; thereafter, the court denied the respondent's motions for clarification and articulation and granted the respondent's petition for certification to appeal, and the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, seeking an order compelling respondent Connecticut Commissioner of Correction (Commissioner) to have the inmate examined by an orthopedic surgeon. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) granted the petition and subsequently denied the Commissioner's motions for clarification and articulation. The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: An inmate claimed that the institution where he was incarcerated failed to provide adequate medical care to alleviate pain resulting from an injury to his hand. The trial court found that the inmate had reported tenderness to his hand but had not established any objective symptoms normally associated with a hand injury, that the institution had regularly provided him with over-the-counter pain medication, and that it was conceivable that some neurological involvement might be the cause of his pain. The trial court made no finding that the institution had violated the inmate's rights under the Eighth Amendment and it refused to state whether the inmate had established deliberate indifference by the institution or to identify any facts which showed deliberate indifference. The appellate court held that, in the absence of a finding by the trial court that the institution acted with deliberate indifference to the inmate's medical condition, there could be no finding that his rights under the Eighth Amendment were violated, and the trial court erred by granting the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment denying the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

In re Brianna B.


(AC 20946)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


66 Conn. App. 695; 785 A.2d 1189; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 528


April 23, 2001, Argued  
November 6, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking custody of a minor child from the commissioner of children and families, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Juvenile Matters, where the court, Holden, J., denied the petition; thereafter, the court, Lopez, J., granted the motion for a protective order filed by the commissioner; thereafter, the court, Damiani, J., denied the petitioner's motion to open the courtroom to the public and the news media; subsequently, the court granted the commissioner's motion to find the petitioner in contempt and for attorney's fees, and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Waterbury (Connecticut), finding her in civil contempt of an order of confidentiality in a juvenile proceeding.


OVERVIEW: During a habeas corpus proceeding, in which the mother sought the return of her child that was removed from the home, the mother violated the confidentiality of the proceedings. After the mother failed to comply with two protective orders requiring her to remove photos of the child and case information from the internet, the Commissioner of Children and Families filed a motion for contempt. The motion was granted. The appellate court affirmed. The order of confidentiality of the juvenile proceedings did not violate the mother's right to free speech, as the protection of the juvenile's confidentiality was sufficiently compelling to justify the prior restraint, and the order imposed was narrowly tailored. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in closing the juvenile proceedings, as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-122 mandated that such proceedings be closed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

715 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Golden v. Johnson Mem. Hosp., Inc.


(AC 20196)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


66 Conn. App. 518; 785 A.2d 234; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 516


April 5, 2001, Argued  
October 30, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for medical malpractice, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Fineberg, J., granted the defendants' motions for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

Golden v. Johnson Mem. Hosp., 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2536 (Conn. Super. Ct. Sept. 17, 1999) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff patient's medical malpractice action, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) entered a judgment granting the motions for summary judgment filed by defendants, hospital and pathologists, on their defense that the patient's action was time-barred pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the patient claimed that the trial court's judgment was improper, because: (1) the repose section of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 was tolled by the continuing course of conduct doctrine; and (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 barred his claim before he could have known that he had suffered actionable harm, in violation of the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. The appellate court held that there was no initial duty for the hospital or the pathologists to provide follow-up treatment or to instruct the patient on follow-up care. Therefore, there was no subsequent wrongful misconduct and no genuine issue of material fact as to whether there was a continuing duty. Furthermore, although Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 resulted in disparate treatment for individuals, such as the patient, who did not discover their injury within the three-year limitations period, the classification bore a reasonable relationship to the legislature's goal of limiting the legal consequences of wrongs to a controllable degree. Accordingly, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 was constitutional as applied to the patient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Elf v. Dep't of Pub. Health


(AC 20874)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


66 Conn. App. 410; 784 A.2d 979; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 503


June 12, 2001, Argued  
October 23, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant revoking the plaintiff's license to operate a family day care home, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Radcliffe, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal; thereafter, the court, Moraghan, J., denied the plaintiff's motion for a rehearing or for reconsideration, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.

Elf v. State Dep't of Pub. Health, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 540 (Conn. Super. Ct. Feb. 29, 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff home day care provider appealed affirmance, by the Superior Court, Danbury Judicial District (Connecticut), of a decision of defendant public health department to revoke her license, arguing lack of substantial evidence, absence of legal basis, and various constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: A home day care provider's license was summarily suspended and then revoked by Connecticut's Department of Public Health after she was uncooperative with inspectors. Both a trial court and the appeals court, exercising limited review, upheld the administrative action. Although the parties' accounts of the altercation varied greatly, the administrative law judge's credibility determinations were entitled to deference, and there was no evidence indicating she was biased. Substantial evidence that the provider refused to permit an inspection was grounds enough in itself to warrant revocation. The provider's due process rights were also not violated. There was no impropriety in allowing an agency to conduct its own adjudications, and she was clearly provided with notice and an opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

717 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


(AC 20448)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


65 Conn. App. 687; 783 A.2d 526; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 466


April 4, 2001, Argued  
September 18, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Procedural History

Appeal from the decision by the named defendant upholding the cease and desist order issued by the town zoning enforcement officer concerning certain activities on the plaintiffs' property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hon. John T. Downey, judge trial referee; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) dismissing their appeal from the decision of defendant zoning board of appeals upholding the action of the town's zoning enforcement officer, who issued a cease and desist order to the landowners.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that when the town enacted zoning regulations, the landowners' use of their property as a quarry became a valid, preexisting, nonconforming use. The landowners continued to operate the quarry for several decades. The town later enacted a regulation permitting the use of the property as a quarry, subject to a special permit. The landowners were granted such a permit, and renewed it twice. At the last expiration of the permit, the landowners did not seek a further renewal but continued their operation of the land as a quarry. The town's zoning enforcement officer ordered the landowners to cease the operation of their quarry for their failure to renew the permit. The trial court held that even if the landowners' use continued to be a valid, preexisting, nonconforming use, the appeal still failed because nonconforming uses were subject to regulation in the interest of public health, safety, and welfare. The appellate court agreed. The landowners acquired, and continued to have, a valid, preexisting nonconforming use. The requirement that the landowners obtain a permit, however, was a reasonable regulation of its nonconforming use under the town's police powers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

718 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooper


(AC 19850)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


65 Conn. App. 551; 783 A.2d 100; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 454


May 1, 2001, Argued  
September 11, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Cooper, 258 Conn. 940, 786 A.2d 427, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 498 (2001)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Cooper, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1587 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 22, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Cooper v. Murphy, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 134186 (D. Conn., Dec. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Procedural History

Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree and with commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Maloney, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss certain evidence and his motions in limine to exclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal, and the defendant appealed to this court. Affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) entered a judgment which: (1) convicted defendant of first degree robbery under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), and of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k; and (2) sentenced him to a 20-year prison term, suspended after 15 years, and 5 years' probation on the robbery conviction, and to a consecutive 5-year term under § 53-202k. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from his use of a sawed-off, single-barreled shotgun to rob the victim of her car and her pocketbook, which contained two or three credit cards and cash. On appeal, defendant raised numerous assignments of error. The appellate court held, first, that the State was not precluded from prosecuting defendant for the robbery on double jeopardy grounds, because there was no constitutional prohibition against a state prosecution for the same acts which had resulted in a federal prosecution. Second, the evidence was sufficient to support the robbery conviction, because the jury reasonably could have concluded that the cumulative force of the evidence established beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was the robber. Third, defendant's motion to suppress the victim's credit cards was properly denied, because the search that yielded the credit cards was incident to his lawful arrest. Finally, the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on either of the two elements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k was harmless error, because the jury would have found that defendant was subject to a sentence enhancement under § 53-202k had it been properly instructed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Corcoran v. Taylor


(AC 20571)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


65 Conn. App. 340; 782 A.2d 728; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 434


April 5, 2001, Argued  
August 28, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. Donald W. Celotto, judge trial referee; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion to set aside the verdict and for an additur, and granted the defendant's motion for reduction of the verdict due to collateral source payments; subsequently, the court rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) granted defendant driver's motion for reduction of the verdict due to collateral source payments; subsequently, the a jury rendered judgement for plaintiff injured, from which the injured appealed.


OVERVIEW: The injured first claimed the trial court improperly reduced her economic damages on the basis of collateral source benefits. The court reduced the amount of verdict to zero because the amount paid by collateral sources greatly exceeded the jury award. The result was consistent with legislative intent to prevent double recoveries. Second, she claimed abuse of discretion in the trial court's refusal to submit certain interrogatories to the jury. She brought a one count cause of action, so it was within the trial court's discretion to deny her request. It was not an abuse of discretion. The third claim was that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-225a was unconstitutionally vague as it applied to her because it did not require a jury to make specific awards for past and future economic damages. However, the injured cited no Connecticut or federal law in support of her position and provided no legal analysis. The final claim was that the driver's counsel made prejudicial comments that caused the jury to view her claims unfairly. The injured's counsel did not object to the remarks at the time they were made or at the conclusion of the argument, so the claim was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: Judgement was affirmed.

 

720 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neil


(AC 19710)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


65 Conn. App. 145; 782 A.2d 209; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 421


March 26, 2001, Argued  
August 21, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. O'Neil, 258 Conn. 932, 785 A.2d 229, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 459 (2001)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. O'Neil, 261 Conn. 49, 801 A.2d 730, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 276 (2002)
Affirmed by State v. O'Neil, 262 Conn. 295, 811 A.2d 1288, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 3 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of attempt to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield Judicial District (Connecticut), convicting him on a jury verdict of attempted murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a), 53a-54a(a), arguing most prominently that the evidence was insufficient to sustain conviction of that offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in jail awaiting trial on a murder charge when a guard intercepted a letter that exhorted another person to murder the chief witness against him. The appeals court reversed his conviction of attempted murder on charges arising out of these facts. It noted that Connecticut's attempt statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(a), and its solicitation statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-179a(a), maintained the common law distinction between these two inchoate offenses. The legislative history of several revisions of the criminal statutes supported this interpretation. The facts alleged in the charging instrument made out a solicitation of murder, not an attempt, which required an overt endeavor toward the commission of the offense. Since the evidence was insufficient to find defendant guilty of attempted murder beyond a reasonable doubt, his conviction violated due process and was plain error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with direction to render a judgment of not guilty.

State v. Edelman


(AC 20145)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


64 Conn. App. 480; 780 A.2d 980; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 383


April 26, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
July 24, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 11, 2002.

PRIOR HISTORY: Amended information charging the defendant with violation of the state building code, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, and tried to the jury before Foley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-263 entered in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham, Geographical Area Number 11 (Connecticut), claiming that § 29-263 was vague, and that the court erred in denying his request to poll the jury and in refusing his jury charge.


OVERVIEW: While driving by defendant's house, a building official noticed that part of the defendant's roof was being replaced without a building permit. He issued a stop work order and prepared a warrant for the defendant's arrest. The trial court refused to give defendant's requested charge concerning the definition of "alteration." PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint alleging retaliatory discharge from employment in violation of the Workers' Compensation Act, brought to the workers' compensation commissioner for the sixth district, who determined that the defendant had terminated the plaintiff's employment in violation of § 31-290a, and the plaintiff and the defendant filed separate appeals to this court; subsequently, the appeals were withdrawn, and the parties entered into a settlement agreement that provided for, inter alia, attorney's fees to the plaintiff; thereafter, the commissioner reduced the award of attorney's fees; subsequently, the plaintiff's trial counsel appealed to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff's trial counsel appealed to this court.

Stat. § 31-327(a), (b) provided that the commissioner could award such fees and that all such fees were subject to the commissioner's approval. There was no distinction between fees awarded separately and fees combined with other compensation. The attorney's other claims were not preserved for appeal.

State v. Brocuglio


(AC 18520)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


64 Conn. App. 93; 779 A.2d 793; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 325


December 7, 2000, Argued  
July 3, 2001, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Brocuglio, 258 Conn. 908, 782 A.2d 1247, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 401 (2001)
Affirmed by State v. Brocuglio, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 268 (Conn., July 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault of a peace officer and three counts of the crime of interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, where the court, Owens, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of interfering with an officer, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Brocuglio, 1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1269 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 5, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) entered a judgment, upon a jury verdict, convicting defendant of two counts of interfering with an officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence derived from a warrantless entry onto his property. He argued that the search conducted by the police violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 7. The appellate court agreed with defendant in part. It found that the officers' warrantless entry into defendant's front yard and front driveway to ticket unregistered vehicles was constitutional, because defendant had a lesser expectation of privacy in the area in front of the house. However, the officers' warrantless entry into defendant's backyard and rear driveway was unconstitutional, because defendant manifested an objective intent that the area be preserved as private. That intent was evidenced by his placement of a six-foot fence in the middle of the rear driveway and the "no trespassing," "keep out," and "beware of dog" signs. The rear areas in question were curtilage of the house and, thus, the privacy expectation in those areas was the same as that inside the house. To enter those areas without a warrant was a violation of defendant's rights under both U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 7.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Vicente


(AC 19471)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


62 Conn. App. 625; 772 A.2d 643; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 173

April 10, 2001, Officially Released

Related proceeding at State v. Ibrahim, 62 Conn. App. 634, 772 A.2d 680, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 174 (2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Fasano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court of Waterbury (Connecticut) of manslaughter in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(1). Defendant appealed, raising claims of jury instruction error.


OVERVIEW: The charge arose from a gang-related shooting. Defendant argued on appeal that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on reasonable doubt and the presumption of innocence, and that even if the individual instructions were proper, the repeated description of what was not reasonable doubt diluted the State's burden of proof in violation of his due process rights under the Connecticut Constitution and the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The appellate court first noted that none of defendant's jury instruction issues were properly preserved at trial. Applying the Golding test for reviewing unpreserved claims of constitutional trial error, the appellate court held that although, the record was adequate for review and the issues were of constitutional magnitude, the claims failed because no constitutional violation clearly existed where the reasonable doubt jury instruction did not cause injustice, defendant's claims regarding the presumption of innocence instruction were inadequately briefed, and the jury instructions were correct in law, sufficient to guide the jury without misleading them, and resulted in no manifest injustice.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction.
