State v. Turner


(AC 18934)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


62 Conn. App. 376; 771 A.2d 206; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 113


October 26, 2000, Argued  
March 20, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit, having a weapon in a motor vehicle, altering or removing identification marks from a pistol and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Harper, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), convicting him for carrying a pistol without a permit, having a weapon in a motor vehicle, altering or removing identification marks from a pistol, and interfering with an officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court for carrying a pistol without a permit, having a weapon in a motor vehicle, altering or removing identification marks from a pistol, and interfering with an officer, following denial of his motion to suppress. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court improperly: excluded evidence at trial that corroborated his testimony and impeached state witness testimony, instructed the jury regarding the presumption in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-36, accepted the jury's finding that he altered the identification mark of the gun, and denied his motion to suppress unlawfully seized evidence. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court's evidentiary rulings and the improper jury instruction were harmful to defendant. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by ruling to exclude additional testimony by the officers regarding fingerprint testing, and that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Convictions were reversed and remanded because the trial court's evidentiary rulings and the improper jury instruction were harmful to defendant.

 

728 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Green


(AC 18369)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


62 Conn. App. 217; 774 A.2d 157; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 99


September 14, 2000, Argued  
March 6, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder as an accessory, conspiracy to commit murder and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, brought to the Superior Court  [***2] in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Fracasse, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION:  [***3] Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the jury verdict in the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut) in which defendant was convicted of murder as an accessory, conspiracy to commit murder, and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury trial, of conspiracy to commit murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48, 53a-54a(a), murder as an accessory in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8, 53a-54a(a) and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217c. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, argued improper jury instructions, and made a Batson challenge. The appellate court found the record simply did not contain evidence of separate acts and circumstances to support a prior agreement between the defendant and any of the alleged coconspirators. Accordingly, the defendant's conviction of conspiracy to commit murder was set aside. Further, the appellate court found that the defendant failed to demonstrate that the challenged language in the court's instruction unconstitutionally diluted the State's burden of proof. Additionally, the appellate court found that in most of the instances of defendant's five challenges, he failed to properly preserve error. As such, the judgment was reversed in part, and affirmed in part.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the conviction of the crime of conspiracy to commit murder and the case was remanded with the direction to render judgment of not guilty of that crime because there was insufficient evidence to support a conviction in a conspiracy charge. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Sanko


(AC 18787)

February 27, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle and with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle and interfering with an officer and, in the second part, with having committed an offense while released on a written promise to appear, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, and tried to the jury before Crawford, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle and of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the court on the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) which convicted him of two counts of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle, and with having committed an offense while released on a written promise to appear.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, inter alia, of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle. On appeal, defendant challenged both the validity of his manslaughter conviction and the propriety of the enhanced sentence ordered by the court. In addition, the appellate court concluded the trial court had constitutional authority to decide, without empanelling a jury, that defendant's prior conviction triggered an enhanced penalty under § 53a-40b.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment because the trial court had constitutional authority to decide, without empanelling a jury, that defendant's prior conviction triggered an enhanced penalty.

 

730 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bard v. Comm'r of Motor Vehicles


(AC 19788)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


62 Conn. App. 45; 768 A.2d 960; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 86


October 23, 2000, Argued  
February 27, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant suspending the plaintiff's license to operate a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district New Britain and tried to the court, Hartmere, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorist appealed Superior Court, New Britain Judicial District (Connecticut), affirmance of defendant commissioner of motor vehicles' one-year suspension of plaintiff's driver's license, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-111c, after his conviction of drunk driving in Maine.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was convicted of drunk driving in Maine. Pursuant to an interstate driver's license compact, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-111c, originals and photocopies of various records were transmitted to Connecticut, where defendant commissioner of motor vehicles suspended his license. The court reviewed defendant's proceeding, and the trial court's affirmance of it, only to assure that they were supported by substantial evidence, and found that they were. Although Maine's drunk driving statute criminalized driving at a lower blood alcohol level than did the Connecticut statute, review of the record, particularly the penalties imposed in Maine, supported an inference that plaintiff's blood alcohol level far exceeded the limit under either statute. Finally, Maine appeared to have satisfactorily met all its obligations under the compact in supplying information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's decision, because substantial evidence supported it. The evidence of foreign conviction was sufficient, defendant and the trial court properly inferred therefrom that plaintiff's conduct would have constituted drunk driving in Connecticut, and Maine properly satisfied all statutory formalities.

 

731 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weiner


(AC 18871)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


61 Conn. App. 738; 767 A.2d 1220; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 67


December 1, 2000, Argued  
February 13, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree and risk of injury to a child; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's petition for a new trial, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree, and risk of injury to a child. He appealed those convictions, challenging the denial of his motion for judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the verdict, motion to dismiss a charge, and petition for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The court found defendant's assignments of error unpersuasive. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the unlawful restraint charge. The jury's verdict on that charge was not inconsistent with the verdict acquitting defendant of the charge of sexual assault in the first degree. Those two offenses required different elements. Factual inconsistency was not a ground for overturning a verdict. The jury reasonably could have found that defendant did not force the victim to have intercourse but did force the victim to masturbate him. The trial court also did not err in denying defendant's motion for new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The lower court found, and the instant court agreed, that the new evidence presented was not likely to produce a different result. Cross-examination of the new witnesses would have undermined their credibility while the victim appeared credible. Finally, defendant did not demonstrate that the prosecutor's argument was so prejudicial that it deprived defendant of a fair hearing of his petition for a new trial. On that issue, defendant presented nothing but bare statements of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The unlawful restraint conviction was not inconsistent with the acquittal for first degree sexual assault. The lower court did not err in finding that defendant's newly discovered evidence would not have altered the outcome of the trial. Defendant did not demonstrate that overzealous prosecution denied him a fair hearing on his petition for new trial.

 

732 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


(AC 18619)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


61 Conn. App. 621; 767 A.2d 137; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 49


November 1, 2000, Argued  
February 6, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree, risk of injury to a child and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Stodolink, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain identification evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree, risk of injury to a child and the lesser included offense of unlawful restraint in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sexual assault and unlawful restraint convictions, in Superior Court, Fairfield Judicial District (Connecticut), arguing trial court error in failing to suppress eyewitness identification evidence, denying his motion for acquittal, and instructing the jury in a misleading manner regarding the element of force.


OVERVIEW: A teenage sexual assault victim (victim) and her friend saw defendant several times the evening he eventually assaulted her. Both girls described defendant to police, and then victim identified him later that evening in a show-up at the hospital. Despite an officer's suggestive remarks, so many circumstances supported the identification's reliability that defendant's suppression motion was properly denied. The court then looked at the evidence supporting defendant's convictions of first- and second-degree sexual assault, and found sufficient evidence supporting the jury's finding of all elements, including force, beyond reasonable doubt, so the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to acquit. Finally, defendant failed to preserve his objection to the trial court's jury instruction defining the element of force. Since the court found no constitutional violation in the trial court's straightforward instruction based on statutory language, review was waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, because under the circumstances the identification was reliable, the evidence was legally sufficient to sustain all convictions, and since defendant failed to show the jury instruction violated his constitutional rights, he waived review of unpreserved error.

 

733 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


(AC 18853)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


61 Conn. App. 417; 767 A.2d 107; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 33


September 18, 2000, Argued  
January 23, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault in the first degree with a deadly weapon, carrying a pistol without a permit and possession of a weapon in a vehicle, and, in the second part, with the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury on the first part of the substitute information before Licari, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the court on the second part of the substitute information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), by jury, convicted defendant of first degree assault, carrying a weapon in a vehicle, and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-59(a)(1), 29-38, and 29-35(a). Defendant got a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k 5 year term for committing a class B felony with a firearm, in addition to 25 years under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a(5). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A shooting victim said he did not know his assailant, gave conflicting incident accounts, then finally accused defendant. Defendant was convicted of first degree assault, carrying a weapon, and carrying a pistol without a permit, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-59(a)(1), 29-38, and 29-35(a) respectively. The trial court also found, as a matter of law, that defendant committed a class B felony with a firearm, warranting a mandatory, nonsuspendable five year prison term under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k. The court affirmed. Because the enhanced punishment exceeded the statutory maximum under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a(5), the trial court should have instructed the jury regarding the enhanced punishment provision under § 53-202k. Although the jury, not the trial court, should have made the § 53-202k factual determinations, the failure to instruct the jury of the § 53-202k elements was harmless. The jury, having concluded that defendant shot the victim, could reasonably have inferred that defendant possessed the gun in his vehicle. The trial court was within its discretion to restrict defense cross-examination as to whether the victim had a gun.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Because the enhanced term defendant received for committing a felony with a firearm exceeded the statutory maximum for assault, the trial court should have instructed the jury as to the enhancement provisions rather than making the requisite factual determinations itself. That failure, however, was harmless.

 

734 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Renz v. Allstate Ins. Co.


(AC 20367)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


61 Conn. App. 336; 763 A.2d 1072; 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 9


October 27, 2000, Argued  
January 9, 2001, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover uninsured motorist benefits allegedly due pursuant to two automobile insurance policies issued by the named defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court rendered judgment limiting the plaintiff's recovery to one of the two policies in question, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured appealed judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), which limited plaintiff's recovery of uninsured motorist benefits to one of the two automobile insurance policies issued by defendant insurance company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insured suffered injuries and losses as a result of an accident that occurred on Feb. 2, 1994 involving an uninsured vehicle. Plaintiff sought to recover from defendant insurance company the uninsured motorist benefits provided under an automobile insurance policy that had been issued to her on Aug. 21, 1993, and the uninsured motorist benefits provided under another insurance policy that had been issued to her parents on Sept. 23, 1993. The court held that plaintiff could recover under both policies because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-336(d), which prohibited the stacking of automobile insurance coverages, did not apply to insurance policies issued in the gap period between the enactment of the statute on July 1, 1993 and its effective date on Jan. 1, 1994. The reference in 1993 Conn. Acts 93-297, § 29, to "acts or omissions" did not unambiguously foreclose plaintiff from enforcing the terms of gap policies permitting stacking. Although § 38a-336(d) did not provide expressly for the continued enforceability of stacking provisions contained in gap insurance policies, the language was ambiguous and applying it retroactively would have overturned reasonable expectations.


OUTCOME: Judgment limiting plaintiff's recovery of uninsured motorist benefits to one of the two automobile insurance policies issued by defendant insurance company reversed and remanded because the statute prohibiting the stacking of automobile insurance coverages did not apply to policies issued in the gap period between the enactment and the effective date of the statute due to the ambiguous language of the statute.

 

735 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Meikle


(AC 20516)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


60 Conn. App. 802; 761 A.2d 247; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 563


September 25, 2000, Argued  
November 21, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 9, 2001.
Appeal denied by State v. Meikle, 255 Conn. 947, 769 A.2d 63, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 87 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Meikle v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1467 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 9, 2003)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Meikle, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1623 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 25, 2004)
Related proceeding at Meikle v. Kirschbaum, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3278 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for murder from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), claiming the State's peremptory challenge of an African-American juror was an Equal Protection Clause violation, redirect testimony of expert was improper, and trial court erred in allowing State to reopen its case-in-chief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sought review. The court affirmed. The prosecution's peremptory challenge of an African-American juror was not an Equal Protection Clause violation. The juror demonstrated difficulty in accepting the principle that it was the duty of jurors to apply the law as given by the court to the facts as found by them, showed a reluctance to judge others, and hesitated in affirming that she could have been fair and impartial to both sides. The trial court properly exercised its discretion in allowing the State to present redirect testimony as to the approximate firing distance. Appellant's counsel opened the door to such evidence by cross-examining the expert about gunpowder residue results as to the victim's shirt. The trial court did not error in allowing the State to reopen its case-in-chief. The State had presented a prima facie case; it was allowed to reopen for the limited purpose of establishing a chain of custody as to the victim's shirt, tested by an expert.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because peremptory challenge was not unconstitutional, appellant's counsel opened the door to redirect testimony, and reopening the State's case-in-chief was not error where it was for the limited purpose of establishing chain of custody.

Bunting v. Bunting


(AC 19378)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


60 Conn. App. 665; 760 A.2d 989; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 543


May 2, 2000, Argued  
November 14, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the orders and decrees of the Probate Court for the district of Wallingford, approving the defendant's final account and amended final account of the estate of the defendant's decedent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the appeals were consolidated; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Beach, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, in part, and remanding the case to the Probate Court for further proceedings, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiffs cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant estate executor appealed from the judgment of the Probate Court for the District of Wallingford (Connecticut), ordering a proration of the tax burden of an estate in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-401.


OVERVIEW: Following a probate proceeding, the trial court ordered a proration of the tax burden of decedent's estate in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-401. Defendant estate executor appealed, claiming the trial court improperly permitted the introduction of evidence of the decedent's intent as to the payment of federal estate and state succession taxes, and ordered a distribution of the estate after a proration of taxes. The court affirmed in part. Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-376, 12-401 provided for a statutory presumption that taxes were to be prorated among the beneficiaries, unless the testator directed otherwise. There was an ambiguity as to whether decedent intended to avoid proration of taxes on an gift made to defendant. The trial court did not abuse its discretion or commit clear error when it permitted the introduction of parol or extrinsic evidence to aid it in determining the decedent's intent as to the allocation of death taxes.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Decedent's will provision was a sufficient direction against proration, however, proration did not apply to a prior gift made to defendant that was thought not to be taxable.

Kroll v. Steere


(AC 19276)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


60 Conn. App. 376; 759 A.2d 541; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 475


May 8, 2000, Argued  
October 10, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Kroll v. Steere, 255 Conn. 909, 763 A.2d 1035, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 438 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from, inter alia, implementing a cease and desist order preventing the named plaintiff from continuing to display a sign on certain of her real property in violation of zoning regulations, and for other relief, brought to Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Mihalakos, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court denied the named plaintiff's motion to open the judgment, and the named plaintiff appealed to this court.
Kroll v. Steere, 1998 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3617 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 18, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner appealed summary judgment entered by the Superior Court, New London, Connecticut, in favor of defendant zoning enforcement officer, in an action to enjoin defendant from implementing a cease and desist order under Groton Long Point Ass'n, Inc., Conn., Zoning Reg. § 3.20 to prevent plaintiff from displaying a painting protesting a deer hunting ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff homeowner set a 20 square foot painting protesting adoption of a deer hunting ordinance against her garage door. Plaintiff filed suit against defendant zoning enforcement officer, when he ordered her to remove the painting as a violation of Groton Long Point Ass'n, Inc., Conn., Zoning Reg. § 3.20. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendant and plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that plaintiff's painting was not a mural, but a message bearing sign subject to zoning regulations. Section 3.20 did not infringe on plaintiff's right of free speech under U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV, because it did not regulate the content, but only the size as deemed necessary for traffic safety. The trial court should not have granted summary judgment on the ground that plaintiff's allegations of selective enforcement were insufficient as a matter of law. The specific identification of other alleged violations of the sign ordinance should have been a matter of proof at trial. The summary judgment was reversed as to plaintiff's claim of selective enforcement, but affirmed in other respects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment as to plaintiff's claims of selective enforcement and remanded to allow identification of other allegedly unprosecuted violations of the sign ordinance, but affirmed the judgment in other respects.

State v. Gurreh


(AC 19846)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


60 Conn. App. 166; 758 A.2d 877; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 464


June 2, 2000 Argued  
October 3, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a hallucinogen and sale of a controlled substance and amended information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to possess a controlled substance and attempt to possess a controlled substance with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Santos, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss the informations; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Gallagher, J., on conditional pleas of nolo contendere to the charges of sale of a controlled substance and attempt to possess a controlled substance with intent to sell, and the state nolled the remaining charges; subsequently, the court rendered judgments of guilty in accordance with the pleas, from which the defendant filed a consolidated appeal to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who pleaded no contest to possession and sale of controlled substance charges, sought review of the Superior Court, judicial district of Hartford's (Connecticut) decision denying his motion to dismiss the charges, claiming khat was not a controlled substance pursuant to Connecticut statutes.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded no contest to sale and possession with intent to sell a controlled substance and sought review of his denied motion to dismiss. The court affirmed. Appellant possessed khat, a plant material that contained the prohibited controlled substances of cathinone and cathine. The legislature had, by its language, indicated an intent to include these materials in the definition of controlled substances. Cathinone was listed as a material considered a controlled substance in Conn. Agencies Regs. § 21a-243-7(e). Khat contained, however small, a quantity of cathinone that caused a stimulant effect. The review of a dictionary definition of khat revealed it was a habituating stimulant. Appellant, a native of Somalia, was already aware of the stimulant characteristic of the substance because of its widespread use in that country. Appellant's use of an assumed name to accept the very large packages of khat indicated consciousness of guilt.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed because khat was a controlled substance as shown in the state regulations and statutes and sufficient facts showed appellant understood its controlled nature.

Dietzel v. Planning Comm'n


(AC 19063)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


60 Conn. App. 153; 758 A.2d 906; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 468


April 25, 2000, Argued  
October 3, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying, in part, and granting, in part, with certain modifications and conditions, the plaintiffs' application for subdivision approval, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Radcliffe, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment, and rendered judgment in accordance with the parties' stipulation; thereafter, the court granted the motion to intervene filed by William A. Oppenheimer et al. and denied the intervenors' motion to open the judgment, from which the intervenors, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenors appealed the decision of the Danbury Superior Court (Connecticut), denying their motion to open the judgment approving plaintiffs' application for a subdivision.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, two individuals, filed an application with defendant planning commission for approval of a subdivision. Intervenors, two individuals, appealed from the denial of their motion seeking review of the decision approving a settlement agreement between the plaintiffs and defendant. On appeal, the court reversed. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 8-8(n), 22a-19, the intervenors had standing to raise environmental concerns regarding the settlement agreement. Section 22a-19(a) permitted any person, on the filing of a verified pleading, to intervene in any administrative proceeding for the limited purpose of raising environmental issues. Section 8-8 required a public hearing before establishing zoning regulations. The trial court's failure to comply with §§ 8-8(n), 22a-19 constituted plain error. Therefore, denial of intervenor's motion seeking review of the judgment was an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Order denying intervenor's motion to open was reversed. The trial court was directed to afford intervenors the opportunity to participate in the proceedings.

Ford v. Comm'r of Corr.


(AC 18737)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


59 Conn. App. 823; 758 A.2d 853; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 440


June 2, 2000, Submitted on Briefs  
September 12, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Downey, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) that denied his habeas corpus petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of and sentenced for robbery in the first degree, robbery in the second degree and tampering with a witness. Petitioner subsequently pled guilty in a second criminal case to burglary in the third degree and was sentenced to a term of three years imprisonment on the burglary conviction, to run concurrently with the sentence imposed for the robbery conviction. After he had finished serving his three year sentence for the burglary conviction, petitioner filed petition for a writ of habeas corpus based on the burglary conviction. The court affirmed judgment denying the petition. Petitioner was still in custody for the longer concurrent robbery sentence, but was not in custody for the burglary conviction. Since petitioner suffered no present restraint from the conviction being challenged, a habeas petition could not lie. Since the "in custody" requirement was not met, subject matter jurisdiction was implicated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Petitioner was still in custody for the longer concurrent robbery sentence. Petitioner's burglary sentence had expired prior to filing of his petition for habeas corpus on that burglary sentence. Petitioner was not in custody on the burglary sentence. Where a petitioner suffered no present restraint from the conviction being challenged, a habeas petition could not lie. The court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.

 

741 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wendt v. Wendt


(AC 18388)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


59 Conn. App. 656; 757 A.2d 1225; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 431


April 4, 2000, Argued  
September 5, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Tierney, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ex-wife appealed from an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which dissolved the marriage and divided the marital property pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-81.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant husband for divorce after a 32-year marriage in which plaintiff served as a mother, homemaker, and corporate wife while defendant climbed the corporate ladder and became chairman and chief executive officer of one of the largest corporations in the world. After an 18-day trial, the superior issued a 500-plus page decision dividing the marital assets. Plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed, holding that: the trial court properly valued and divided the assets as of the date of the parties' dissolution, not their separation; the trial court's application of the date of separation as a coverture factor was within its discretion; the trial court's valuation and division of defendant's deferred compensation plans and supplementary retirement plans was proper; and that Connecticut's Equal Rights Amendment, Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, did not require the trial court to divide the marital property 50-50 under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-81.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the trial court did not abuse its discretion in valuing and dividing the marital assets as of the date of the parties' dissolution. Connecticut's Equal Rights Amendment did not require the trial court to divide the marital property equally.

 

742 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Madagoski


(AC 18789)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


59 Conn. App. 394; 757 A.2d 47; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 399


April 28, 2000, Argued  
August 15, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of attempted assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree, assault on a peace officer and larceny in the second degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, for having previously been convicted of burglary in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury on the first part of the information before Stodolink, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was tried to the court on the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of several felonies, in Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), arguing insufficiency of evidence of attempted assault, improper jury charge on reasonable doubt, improper denial of bill of particulars, and restriction of cross-examination in violation of his constitutional right of confrontation.


OVERVIEW: When a police officer tried to apprehend defendant on auto larceny charges, defendant nearly caused him to be crushed between cars. The account of this event was sufficient evidence to support jury's guilty finding on the charge of attempted assault, and criminal intent was properly inferred from circumstantial evidence. A reasonable doubt instruction that might been objectionable in isolation did not prejudice defendant where the charge as a whole emphasized the burden to prove guilt beyond reasonable doubt. There was no abuse of discretion in denying defendant's motion for bill of particulars because the long form of information used provided full information about charges. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's attempt to cross-examine the police officer about internal affairs investigation of his conduct during the alleged assault, because it had reviewed the witness's personnel records in camera and found them irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed convictions, because there was ample evidence to support attempt assault finding, reasonable doubt instruction was proper in the context of the whole charge, the long form information provided defendant sufficient notice of charges, and proper restriction of cross-examination to relevant topics was not unconstitutional.

 

743 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kish v. Cohn


(AC 18382)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


59 Conn. App. 236; 756 A.2d 313; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 373


December 7, 1999, Argued  
August 8, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from lowering or removing a dam that fronts on certain of their real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Lewis, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss and rendered judgment dismissing the action, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed dismissal, by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), of their action to enjoin defendant dam owners from lowering or removing their dam. Plaintiffs argued that exhaustion of remedies was not required because of futility and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-403 denied them due process.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs owned land abutting a pond created by defendants' dam. The Connecticut commissioner of environmental protection (commissioner), responsible by statute for dam safety, ordered defendants to repair, lower, or demolish the dam. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin lowering or demolition. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-403(a) provided a method for persons threatened by a construction or demolition action within the commissioner's area of responsibility to obtain review of planned actions. The court held that despite plaintiffs' arguments that agency review would be futile because the commissioner ordered the action, they still had to exhaust their administrative remedies. Repair of the dam was one of the options in the order, and there was no certainty that an administrative appeal would not have worked. Plaintiffs argued that the statutory procedures unconstitutionally burdened their appeal rights, but the court, having other grounds for decision, declined to decide a constitutional question first raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal, because plaintiffs failed to exhaust administrative remedies and failed to show futility of administrative proceedings. The court declined to address constitutionality arguments since exhaustion of remedies was sufficient grounds for its decision.

 

744 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hill


(AC 19996)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 797; 755 A.2d 919; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 338


May 4, 2000, Argued  
July 18, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; verdict of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty to the charge of failure to appear in the first degree; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his first-degree kidnapping conviction in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), claiming Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him and insufficient evidence supported his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for first-degree kidnapping. The court affirmed, finding Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A) constitutional as applied to appellant and sufficient evidence supported the conviction. Appellant claimed the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts supporting the conviction. However, the record showed that appellant, without victim's consent, moved victim from the street to a place under a stairwell in an empty parking area, confined her there when she attempted to leave, and raped her. It did not matter that appellant's underlying motive in either moving victim from the street to the stairwell, or in confining her there, was to accomplish a rape. Such intent did not preclude a conviction for kidnapping. Sufficient evidence supported the conviction where victim was later observed to have red marks on her arms and throat.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because kidnapping statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant where evidence showed appellant confined victim under a stairwell against her will.

 

745 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Salmon v. Dep't of Pub. Health & Addiction Servs.


(AC 18253)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 642; 754 A.2d 828; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 312


December 10, 1999, Argued  
July 11, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant finding that the plaintiff had verbally abused a patient under her care and ordering the finding to be filed with the Connecticut Nurse Aide Registry, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, DiPentima, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal in part and remanding the case to the defendant for further proceedings, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties cross-appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) that affirmed in part a decision by defendant state department of public health, which held that the plaintiff had verbally abused a patient under her care and ordered that the finding to be filed with the state nurse aide registry.


OVERVIEW: After finding that plaintiff registered nurse's aide had made verbally abusive remarks to a nursing home patient, defendant state department of public health ordered its finding to be filed with the state nurse aide registry. The appeals court affirmed the trial court judgment affirming in part defendant's determinations. Defendant had jurisdiction to hear the Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 19a-9, 19a-14 charges, and the charging instrument's reference to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1395i-3(g)(1)(C) did not destroy that jurisdiction. The statutory term "resident abuse" was not unconstitutionally vague; defendant could define that term according to terms familiar to those in the industry and on a case by case basis. "Resident abuse" included verbal abuse. Plaintiff was not subject to arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. It was for the defendant, not the court, to weigh the credibility of the witness's testimony. The trial court did not err in concluding that "adverse impact" or "harm" was prerequisite to an abuse finding and that remand was necessary. In the instant case, a subjective, rather than objective, test was more appropriate for making that determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Defendant had jurisdiction to hear the charges against plaintiff. "Resident abuse" included verbal abuse. Remand was appropriate to determine, by use of a subjective test, whether the patient suffered the required "adverse impact" or "harm."

State v. Rocco

He argued Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70 (a) (1) was unconstitutionally vague and evidence of abduction was insufficient to support kidnapping conviction.

In re Amanda A.


(AC 19810)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 451; 755 A.2d 243; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 292


March 27, 2000, Argued  
June 27, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their three minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the matter was tried to the court, Quinn, J.; judgments terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed a decision of the Child Protection Session at Middletown (Connecticut), which terminated her parental rights with respect to her three minor children.


OVERVIEW: Respondent mother appealed the termination of her parental rights with respect to her three minor children. The court affirmed the decision. The court found that it was established by clear and convincing evidence that petitioner commissioner complied with the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(c)(1) by making reasonable efforts to reunite respondent with her children. The court determined that "reasonable efforts," as required in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(c)(1), meant doing everything reasonable, not everything possible, in attempting to reunify respondent and her children. The court determined that the record failed to establish that respondent was under a mental disability for purposes of equal protection of the law pursuant to Conn. Const. art. I, § 20. The court concluded that the failure of counsel to request the appointment of a guardian ad litem to protect the interests of respondent did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel, because the record failed to disclose evidence sufficient to raise a reasonable doubt as to respondent's ability to understand the proceedings or to assist her counsel on her behalf.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that terminated the parental rights of respondent mother. The court found that petitioner commissioner made a reasonable effort to reunite respondent with her children, but respondent was hostile and uncommunicative with petitioner, which rendered the efforts futile. The court found no evidence that there was an equal protection violation, because respondent failed to establish any mental disability.

 

748 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lacks


(AC 18589)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 412; 755 A.2d 254; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 281


October 22, 1999, Argued  
June 27, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lacks, 254 Conn. 919, 759 A.2d 1026, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 325 (2000)
Related proceeding at State v. Payne, 63 Conn. App. 583, 777 A.2d 731, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 270 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lacks v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1867 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Challenging denial of his motion to dismiss for lack of a speedy trial, alleged prosecutorial misconduct, and alleged errors in the jury instructions, defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), of felony murder and robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of felony murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, and robbery in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134. The appellate court affirmed. Although there had been nearly a two year delay in bringing defendant to trial, and voir dire was not concluded until nearly two months after it began, defendant's statutory and constitutional right to a speedy trial was not violated. Voir dire commenced within 30 days of when defendant filed his speedy trial motion, defendant's motion to dismiss was untimely because it was filed after voir dire began, and the delay in concluding voir dire did not weigh heavily against the State--that delay was caused by the State's decision to try defendant's accomplice first. Defendant waived his objections to alleged prosecutorial misconduct and to alleged errors in the jury instructions by failing to raise those issues before the trial court.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed. Because voir dire began within 30 days of defendant's motion for speedy trial, defendant's speedy trial rights were not violated. The Golding factors for reviewing an unpreserved claim of constitutional error were not present and the circumstances did not warrant the court's use of its supervisory authority to order a new trial for alleged prosecutorial misconduct.

In re Shane P.


(AC 19430)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 244; 754 A.2d 169; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 257


January 18, 2000, Argued  
June 13, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, Juvenile Matters, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the respondent mother filed a motion to transfer guardianship to the maternal grandparents; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights and denying the motion to transfer guardianship, from which the respondent father appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), terminating his parental rights in a suit to determine whether the evidence was sufficient to support the determination that he abandoned his minor child, and whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112 (Rev. to 1997) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner commissioner of children and families filed a petition to terminate respondent mother's and respondent father's parental rights with respect to their minor child. Respondent mother moved to transfer guardianship of the child to the maternal grandparents. The trial court denied respondent mother's motion and terminated respondents' parental rights. Respondent father appealed the termination of his parental rights. The court held that, based on the criteria for abandonment in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(c)(3)(A) (Rev. to 1997), the evidence was sufficient to support the determination that respondent father abandoned the child. Moreover, § 17a-112(c)(3)(A) was not void for vagueness as applied to respondent father, because § 17a-112(c)(3)(A) provided fair warning of the conduct necessary to avoid a finding of abandonment. Lastly, the termination of respondent father's parental rights did not signify an additional punishment (i.e., in addition to his incarceration) constituting double jeopardy, because § 17a-112(c)(3)(A) served a remedial purpose. Consequently, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment terminating respondent father's parental rights was affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to support the determination that respondent father abandoned his minor child; and the statutory grounds for abandonment were not void for vagueness as applied to respondent father, because they provided fair warning of the conduct necessary to avoid a finding of abandonment.

State v. Williams


(AC 18343)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


58 Conn. App. 125; 752 A.2d 1120; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 245


April 3, 2000, Argued  
June 6, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, burglary in the first degree and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Devlin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions, in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), of robbery and related offenses, arguing that identification evidence was insufficient, he was denied effective assistance of counsel, sentence was harsh and excessive, trial court should have noted his incompetence, and reasonable doubt instruction was improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his robbery and burglary conviction on many grounds, most prominently sufficiency of identification evidence to support verdict. 751 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Retirement Bd.


(AC 18844)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


57 Conn. App. 751; 750 A.2d 1139; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 212


February 23, 2000, Argued  
May 23, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant excluding the plaintiffs from participating in the defendant's retirement benefits pension plan, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Pellegrino, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff Marie Colacrai et al. appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from the decision of the defendant city retirement board, which excluded them from participation in the defendant's retirement benefits pension plan, after imposing a six-year statute of limitations for application for reinstatement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff teachers severed city employment prior to and were rehired after March 1, 1970. A collective bargaining agreement, excluding new hires after that date from plan participation, did not apply to plaintiffs. City code provided that any former participant who ceased to be a participant by reason of severance of service could, upon again becoming an employee, apply to the retirement board for reinstatement as follows: "Said board may reinstate such person only upon his payment into the retirement fund of any amounts previously withdrawn therefrom and upon demonstrating to the satisfaction of the retirement board that he is in reasonably good physical condition as indicated by the results of such medical examination as said board may prescribe." The court reversed, the trial court and defendant board's finding that since the plaintiff's were rehired after March 1, 1970, they were excluded as newly employed. Plaintiffs were entitled to participation if they repaid amounts previously withdrawn and were in reasonably good physical condition. "May" meant "shall" where conditions specifically stated. Defendant could not impose a six-year limitations statute for applications.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; because the applicable city code section required that plaintiffs, as former participants, could apply for reinstatement and had to be reinstated if they repaid to the plan amounts previously withdrawn and by demonstrated to the defendant that they were in reasonably good physical condition; and the section did not permit the defendant to impose a six-year statute of limitations for claims for reinstatement.

State v. Davidson


(AC 18085)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


57 Conn. App. 541; 750 A.2d 1106; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 189


November 1, 1999, Argued  
May 2, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, where the court, Zarella, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the information; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, judicial district of Tolland, Connecticut, convicting him, after a conditional plea of nolo contendere, of operating a motor vehicle while his driver's license was under suspension in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while his driver's license was under suspension pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(c). Defendant claimed that his special operator's permit, allowing him to drive for employment purposes, precluded a prosecution, and prosecuting him violated his constitutional right to procedural due process. The statute conveyed a clear intention to provide the state with the legal authority to prosecute any person operating a motor vehicle outside the scope of the work permit while his license was under suspension. Defendant was given fair warning that driving outside the parameters of the work permit could expose him to the penalties for operating while his operator's permit was under suspension. There was no reason why defendant should have been entitled to a hearing on the question of whether his already suspended license should be suspended or why the lack of a hearing should affect his conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; state had legal authority to prosecute persons operating motor vehicles outside scope of work while his license was under suspension, defendant was given fair warning that driving outside parameters of the work permit could expose him to statutory penalties.

State v. Mills


(AC 17986)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


57 Conn. App. 202; 748 A.2d 318; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 132


October 21, 1999, Argued  
April 4, 2000, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Mills, 253 Conn. 914, 754 A.2d 163, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 192 (2000)
Appeal denied by State v. Mills, 253 Conn. 915, 754 A.2d 163, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 193 (2000)
Appeal after remand at State v. Mills, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 547 (Conn. App. Ct., Dec. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder and with two counts each of the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Gill, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) finding him guilty of first degree manslaughter and first degree assault, alleging prosecutorial misconduct in closing arguments and the improper introduction of evidence seized pursuant to an allegedly unlawful warrantless arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree manslaughter and first degree assault for the stabbing death of victim. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress his statement and the evidence seized during defendant's warrantless arrest; defendant's motions for mistrial and a new trial, based on prosecutorial misconduct, were denied. In closing arguments, prosecutor made numerous pleas to the jurors to identify with victim, stated that society would be in trouble if defendant was acquitted, and asked the jury not victimize the victim again by acquitting him. On appeal the court remanded, ruling that because prosecutor repeatedly expressed personal opinions, appealed to the jurors' passions and emotions, and injected extraneous matters into the case during closing argument, defendant's motion for new trial was improperly denied. However, because the evidence established that exigent circumstances existed, the warrantless arrest and subsequent search of defendant was reasonable, and thus the motion to suppress was properly denied.


OUTCOME: Reversed and affirmed in part, and remanded. Prosecutor, in closing argument, improperly expressed his personal opinions, appealed to jurors' passions and emotions, and injected extraneous matters into case, so motion for new trial was improperly denied. Because exigent circumstances rendered warrantless arrest and subsequent search of defendant reasonable, motion to suppress was properly denied.

State v. Thorp


(AC 18539)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


57 Conn. App. 112; 747 A.2d 537; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 127


December 1, 1999, Argued  
March 28, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and attempted sexual assault in the first degree and with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, burglary in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the defendant was presented to the court, Devlin, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to one count of sexual assault in the first degree; judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea; thereafter, the court, Damiani, J., granted the motion filed by the office of adult probation to modify the conditions of the defendant's probation, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed order of Superior Court in judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), granting motion of State's office of adult probation modifying terms of probation to include sex offender treatment, on grounds that modification violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-30(c) and unconstitutionally increased restrictions without permitting withdrawal of guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: When defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree sexual assault, the agreement was for imprisonment followed by a term of probation. At sentencing, the court imposed several conditions on probation. Shortly before defendant's scheduled release, on motion of State's office of adult probation, the court added a condition that defendant undergo sex offender evaluation and treatment. The court held that Connecticut's probation statute provided broad discretion to a sentencing court in imposing conditions. The statute specifically authorized imposition of sex offender treatment conditions on persons convicted of defendant's offense. A statutory argument that court could only change conditions during period of release was inapplicable because office of adult probation had authority to modify without seeking court approval. Because defendant had bargained for a sentence including probation that was inherently modifiable, he did not allege a constitutional violation that could be reviewed despite his failure to raise the issue in trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed modification, because State had statutory authority to modify probation even without court approval; defendant did not allege violation of constitutional right when his guilty plea was given in exchange for a sentence that included probation, and terms of probation were always subject to change.

In re Michael L.


AC 19431


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 688; 745 A.2d 847; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 73


October 29, 1999, Argued  
February 22, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their three minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Juvenile Matters, and transferred to the Child Protection Session at Middletown, where the matter was tried to the court, Foley, J.; judgments terminating the respondent mother's parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought relief from a judgment of the Superior Court, Waterbury district, Connecticut, which terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was involved in drug activity and overall neglect of her children. Respondent sought relief from an order that terminated her parental rights. The court affirmed the order, finding it was not clearly erroneous. The court held that respondent's continued drug use demonstrated respondent's failure to rehabilitate within a reasonable time. The court held that respondent was not deprived of a fair trial in light of evidence that respondent received numerous court expectations and treatment plans. In addition, the court found that respondent failed to offer evidence to prove ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the termination of respondent's parental rights because respondent could not be rehabilitated with a reasonable time due to her continued drug use. The court also held that respondent received a fair hearing.

 

757 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nanowski


(AC 17647)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 649; 746 A.2d 177; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 59


December 6, 1999, Argued  
February 15, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with seven counts of the crime of failure to pay wages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Harleston, J., dismissed count five of the information; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut), convicting him for failure to pay wages in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-71c (a), (b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in trial court for failure to pay wages, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-71c (a), (b). Defendant appealed, claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-71a was unconstitutional, the trial court erred in striking his mistake of law defense and failing to instruct the jury on intent, and that there was insufficient evidence to convict him. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err, because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-71a had been upheld as constitutional, mistake of law was not a proper defense to failure to pay wages and intent was not a requirement for conviction, and there was sufficient evidence for a reasonable jury to convict defendant of failure to pay wages.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because the statute covering criminal penalty for failure to pay wages had been upheld as constitutional, mistake of law was not a proper defense to failure to pay wages and intent was not a requirement for conviction, and there was sufficient evidence for a reasonable jury to convict defendant.

 

758 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gordon


(AC 18143)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 512; 744 A.2d 453; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 37


November 2, 1999, Argued  
February 1, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Devlin, J.; denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain identification evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Because his motion to suppress certain identification evidence was denied, defendant appealed his conviction from Conn. Super. Ct., judicial district of Hartford, of manslaughter in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55 (a) (1), and assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59 (a) (5).


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress photographic identification evidence where the witness had been unable to specifically identify defendant but had identified similar looking males from the photo array. Defendant was convicted of manslaughter. On appeal, the court held that the record did not show that the photographic array was unduly suggestive or that the officers who presented influenced the choices. The defendant failed to meet his burden of establishing that the identification resulted from the employment of an unconstitutional procedure by the police. The court found that the trial court properly denied the suppression motion, and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, because the photographic array of possible perpetrators was not unduly suggestive and the officers presenting it did not so influence the identifying witness that identification resulted from unconstitutional police procedure; therefore, denial of the suppression motion was proper.

 

759 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Branham


(AC 18065)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 395; 743 A.2d 635; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 18


November 2, 1999, Argued  
January 18, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of assault in the third degree and with four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Lager, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), convicting him for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and of assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who left three small children in an apartment alone, was convicted for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, and for assault. Defendant appealed, arguing that there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction, and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied to his case. The court found that the amount of time the children were left unattended was not a necessary element of the offense, and even if it were a necessary element, the jury reasonably could have inferred that the children were seriously at risk of injury to their health, or that their lives or limbs were endangered when they were left unattended. The court also concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was constitutional as applied to defendant's conduct because it provided sufficient notice to him that his conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed because the jury could have reasonably found that the children were at risk when defendant left them alone, and the law provided defendant with sufficient notice that his conduct was prohibited.

 

760 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


(AC 18439)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 264; 742 A.2d 812; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 3


November 1, 1999, Argued  
January 4, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of stalking in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, and tried to the jury before Schuman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of stalking in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of conviction for crime of stalking in third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181e, which was entered upon jury verdict in Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, Connecticut.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was patient of victim. Victim was an anesthesiologist who provided pain management treatment to defendant. Victim began to receive strange phone calls. Defendant admitted to victim's office coordinator that she made the phone calls. Victim terminated his physician-patient relationship with defendant. Telephone calls were made repeatedly to victim's office and home. Victim received notes and letters from defendant. Defendant followed victim and stared at him on several occasions. On appeal, defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-181d and 53a-181e violated her due process rights under both federal and state constitutions because the words "repeatedly" and "followed" were indefinite and imprecise. The court found evidence from which jury could have concluded defendant followed victim on three occasions. Also, the court found it clear that defendant acted more than once or repeatedly. The court found no merit in defendant's remaining arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, finding stalking statute was not vague or overbroad, sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction, the Chip Smith instruction to jury did not violate defendant's due process rights, jury instruction regarding repeatedly follow was proper, and prosecutor did not commit prejudicial error during closing arguments.

 

761 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kellman


(AC 19110)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


56 Conn. App. 279; 742 A.2d 423; 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 4


October 25, 1999, Argued  
January 4, 2000, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, carrying a pistol without a permit, stalking in the first degree and criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Licari, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of murder, carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal violation of a protective order, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction, which was entered after a jury trial, in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35, and criminal violation of a protective order in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-110b (a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim had a history of romantic involvement that included domestic incidents. Defendant's violence toward the victim escalated. The victim obtained a protective order. One evening, the victim and her sister returned to victim's home from a night out. Defendant was waiting in the victim's driveway. He pulled out his gun, chased the victim, and shot her five times at close range. The victim died. On appeal, defendant asserted that an improper jury instruction on intoxication invalidated the instruction on extreme emotional disturbance. The court refused review of the claim because it was unpreserved and the improper jury instructions on the defense of extreme emotional disturbance was not of constitutional dimension. Next, defendant argued that defense counsel should have been permitted surrebuttal argument on the issue of extreme emotional disturbance. The court concluded that defendant failed to show surrebuttal argument was needed to protect the constitutional right of due process. The court rejected defendant's challenge to a jury instruction on reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The court determined that jury instruction on defense of extreme emotional disturbance was not of constitutional dimension, that defense counsel was not entitled to surrebuttal argument on the issue of extreme emotional disturbance, and that defendant's objection to a jury instruction on reasonable doubt was without merit.

Lawson v. Stamford Bd. of Educ.


FSTCV156024387S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2016 Conn. Super. LEXIS 744



April 6, 2016, Decided
